\title[Graded Endomorphisms of $H^*(\mathbb{S}^m \times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$]{Rational Cohomology Endomorphisms of product of Sphere with Grassmannian and coincidence theory}

\author[M. Mandal]{Manas Mandal}
\address{Indian Institute of Technology Kanpur, Kanpur 208016, India}
	\email{manasm.imsc@gmail.com}
	
	\author[D. Setia]{Divya Setia}
	\address{Institute of Mathematics, Polish Academy of Sciences, Krak{\'o}w 31-027, Poland}
	\email{divyasetia01@gmail.com}
	
	\subjclass[2020]{Primary: 55S37, 08A35,  55M20; Secondary: 14M15}
	\keywords{cohomology endomorphisms, complex Grassmann manifolds, generalized Dold spaces,  fixed point theory, coincidence theory}


\newwrite\markfile
\immediate\openout\markfile=boxpositions_endomorphisms.txt

  \setbox0=\hbox{#2}%

  \pdfsavepos

\begin{document}
\begin{abstract}
We classified graded endomorphisms of the rational cohomology algebra of the product of a sphere and a complex Grassmannian, whose images are nonzero  in the second cohomology of the Grassmannian.

We also derive necessary conditions for the generalized Dold spaces to satisfy the coincidence property, in particular the fixed-point property. As an application of our results, we obtain several sufficient conditions for the existence of a point of coincidence between a pair of continuous functions on certain generalized Dold spaces. 
\end{abstract}
	
\maketitle
	
	\section{Introduction} \label{intro}
	\markbox{0}{The} \markbox{1}{classification} \markbox{2}{of} \markbox{3}{endomorphisms} \markbox{4}{of} \markbox{5}{the} \markbox{6}{rational} \markbox{7}{cohomology} \markbox{8}{algebra} \markbox{9}{of} \markbox{10}{formal} \markbox{11}{spaces} \markbox{12}{was} \markbox{13}{greatly} \markbox{14}{motivated} \markbox{15}{by} \markbox{16}{Sullivan's} \markbox{17}{theory} \markbox{18}{where} \markbox{19}{it} \markbox{20}{was}  \markbox{21}{proved} \markbox{22}{that} \markbox{23}{rational} \markbox{24}{homotopy} \markbox{25}{class} \markbox{26}{of} \markbox{27}{self-maps} \markbox{28}{are} \markbox{29}{completely} \markbox{30}{determined} \markbox{31}{by} \markbox{32}{the} \markbox{33}{induced} \markbox{34}{graded} \markbox{35}{endomorphisms} \markbox{36}{of} \markbox{37}{their} \markbox{38}{rational} \markbox{39}{cohomology} \markbox{40}{algebras.} 
	
	\markbox{41}{In} \cite{brewster}, \markbox{42}{the} \markbox{43}{authors} \markbox{44}{developed} \markbox{45}{the} \markbox{46}{foundational} \markbox{47}{work} \markbox{48}{by} \markbox{49}{classifying} \markbox{50}{automorphisms} \markbox{51}{of} \markbox{52}{the} \markbox{53}{rational} \markbox{54}{cohomology} \markbox{55}{algebra} \markbox{56}{of} \markbox{57}{complex} \markbox{58}{Grassmannian.} \markbox{59}{Their} \markbox{60}{results} \markbox{61}{were} \markbox{62}{generalized} \markbox{63}{in} \cite{hoffman}, \markbox{64}{where} \markbox{65}{the} \markbox{66}{author} \markbox{67}{classified} \markbox{68}{graded} \markbox{69}{endomorphisms} \markbox{70}{of} \markbox{71}{the} \markbox{72}{rational} \markbox{73}{cohomology} \markbox{74}{algebra} \markbox{75}{of} \markbox{76}{complex} \markbox{77}{Grassmannian} \markbox{78}{which} \markbox{79}{are} \markbox{80}{nonzero} \markbox{81}{on} \markbox{82}{dimension} \markbox{m83}{$2$}. \markbox{84}{Further,} \markbox{85}{he} \markbox{86}{conjectured} \markbox{87}{that} \markbox{88}{every} \markbox{89}{graded} \markbox{90}{endomorphism}  \markbox{91}{vanishing} \markbox{92}{on} \markbox{93}{dimension} \markbox{94}{two} \markbox{95}{is} \markbox{96}{necessarily} \markbox{97}{trivial.} \markbox{98}{This} \markbox{99}{conjecture} \markbox{100}{was} \markbox{101}{proved} \markbox{102}{in} \cite{glover-homer} \markbox{103}{for} \markbox{104}{several} cases.
	
	\markbox{105}{The} \markbox{106}{cohomology} \markbox{107}{endomorphisms} \markbox{108}{are} \markbox{109}{also} \markbox{110}{studied} \markbox{111}{for} \markbox{112}{a} \markbox{113}{variety} \markbox{114}{of} \markbox{115}{homogeneous} \markbox{116}{spaces} \markbox{m117}{$G/H$}, \markbox{118}{where} \markbox{m119}{$G$} \markbox{120}{is} \markbox{121}{a} \markbox{122}{compact} \markbox{123}{connected} \markbox{124}{Lie} \markbox{125}{group} \markbox{126}{and} \markbox{m127}{$H$} \markbox{128}{is} \markbox{129}{a} closed
	\markbox{130}{subgroup} \markbox{131}{of} \markbox{132}{maximal} \markbox{133}{rank.} \markbox{134}{This} \markbox{135}{is} \markbox{136}{a} \markbox{137}{topic} \markbox{138}{of} \markbox{139}{interest} \markbox{140}{since} \markbox{141}{past} \markbox{142}{fifty} \markbox{143}{years} \markbox{144}{and} \markbox{145}{are} \markbox{146}{studied} \markbox{147}{in} \markbox{148}{several} \markbox{149}{papers} \cite{shiga-tezuka2, brewster-homer, hoffman-homer, Papadima, duan, duan-fang, duan-zhao, lin, goswami-sarkar}. 
	
	%However, we are interested in product spaces because a little is known about how cohomology endomorphisms behave under products.
    However, \markbox{150}{the} \markbox{151}{behavior} \markbox{152}{of} \markbox{153}{cohomology} \markbox{154}{endomorphisms} \markbox{155}{for} \markbox{156}{the} \markbox{157}{product} \markbox{158}{spaces} \markbox{159}{is} \markbox{160}{comparatively} \markbox{161}{less} \markbox{162}{explored,} \markbox{163}{and} \markbox{164}{this} \markbox{165}{provides} \markbox{166}{a} \markbox{167}{direction} \markbox{168}{for} study.
    \markbox{169}{We} \markbox{170}{are} \markbox{171}{mainly} \markbox{172}{interested} \markbox{173}{in} \markbox{174}{the} \markbox{175}{product} \markbox{176}{of} \markbox{177}{a} sphere
	\markbox{178}{with} \markbox{179}{complex} \markbox{180}{Grassmannian} \markbox{m181}{$\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{182}{because} \markbox{183}{the} \markbox{184}{sphere} \markbox{m185}{$\mathbb{S}^m$} \markbox{186}{has} \markbox{187}{a} \markbox{188}{simple,} \markbox{189}{singly} \markbox{190}{generated} \markbox{191}{cohomology} \markbox{192}{algebra,} \markbox{193}{while} \markbox{194}{the} \markbox{195}{Grassmannian} \markbox{m196}{$\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{197}{(of} \markbox{m198}{$k$}-planes \markbox{199}{in} \markbox{m200}{$\mathbb C^n$})
	\markbox{201}{carries} \markbox{202}{the} \markbox{203}{rich} \markbox{204}{structure} \markbox{205}{arising} \markbox{206}{from} \markbox{207}{Schubert} \markbox{208}{calculus.} \markbox{209}{We} \markbox{210}{have} \markbox{211}{classified} \markbox{212}{graded} \markbox{213}{endomorphisms} \markbox{214}{of} \markbox{215}{the} \markbox{216}{rational} \markbox{217}{cohomology} \markbox{218}{algebra} \markbox{m219}{$H^*(\mathbb{S}^m \times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb{Q})$}, \markbox{220}{whose} \markbox{221}{image} \markbox{222}{has} \markbox{223}{a} \markbox{224}{nonzero} \markbox{225}{component} \markbox{226}{in} \markbox{m227}{$H^2(\mathbb CG_{n,k},\mathbb Q)$}.  \markbox{228}{As} \markbox{229}{an} \markbox{230}{application} \markbox{231}{we} \markbox{232}{obtain} \markbox{233}{useful} \markbox{234}{results} \markbox{235}{in} \markbox{236}{coincidence} \markbox{237}{theory} \markbox{238}{and} \markbox{239}{in} \markbox{240}{particular,} \markbox{241}{fixed-point} \markbox{242}{theory.}  
	
	\markbox{243}{The} \markbox{244}{rational} \markbox{245}{cohomology} \markbox{246}{algebra} \markbox{247}{of} \markbox{248}{the} product
	\[
	H^*(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)\cong H^*(\mathbb S^m,\mathbb Q)\otimes H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)
	\]
	\markbox{249}{is} \markbox{250}{generated} \markbox{251}{by} \markbox{m252}{$u,c_1,c_2,\dots,c_k$}, \markbox{253}{where} \markbox{m254}{$H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{255}{(resp.} \markbox{m256}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m;\mathbb Q)$}) \markbox{257}{is} \markbox{258}{generated} \markbox{259}{by} \markbox{260}{certain} \markbox{261}{Chern} \markbox{262}{classes} \markbox{m263}{$c_1, \dots, c_k$} \markbox{264}{(resp.} \markbox{m265}{$u$}). \markbox{266}{Now,} \markbox{267}{we} \markbox{268}{are} \markbox{269}{ready} \markbox{270}{to} \markbox{271}{state} \markbox{272}{one} \markbox{273}{of} \markbox{274}{the} \markbox{275}{main} \markbox{276}{results} \markbox{277}{of} \markbox{278}{our} \markbox{279}{paper} \markbox{280}{which} \markbox{281}{proves} \markbox{282}{that} \markbox{283}{the} \markbox{284}{rigidity} \markbox{285}{of} \markbox{m286}{$H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{287}{persists} \markbox{288}{in} \markbox{m289}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{290}{even} \markbox{291}{in} \markbox{292}{the} \markbox{293}{presence} \markbox{294}{of} \markbox{295}{spherical} \markbox{296}{cohomology} classes.
	\begin{theorem}
		\markbox{297}{Let} \markbox{m298}{$\phi$} \markbox{299}{be} \markbox{300}{a} \markbox{301}{graded} \markbox{302}{endomorphism} \markbox{303}{of} 
		\markbox{m304}{$H^*(\mathbb S^{m}\times\mathbb C G_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} 
		\markbox{305}{satisfying} \markbox{m306}{$\phi(c_1)\neq a u, \, a\in\mathbb Q$}.  
		\markbox{307}{Then} \markbox{308}{there} \markbox{309}{exists} \markbox{310}{a} \markbox{311}{nonzero} \markbox{312}{rational} \markbox{m313}{$\lambda$} \markbox{314}{such} \markbox{315}{that} \markbox{316}{the} \markbox{317}{following} holds.
		\begin{enumerate}\label{result main}
			\item {} If \markbox{m318}{$k < n - k,$} 
			$$ \phi(c_i) = \lambda^i c_i, \forall i \in \{1,2,\dots,k\}$$
			\markbox{319}{If} \markbox{m320}{$k = n - k$}, \markbox{321}{there} \markbox{322}{is} \markbox{323}{an} \markbox{324}{additional} \markbox{325}{possibility} \markbox{326}{of} \markbox{m327}{$\phi$} \markbox{328}{that} \markbox{329}{it} \markbox{330}{is} \markbox{331}{induced} \markbox{332}{by} \markbox{333}{the} \markbox{334}{homeomorphism} 
			\[
			\mathbb{C}G_{2k,k} \longrightarrow \mathbb{C}G_{2k,k}, 
			\quad L \longmapsto L^{\perp},
			\]
			\markbox{335}{where} \markbox{m336}{$L^{\perp}$} \markbox{337}{denotes} \markbox{338}{the} \markbox{339}{orthogonal} \markbox{340}{complement} \markbox{341}{of} \markbox{342}{the} \markbox{m343}{$k$}-plane \markbox{m344}{$L$} \markbox{345}{in} \markbox{m346}{$\mathbb{C}^{2k}$}.
			
			\item 
			{} The \markbox{347}{image} \markbox{348}{of} \markbox{m349}{$H^*(\mathbb{S}^m;\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{350}{under} \markbox{m351}{$\phi$} \markbox{352}{lies} \markbox{353}{in} 
			\markbox{m354}{$H^*(\mathbb{S}^m;\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{355}{or} \markbox{356}{in} \markbox{m357}{$H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{358}{i.e.} $$\phi(u) = \mu u,\, \mu \in \mathbb{Q}, \text{ or } \phi(u) \in H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb{Q}), \text{ with } (\phi(u))^2 =0.$$
			
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{theorem}
	\markbox{359}{Unlike} \markbox{360}{the} \markbox{361}{case} \markbox{362}{of} \markbox{363}{the} \markbox{364}{complex} \markbox{365}{Grassmannian,} \markbox{366}{we} \markbox{367}{cannot} \markbox{368}{expect} \markbox{369}{a} graded
	\markbox{370}{endomorphism} \markbox{371}{of} \markbox{m372}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{373}{to} be
	\markbox{374}{trivial} \markbox{375}{merely} \markbox{376}{because} \markbox{377}{it} \markbox{378}{vanishes} \markbox{379}{in} \markbox{m380}{$H^2(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q})$}. 
	\markbox{381}{In} \markbox{382}{fact,} \markbox{383}{we} \markbox{384}{proved} \markbox{385}{that} \markbox{386}{for} \markbox{387}{any} \markbox{388}{choice} \markbox{389}{of} \markbox{m390}{$P_i \in H^{2i-m}(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{391}{and} \markbox{m392}{$Q\in \mathbb Qu\cup  H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{393}{with} \markbox{m394}{$Q^2=0$}, \markbox{395}{there} \markbox{396}{exist} \markbox{397}{a} \markbox{398}{graded} \markbox{399}{endomorphism} \markbox{m400}{$\phi$} \markbox{401}{on} \markbox{m402}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{403}{such} \markbox{404}{that} \markbox{m405}{$\phi(c_i) = uP_i, \, \forall i$} \markbox{406}{and} \markbox{m407}{$\phi(u)=Q$}.
	%In fact, we proved that for any choice of $P_i \in H^{2i-m}(\mathbb{C}G;\mathbb{Q})$ and $Q =au, a\in \mathbb{Q}$, there exist a graded endomorphism $\phi$ on $H^*(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$ such that $\phi(c_i) = uP_i, \, \forall i$ and $\phi(u)=Q$.
	We \markbox{408}{also} \markbox{409}{proved} \markbox{410}{that} \markbox{411}{if} \markbox{412}{a} \markbox{413}{continuous} \markbox{414}{function} \markbox{415}{on} \markbox{m416}{$\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{417}{stabilizes} \markbox{418}{a} \markbox{419}{copy} \markbox{420}{of} \markbox{421}{Grassmannian} \markbox{422}{then} \markbox{423}{the} \markbox{424}{induced} \markbox{425}{cohomology} \markbox{426}{endomorphism} \markbox{427}{stabilizes} \markbox{428}{the} \markbox{429}{subalgebra} \markbox{m430}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m ;\mathbb Q)$}.
	
	\markbox{431}{Our} \markbox{432}{study} \markbox{433}{is} \markbox{434}{also} \markbox{435}{motivated} \markbox{436}{by} \markbox{437}{the} \markbox{438}{theory} \markbox{439}{of} \markbox{440}{generalized} \markbox{441}{Dold} \markbox{442}{spaces} \markbox{443}{because} \markbox{444}{the} \markbox{445}{product} \markbox{446}{space} \markbox{m447}{$\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{448}{is} \markbox{449}{a} \markbox{450}{double} \markbox{451}{cover} \markbox{452}{of} \markbox{453}{certain}  \markbox{454}{generalized} \markbox{455}{Dold} \markbox{456}{spaces} \markbox{457}{(GDS).} %denoted by $P(m,n,k)$.
	The \markbox{458}{classical} \markbox{459}{Dold} \markbox{460}{manifolds} \markbox{461}{were} \markbox{462}{introduced} \markbox{463}{in} \cite{dold} \markbox{464}{to} \markbox{465}{construct} \markbox{466}{odd-dimensional} \markbox{467}{generators} \markbox{468}{for} \markbox{469}{Thom's} \markbox{470}{unoriented} \markbox{471}{cobordism} \markbox{472}{ring.} \markbox{473}{In} \markbox{474}{this} \markbox{475}{paper,} \markbox{476}{we} \markbox{477}{are} \markbox{478}{interested} \markbox{479}{in} \markbox{480}{the} \markbox{481}{GDS} \markbox{482}{introduced} \markbox{483}{in} \cite{nath-sankaran} \markbox{484}{and} \markbox{485}{defined} \markbox{486}{as}  %These spaces have been extensively studied from various aspects (see \cite{ucci, khare, korbas, mukerjee}). 
	\[
	P(m,n,k):=\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}/\!\!\sim, \text { where } (s,L)\sim (-s,\bar L).
	\]
	\markbox{487}{As} \markbox{488}{an} \markbox{489}{application} \markbox{490}{of} \thmref{result main}, \markbox{491}{we} \markbox{492}{describe} \markbox{493}{endomorphisms} \markbox{494}{of} \markbox{m495}{$H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{496}{induced} \markbox{497}{by} \markbox{498}{continuous} \markbox{499}{functions} \markbox{500}{on} \markbox{m501}{$P(m,n,k)$}. \markbox{502}{Using} \markbox{503}{this} \markbox{504}{description,} \markbox{505}{we} \markbox{506}{prove} \markbox{507}{that} \markbox{508}{every} \markbox{509}{automorphism} \markbox{510}{of} \markbox{m511}{$H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{512}{induced} \markbox{513}{by} \markbox{514}{a} \markbox{515}{continuous} \markbox{516}{function} \markbox{517}{on} \markbox{m518}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{519}{lifts} \markbox{520}{to} \markbox{521}{an} \markbox{522}{automorphism} \markbox{523}{of} \markbox{m524}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{525}{if} \markbox{m526}{$n>2$}. 
	
	\markbox{527}{Our} \markbox{528}{broader} \markbox{529}{aim} \markbox{530}{is} \markbox{531}{to} \markbox{532}{apply} \thmref{result main} \markbox{533}{to} \markbox{534}{obtain} \markbox{535}{results} \markbox{536}{in} \markbox{537}{coincidence} \markbox{538}{theory.} \markbox{539}{Coincidence} \markbox{540}{theory} \markbox{541}{has} \markbox{542}{been} \markbox{543}{extensively} \markbox{544}{studied} \markbox{545}{in} \cite{hoffman-noncoin, glover-homer coin, wong}. %and fixed point theory.
	A \markbox{546}{pair} \markbox{m547}{$(X,g)$} \markbox{548}{where} \markbox{m549}{$g$} \markbox{550}{is} \markbox{551}{a} \markbox{552}{continuous} \markbox{553}{function} \markbox{554}{on} \markbox{m555}{$X$} \markbox{556}{is} \markbox{557}{said} \markbox{558}{to} \markbox{559}{have} \markbox{560}{the} \markbox{561}{coincidence} \markbox{562}{property} \markbox{563}{if} \markbox{m564}{$g$} \markbox{565}{has} \markbox{566}{a} \markbox{567}{point} \markbox{568}{of} \markbox{569}{coincidence} \markbox{570}{with} \markbox{571}{every} \markbox{572}{continuous} \markbox{573}{function} \markbox{574}{on} \markbox{m575}{$X$}. \markbox{576}{In} \markbox{577}{particular,} \markbox{578}{if} \markbox{m579}{$g$} \markbox{580}{is} \markbox{581}{the} \markbox{582}{identity} \markbox{583}{map,} \markbox{584}{then} \markbox{585}{the} \markbox{586}{coincidence} \markbox{587}{property} \markbox{588}{is} \markbox{589}{same} \markbox{590}{as} \markbox{591}{the} \markbox{592}{fixed-point} \markbox{593}{property} \markbox{594}{of} \markbox{m595}{$X$}.
	%We are providing necessary conditions for certain generalized Dold spaces to satisfy coincidence property.
	
	We \markbox{596}{have} \markbox{597}{generalized} \markbox{598}{Theorem} \markbox{m599}{$2$} \markbox{600}{of} \cite{glover-homer} \markbox{601}{to} \markbox{602}{the} \markbox{603}{setting} \markbox{604}{of} \markbox{605}{coincidence} \markbox{606}{theory} \markbox{607}{and} \markbox{608}{proved} \markbox{609}{that} \markbox{610}{the} \markbox{611}{pair} \markbox{m612}{$(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k},g)$} \markbox{613}{satisfies} \markbox{614}{the} \markbox{615}{coincidence} \markbox{616}{property} \markbox{617}{if} \markbox{m618}{$k(n-k)$} \markbox{619}{is} \markbox{620}{even} \markbox{621}{and} \markbox{m622}{$g$} \markbox{623}{has} \markbox{624}{nonzero} \markbox{625}{Brouwer} degree.
	\markbox{626}{To} \markbox{627}{conclude,} \markbox{628}{using} \markbox{629}{the} \markbox{630}{Lefschetz} \markbox{631}{Coincidence} \markbox{632}{Theorem} \markbox{633}{and} \thmref{result main}, \markbox{634}{we} \markbox{635}{obtained} \markbox{636}{multiple} \markbox{637}{situations} \markbox{638}{when} \markbox{639}{two} \markbox{640}{continuous} \markbox{641}{functions} \markbox{642}{on} \markbox{643}{the} \markbox{644}{generalized} \markbox{645}{Dold} \markbox{646}{space} \markbox{m647}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{648}{are} \markbox{649}{guaranteed} \markbox{650}{to} \markbox{651}{have} \markbox{652}{a} \markbox{653}{point} \markbox{654}{of} \markbox{655}{coincidence,} \markbox{656}{and} \markbox{657}{found} \markbox{658}{certain} \markbox{659}{pairs} \markbox{m660}{$(P(m,n,k),g)$} \markbox{661}{satisfying} \markbox{662}{the} \markbox{663}{coincidence} property.
	%Using Lefschetz Coincidence Theorem and \thmref{result main}, we succeed in obtaining sufficient conditions for the existence of a point of coincidence between any two continuous functions on $P(m,n,k)$ when $k(n-k)$ is even.
	%At last, we explored when two continuous functions on the generalized Dold space $P(m,n,k)$ has a point of coincidence. Using Lefschetz Coincidence Theorem and \thmref{result main}, we succeed in obtaining sufficient conditions for the existence of a point of coincidence between any two continuous functions on $P(m,n,k)$ when $k(n-k)$ is even.
	
	The \markbox{664}{paper} \markbox{665}{is} \markbox{666}{organized} \markbox{667}{as} \markbox{668}{follows:} \\
	\markbox{669}{In} \secref{section 2} \markbox{670}{we} \markbox{671}{develop} \markbox{672}{the} \markbox{673}{necessary} \markbox{674}{background} \markbox{675}{and} \markbox{676}{recall} \markbox{677}{some} \markbox{678}{relevant} \markbox{679}{results.} \secref{section 3} \markbox{680}{is} \markbox{681}{devoted} \markbox{682}{to} \markbox{683}{the} \markbox{684}{study} \markbox{685}{of} \markbox{686}{graded} \markbox{687}{endomorphisms} \markbox{688}{of} \markbox{689}{the} \markbox{690}{rational} \markbox{691}{cohomology} \markbox{692}{algebra} \markbox{693}{of} \markbox{m694}{$\mathbb S^{m}\times \mathbb C G_{n,k}$}, \markbox{695}{from} \markbox{696}{which} \markbox{697}{we} \markbox{698}{extract} \markbox{699}{several} \markbox{700}{consequences.} \markbox{701}{These} \markbox{702}{are} \markbox{703}{applied} \markbox{704}{in} \secref{section 4} \markbox{705}{to} \markbox{706}{obtain} \markbox{707}{the} \markbox{708}{coincidence-theoretic} results.
	
	\iffalse For \markbox{709}{formal} \markbox{710}{spaces,} \markbox{711}{Sullivan's} \markbox{712}{theory} \markbox{713}{shows} \markbox{714}{that} \markbox{715}{the} \markbox{716}{rational} \markbox{717}{homotopy} \markbox{718}{class} \markbox{719}{of} \markbox{720}{a} \markbox{721}{self-maps} \markbox{722}{are} \markbox{723}{completely} \markbox{724}{determined} \markbox{725}{by} \markbox{726}{the} \markbox{727}{induced} \markbox{728}{graded} \markbox{729}{endomorphisms} \markbox{730}{of} \markbox{731}{their} \markbox{732}{rational} \markbox{733}{cohomology} \markbox{734}{algebras.} \markbox{735}{This} \markbox{736}{viewpoint} \markbox{737}{has} \markbox{738}{motivated} \markbox{739}{extensive} \markbox{740}{work} \markbox{741}{on} \markbox{742}{cohomology} \markbox{743}{endomorphisms} \markbox{744}{of} \markbox{745}{various} \markbox{746}{classical}  spaces.
	%, particularly homogeneous spaces of compact Lie groups.
	%Initial results for complex Grassmannians were obtained by Brewster \cite{}, Glover-Homer \cite{}, and Hoffman \cite{}, followed by contributions of  Shiga-Tezuka \cite{}, Papadima \cite{}, and Duan et al. (\cite{},\cite{},\cite{}) for broader classes of homogeneous spaces.
	% $G/H$, where $G$ is complact connected Lie group and $H$ is a closed subgroup of maximal rank.
	
	
	Early \markbox{747}{foundational} \markbox{748}{work} \markbox{749}{on} \markbox{750}{cohomology} \markbox{751}{endomorphisms} \markbox{752}{of} \markbox{753}{complex} Grassmannians
	\markbox{754}{was} \markbox{755}{carried} \markbox{756}{out} \markbox{757}{in} \markbox{758}{1978} \markbox{759}{by} \markbox{760}{Brewster,} \markbox{761}{in} \markbox{762}{his} Ph.D.\ thesis \cite{brewster} \markbox{763}{on} cohomology
	\markbox{764}{automorphisms,} \markbox{765}{and} \markbox{766}{by} \markbox{767}{Glover} \markbox{768}{and} \markbox{769}{Homer} \cite{glover-homer}.
	\markbox{770}{This} \markbox{771}{was} \markbox{772}{followed} \markbox{773}{by} \markbox{774}{Hoffman's} \markbox{775}{1984} work
	\cite{hoffman}, \markbox{776}{which} \markbox{777}{classified} \markbox{778}{all} \markbox{779}{rational} \markbox{780}{cohomology} \markbox{781}{endomorphisms} \markbox{782}{that} are
	\markbox{783}{non-trivial} \markbox{784}{in} \markbox{785}{degree} \markbox{786}{two.} \markbox{787}{He} \markbox{788}{showed} \markbox{789}{that} \markbox{790}{for} \markbox{791}{the} \markbox{792}{Grassmannians} \markbox{m793}{$\mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{794}{(of} \markbox{m795}{$k$}-planes \markbox{796}{in} \markbox{m797}{$\mathbb{C}^n$}), \markbox{798}{such} \markbox{799}{endomorphisms} \markbox{800}{are} \markbox{801}{precisely} \markbox{802}{\emph{Adams maps}}: \markbox{803}{each} \markbox{804}{cohomology} \markbox{805}{class} \markbox{m806}{$x$} \markbox{807}{of} \markbox{808}{degree} \markbox{m809}{$2i$} \markbox{810}{maps} \markbox{811}{to} \markbox{812}{a} \markbox{813}{scalar} \markbox{814}{multiple} \markbox{m815}{$\lambda^i x$} \markbox{816}{for} \markbox{817}{some} \markbox{818}{fixed} \markbox{819}{nonzero} \markbox{m820}{$\lambda \in \mathbb{Q}$}, \markbox{821}{except} \markbox{822}{in} \markbox{823}{special} \markbox{824}{symmetric} \markbox{825}{cases} \markbox{m826}{$n=2k$}, \markbox{827}{where} \markbox{828}{additional} \markbox{829}{involutive} \markbox{830}{automorphisms} \markbox{831}{appear.} \markbox{832}{Hoffman} \markbox{833}{further} \markbox{834}{conjectured} \markbox{835}{that} \markbox{836}{every} \markbox{837}{endomorphism} \markbox{838}{vanishing} \markbox{839}{in} \markbox{840}{degree} \markbox{841}{two} \markbox{842}{is} \markbox{843}{necessarily} \markbox{844}{trivial.} \markbox{845}{The} \markbox{846}{results} \markbox{847}{of} \markbox{848}{Glover} \markbox{849}{and} \markbox{850}{Homer} \markbox{851}{(see} \cite{glover-homer}) \markbox{852}{support} \markbox{853}{this} \markbox{854}{conjecture} \markbox{855}{in} \markbox{856}{several} \markbox{857}{cases,} \markbox{858}{under} \markbox{859}{a} \markbox{860}{certain} \markbox{861}{hypothesis,} \markbox{862}{say} (GH).
	
	
	\markbox{863}{Later,} \markbox{864}{cohomology} \markbox{865}{endomorphisms} \markbox{866}{were} \markbox{867}{studied} \markbox{868}{for} \markbox{869}{a} \markbox{870}{variety} \markbox{871}{of} homogeneous
	\markbox{872}{spaces} \markbox{m873}{$G/H$}, \markbox{874}{where} \markbox{m875}{$G$} \markbox{876}{is} \markbox{877}{a} \markbox{878}{compact} \markbox{879}{connected} \markbox{880}{Lie} \markbox{881}{group} \markbox{882}{and} \markbox{m883}{$H$} \markbox{884}{is} \markbox{885}{a} closed
	\markbox{886}{subgroup} \markbox{887}{of} \markbox{888}{maximal} \markbox{889}{rank.} \markbox{890}{For} examples,
	\markbox{891}{Shiga} \markbox{892}{and} \markbox{893}{Tezuka} \markbox{894}{examined} cohomology
	\markbox{895}{automorphisms} \markbox{896}{of} \markbox{897}{homogeneous} \markbox{898}{spaces} \markbox{899}{of} \markbox{900}{simple} \markbox{901}{Lie} \markbox{902}{groups} \cite{shiga-tezuka2}, \markbox{903}{and} \markbox{904}{Papadima} \markbox{905}{described} \markbox{906}{all} \markbox{907}{cohomology} \markbox{908}{automorphisms} \markbox{909}{when} \markbox{910}{the} \markbox{911}{subgroup} \markbox{912}{is} \markbox{913}{a} \markbox{914}{maximal} torus,
	\markbox{915}{working} \markbox{916}{over} \markbox{917}{both} \markbox{m918}{$\mathbb Q$} \markbox{919}{and} \markbox{m920}{$\mathbb R$} \cite{Papadima}. \markbox{921}{Hoffman} \markbox{922}{and} \markbox{923}{Homer} also
	\markbox{924}{proposed} \markbox{925}{a} \markbox{926}{general} \markbox{927}{classification} \markbox{928}{for} \markbox{929}{homogeneous} \markbox{930}{spaces} \markbox{931}{arising} \markbox{932}{from} unitary
	\markbox{933}{groups,} \markbox{934}{together} \markbox{935}{with} \markbox{936}{partial} \markbox{937}{results} \markbox{938}{supporting} \markbox{939}{their} \markbox{940}{conjecture.} Further
	\markbox{941}{progress} \markbox{942}{includes} \markbox{943}{the} \markbox{944}{study} \markbox{945}{of} \markbox{946}{integral} \markbox{947}{cohomology} \markbox{948}{endomorphisms} \markbox{949}{of} \markbox{950}{the} \markbox{951}{Grassmannian} \markbox{952}{of} \markbox{953}{complex} structures
	\markbox{m954}{$SO(2n)/U(n)$} \cite{duan}, \markbox{955}{and} \markbox{956}{the} \markbox{957}{work} \markbox{958}{of} \markbox{959}{Duan} \markbox{960}{and} \markbox{961}{Fang} \markbox{962}{on} \markbox{963}{the} \markbox{964}{eight} exceptional
	\markbox{965}{Grassmannians} \cite{duan-fang}. \markbox{966}{Related} \markbox{967}{developments} \markbox{968}{appear} \markbox{969}{in} \cite{duan-zhao}, \cite{lin}, \markbox{970}{and} \cite{goswami-sarkar}.
	
	
	\markbox{971}{Most} \markbox{972}{of} \markbox{973}{these} \markbox{974}{results,} \markbox{975}{however,} \markbox{976}{concern} \markbox{977}{specific} \markbox{978}{classes} \markbox{979}{of} \markbox{980}{homogeneous} spaces.
	\markbox{981}{Comparatively} \markbox{982}{little} \markbox{983}{is} \markbox{984}{known} \markbox{985}{about} \markbox{986}{how} \markbox{987}{cohomology} \markbox{988}{endomorphisms} \markbox{989}{behave} for
	\markbox{990}{products.} \markbox{991}{The} \markbox{992}{product} \markbox{993}{of} \markbox{994}{a} sphere
	\markbox{995}{with} \markbox{996}{a} \markbox{997}{complex} \markbox{998}{Grassmannian} \markbox{m999}{$\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{1000}{offers} \markbox{1001}{a} \markbox{1002}{particularly} \markbox{1003}{useful} \markbox{1004}{setting} \markbox{1005}{for} \markbox{1006}{such} \markbox{1007}{questions:} the
	\markbox{1008}{sphere} \markbox{1009}{has} \markbox{1010}{a} \markbox{1011}{simple,} \markbox{1012}{singly} \markbox{1013}{generated} \markbox{1014}{cohomology} \markbox{1015}{algebra,} \markbox{1016}{while} \markbox{1017}{the} Grassmannian
	\markbox{1018}{carries} \markbox{1019}{the} \markbox{1020}{rich} \markbox{1021}{structure} \markbox{1022}{arising} \markbox{1023}{from} \markbox{1024}{Schubert} \markbox{1025}{calculus.}  
	\markbox{1026}{Although} \markbox{1027}{the} \markbox{1028}{garded} \markbox{1029}{endomorphisms} \markbox{1030}{of} \markbox{1031}{the} \markbox{1032}{rational} \markbox{1033}{cohomology} \markbox{1034}{algebra} \markbox{1035}{of} \markbox{1036}{the} \markbox{1037}{product,} \markbox{m1038}{$\mathrm{End}\big(H^*(\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)\big)$}, \markbox{1039}{are} \markbox{1040}{interesting} \markbox{1041}{in} \markbox{1042}{their} \markbox{1043}{own} \markbox{1044}{right,} \markbox{1045}{our} \markbox{1046}{broader} \markbox{1047}{aim} \markbox{1048}{is} \markbox{1049}{to} \markbox{1050}{apply} \markbox{1051}{them} \markbox{1052}{to} \markbox{1053}{the} \markbox{1054}{\textit{coincidence theory}} \markbox{1055}{of} \markbox{1056}{certain} \markbox{1057}{\textit{generalized Dold space}}s.
	\markbox{1058}{Coincidence} \markbox{1059}{theory} \markbox{1060}{studies} \markbox{1061}{the} \markbox{1062}{set} \markbox{1063}{of} \markbox{1064}{points} \markbox{m1065}{$x$} \markbox{1066}{for} \markbox{1067}{which} \markbox{1068}{two} \markbox{1069}{maps} 
	\markbox{m1070}{$f,g : X \to X$} \markbox{1071}{satisfy} \markbox{m1072}{$f(x)=g(x)$}, \markbox{1073}{and} \markbox{1074}{seeks} \markbox{1075}{criteria} \markbox{1076}{for} \markbox{1077}{the} 
	\markbox{1078}{existence} \markbox{1079}{or} \markbox{1080}{elimination} \markbox{1081}{of} \markbox{1082}{such} \markbox{1083}{points.} 
	
	
	%For a continuous map $g$ on a space $X$, the pair $(X,g)$ is said to have the \emph{coincidence property} (abbreviated as CP) if every continuous map $f:X\to X$ has a coincidence point with $g$; that is, $f(x)=g(x)$ for some $x\in X$.
	The \markbox{1084}{classical} \markbox{1085}{Dold} \markbox{1086}{manifolds} \markbox{m1087}{$P(m,n):=\mathbb S^{m}\times\mathbb CP^{n}/\!\sim$}, 
	\markbox{1088}{where} \markbox{m1089}{$(s,L)\sim(-s,\bar L)$}, \markbox{1090}{were} \markbox{1091}{introduced} \markbox{1092}{by} \markbox{1093}{Dold} \cite{dold} \markbox{1094}{to} \markbox{1095}{construct} \markbox{1096}{odd-dimensional} \markbox{1097}{generators} \markbox{1098}{for} \markbox{1099}{Thom's} \markbox{1100}{unoriented} \markbox{1101}{cobordism} \markbox{1102}{ring.} \markbox{1103}{These} \markbox{1104}{spaces} \markbox{1105}{have} \markbox{1106}{been} \markbox{1107}{extensively} \markbox{1108}{studied} \markbox{1109}{and} \markbox{1110}{generalized.} \markbox{1111}{Nath} \markbox{1112}{and} \markbox{1113}{Sankaran} \cite{nath-sankaran} \markbox{1114}{extended} \markbox{1115}{the} \markbox{1116}{construction} \markbox{1117}{by} \markbox{1118}{replacing} \markbox{m1119}{$\mathbb CP^{n}$} \markbox{1120}{with} \markbox{1121}{a} \markbox{1122}{Hausdorff} \markbox{1123}{space} \markbox{m1124}{$X$} \markbox{1125}{equipped} \markbox{1126}{with} \markbox{1127}{an} \markbox{1128}{involution} \markbox{m1129}{$\sigma$} \markbox{1130}{with} \markbox{1131}{nonempty} \markbox{1132}{fixed} \markbox{1133}{points.} \markbox{1134}{A} \markbox{1135}{further} \markbox{1136}{generalization} \markbox{1137}{in} \cite{mandal-sankaran} \markbox{1138}{replaces} \markbox{1139}{the} \markbox{1140}{sphere} \markbox{m1141}{$\mathbb S^{m}$} \markbox{1142}{by} \markbox{1143}{a} \markbox{1144}{space} \markbox{m1145}{$S$} \markbox{1146}{equipped} \markbox{1147}{with} \markbox{1148}{a} \markbox{1149}{free} \markbox{1150}{involution} \markbox{m1151}{$\alpha$}, \markbox{1152}{leading} to
	\[
	P(S,\alpha,X,\sigma):=S\times X/\!\sim,\text{ where } (s,x)\sim(\alpha(s),\sigma(x)),
	\]
	\markbox{1153}{which} \markbox{1154}{is} \markbox{1155}{called} \markbox{1156}{a} \markbox{1157}{\emph{generalized Dold space}} (GDS).
	\markbox{1158}{Here} \markbox{1159}{the} \markbox{1160}{quotient} \markbox{1161}{map} \markbox{m1162}{$\pi: S\times X\to P(S,\alpha,X,\sigma)$} \markbox{1163}{is} \markbox{1164}{a} \markbox{1165}{double} covering.
	%The space $P(S,\alpha,X,\sigma)$ has a $X$-bundle structure over $Y:=S/\!\sim,$ where $s\sim \alpha(s)$.
	
	
	The \markbox{1166}{class} \markbox{1167}{of} \markbox{1168}{GDS} \markbox{1169}{which} \markbox{1170}{we} \markbox{1171}{are} \markbox{1172}{interested} \markbox{1173}{in} \markbox{1174}{is} \markbox{m1175}{$P(m,n,k):=P(\mathbb S^m,\alpha,\mathbb CG_{n,k},\sigma)$}, \markbox{1176}{where} \markbox{m1177}{$\alpha $} \markbox{1178}{is} \markbox{1179}{the} \markbox{1180}{antipodal} \markbox{1181}{map} \markbox{1182}{on} \markbox{1183}{the} \markbox{1184}{sphere} \markbox{1185}{and} \markbox{1186}{the} \markbox{1187}{involution} \markbox{m1188}{$\sigma$} \markbox{1189}{on} \markbox{m1190}{$\mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{1191}{is} \markbox{1192}{induced} \markbox{1193}{from} \markbox{1194}{the} \markbox{1195}{standard} \markbox{1196}{complex} \markbox{1197}{conjugation} \markbox{1198}{on} \markbox{m1199}{$\mathbb C^n$}. \markbox{1200}{One} \markbox{1201}{observes} \markbox{1202}{that} \markbox{1203}{for} \markbox{1204}{any} \markbox{1205}{map} \markbox{m1206}{$f$} \markbox{1207}{on} \markbox{m1208}{$P(m,n,k)$}, \markbox{1209}{there} \markbox{1210}{exist} \markbox{1211}{a} \markbox{m1212}{$\alpha\times \sigma$}-equivariant \markbox{1213}{map} \markbox{m1214}{$\tilde f$} \markbox{1215}{on} \markbox{m1216}{$\mathbb S^m\times\mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{1217}{such} \markbox{1218}{that} \markbox{m1219}{$\pi\circ \tilde f=f\circ \pi.$}
	
	
	\markbox{1220}{Let} \markbox{1221}{us} \markbox{1222}{regard} \markbox{m1223}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m;\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{1224}{and} \markbox{m1225}{$H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} as
	\markbox{1226}{subalgebras} \markbox{1227}{of} \markbox{m1228}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$}.
	\markbox{1229}{Since} \markbox{m1230}{$H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{1231}{is} \markbox{1232}{generated} \markbox{1233}{by} \markbox{1234}{certain} \markbox{1235}{Chern} classes
	\markbox{m1236}{$c_1,c_2,\dots,c_k$}, \markbox{1237}{it} \markbox{1238}{follows} \markbox{1239}{that} 
	\[
	H^*(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)\cong H^*(\mathbb S^m,\mathbb Q)\otimes H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)
	\]
	\markbox{1240}{is} \markbox{1241}{generated} \markbox{1242}{by} \markbox{m1243}{$u,c_1,c_2,\dots,c_k$}, \markbox{1244}{where} \markbox{m1245}{$u$} \markbox{1246}{generates} \markbox{m1247}{$H^m(\mathbb S^m;\mathbb Q)$}.
	\markbox{1248}{We} \markbox{1249}{are} \markbox{1250}{now} \markbox{1251}{ready} \markbox{1252}{to} \markbox{1253}{present} \markbox{1254}{our} \markbox{1255}{main} \markbox{1256}{results;} \markbox{1257}{the} \markbox{1258}{following} \markbox{1259}{is} \markbox{1260}{one} \markbox{1261}{of} \markbox{1262}{them,} \markbox{1263}{which} \markbox{1264}{shows} \markbox{1265}{that} \markbox{1266}{the} \markbox{1267}{rigidity} of
	\markbox{m1268}{$H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{1269}{persists} \markbox{1270}{in} \markbox{1271}{the} \markbox{1272}{cohomology} \markbox{1273}{of} \markbox{1274}{the}  \markbox{1275}{product:} \markbox{1276}{even} \markbox{1277}{in} \markbox{1278}{the} presence
	\markbox{1279}{of} \markbox{1280}{spherical} \markbox{1281}{cohomology} \markbox{1282}{classes,} \markbox{1283}{any} \markbox{1284}{graded} \markbox{1285}{endomorphism} \markbox{1286}{whose} \markbox{1287}{image} \markbox{1288}{has} \markbox{1289}{a} \markbox{1290}{nonzero} \markbox{1291}{component} \markbox{1292}{in} \markbox{m1293}{$H^{2}(\mathbb C G_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{1294}{forces}  \markbox{m1295}{$H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{1296}{to} \markbox{1297}{behave} \markbox{1298}{exactly} \markbox{1299}{as} \markbox{1300}{it} \markbox{1301}{does} \markbox{1302}{on} \markbox{1303}{its} own.
	\markbox{1304}{More} \markbox{1305}{precisely,} \markbox{1306}{we} \markbox{1307}{obtain:} %that any graded endomorphism which is nontrivial on $H^2(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$ necessarily preserves  $H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$.  Furthermore, the image of $H^*(\mathbb S^m;\mathbb Q)$ under such an endomorphism lies either entirely in $H^*(\mathbb S^m;\mathbb Q)$ or entirely in $H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$.
	\begin{theorem}
		\markbox{1308}{Let} \markbox{m1309}{$\phi$} \markbox{1310}{be} \markbox{1311}{a} \markbox{1312}{graded} \markbox{1313}{endomorphism} \markbox{1314}{of} 
		\markbox{m1315}{$H^*(\mathbb S^{m}\times\mathbb C G_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} 
		\markbox{1316}{satisfying} \markbox{m1317}{$\phi(c_1)\neq a u$} \markbox{1318}{for} \markbox{1319}{any} \markbox{m1320}{$a\in\mathbb Q$}.  
		\markbox{1321}{Then} \markbox{1322}{the} \markbox{1323}{following} \markbox{1324}{statements} hold:
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item {} If \markbox{m1325}{$k < n - k$}, \markbox{1326}{there} \markbox{1327}{exists} \markbox{1328}{a} \markbox{1329}{nonzero} \markbox{1330}{rational} \markbox{1331}{number} \markbox{m1332}{$\lambda$} \markbox{1333}{such} that
			\[
			\phi(x) = \lambda^i x 
			\quad \text{for all } x \in H^{2i}(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}).
			\]
			\markbox{1334}{If} \markbox{m1335}{$k = n - k$}, \markbox{1336}{there} \markbox{1337}{is} \markbox{1338}{an} \markbox{1339}{additional} \markbox{1340}{possibility} \markbox{1341}{of} \markbox{m1342}{$\phi$} \markbox{1343}{induced} \markbox{1344}{by} \markbox{1345}{the} \markbox{1346}{homeomorphism} 
			\[
			\mathbb{C}G_{2k,k} \longrightarrow \mathbb{C}G_{2k,k}, 
			\quad L \longmapsto L^{\perp},
			\]
			\markbox{1347}{where} \markbox{m1348}{$L^{\perp}$} \markbox{1349}{denotes} \markbox{1350}{the} \markbox{1351}{orthogonal} \markbox{1352}{complement} \markbox{1353}{of} \markbox{1354}{the} \markbox{m1355}{$k$}-plane \markbox{m1356}{$L$} \markbox{1357}{in} \markbox{m1358}{$\mathbb{C}^{2k}$}.
			
			\item 
			{} The \markbox{1359}{image} \markbox{1360}{of} \markbox{m1361}{$H^*(\mathbb{S}^m;\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{1362}{under} \markbox{m1363}{$\phi$} \markbox{1364}{lies} \markbox{1365}{either} \markbox{1366}{in} 
			\markbox{m1367}{$H^*(\mathbb{S}^m;\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{1368}{or} \markbox{1369}{in} \markbox{m1370}{$H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb{Q})$}.
			
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{theorem}
	
	\markbox{1371}{Unlike} \markbox{1372}{the} \markbox{1373}{case} \markbox{1374}{of} \markbox{1375}{the} \markbox{1376}{complex} \markbox{1377}{Grassmannian,} \markbox{1378}{we} \markbox{1379}{cannot} \markbox{1380}{expect} \markbox{1381}{a} graded
	\markbox{1382}{endomorphism} \markbox{1383}{of} \markbox{m1384}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{1385}{to} be
	\markbox{1386}{trivial} \markbox{1387}{merely} \markbox{1388}{because} \markbox{1389}{it} \markbox{1390}{vanishes} \markbox{1391}{in} \markbox{1392}{degree} \markbox{1393}{two.} \markbox{1394}{Indeed,} \markbox{1395}{for} \markbox{1396}{any} \markbox{1397}{choice} of
	\markbox{1398}{elements} \markbox{m1399}{$P_i \in H^{2i-m}(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$},
	\markbox{m1400}{$i=1,\dots,k$}, \markbox{1401}{one} \markbox{1402}{obtains} \markbox{1403}{a} \markbox{1404}{well-defined} \markbox{1405}{graded} \markbox{1406}{endomorphism} \markbox{m1407}{$\phi$} of
	\markbox{m1408}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{1409}{by} setting
	\markbox{m1410}{$\phi(c_i) = uP_i$} \markbox{1411}{for} \markbox{m1412}{$i=1,\dots,k$} \markbox{1413}{and} \markbox{m1414}{$\phi(u)=u$}, \markbox{1415}{when} \markbox{1416}{the} \markbox{1417}{hypothesis} \markbox{1418}{(GH)} \markbox{1419}{holds.} \markbox{1420}{Hence,} \markbox{1421}{even} \markbox{1422}{in} \markbox{1423}{the} \markbox{1424}{case} \markbox{m1425}{$P_1 = 0$}, \markbox{1426}{a} \markbox{1427}{large} \markbox{1428}{family} \markbox{1429}{of} \markbox{1430}{nontrivial} \markbox{1431}{graded} \markbox{1432}{endomorphisms} \markbox{1433}{still} \markbox{1434}{exists.} \markbox{1435}{See} \markbox{1436}{Proposition} \ref{main thm 2}.
	\markbox{1437}{We} \markbox{1438}{show} \markbox{1439}{that} \markbox{1440}{if} \markbox{1441}{a} \markbox{1442}{map} \markbox{1443}{on} \markbox{m1444}{$\mathbb S^{m}\times \mathbb C G_{n,k}$} \markbox{1445}{stabilizes} \markbox{1446}{a} \markbox{1447}{Grassmannian} \markbox{1448}{factor,} \markbox{1449}{then} \markbox{1450}{the} \markbox{1451}{induced} \markbox{1452}{cohomology} \markbox{1453}{endomorphism} \markbox{1454}{stabilizes} \markbox{1455}{the} \markbox{1456}{subalgebra} \markbox{m1457}{$H^*(\mathbb S^{m};\mathbb Q)$}. \markbox{1458}{See} \thmref{ind from top}.
	
	%(see Theorem \ref{ind from top}). 
	%\textcolor{gray}{If the map on $\mathbb S^m \times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$ has nonzero  Brouwer degree, the induced map in cohomology splits as a tensor product of two maps: one acting on the cohomology of the sphere and the other on the cohomology of the Grassmannian. (see  \ref{}).}
	
	\iffalse
	Using \markbox{1459}{the} \markbox{1460}{study} \markbox{1461}{of} \markbox{m1462}{$\mathrm{End}(H^*(\mathbb S^{m}\times \mathbb C G_{n,k};\mathbb Q))$}, \markbox{1463}{we} \markbox{1464}{obtain} \markbox{1465}{several} \markbox{1466}{coincidence-theoretic} \markbox{1467}{consequences.} \markbox{1468}{The} \markbox{1469}{next} \markbox{1470}{result} \markbox{1471}{provides} \markbox{1472}{a} \markbox{1473}{necessary} \markbox{1474}{criterion} \markbox{1475}{for} \markbox{1476}{determining} \markbox{1477}{when} \markbox{1478}{the} \markbox{1479}{pair} \markbox{m1480}{$\big(P(S,\alpha,X,\sigma),g\big)$} \markbox{1481}{have} \markbox{1482}{the} \markbox{1483}{coincidence} \markbox{1484}{property,} \markbox{1485}{for} \markbox{1486}{certain} \markbox{1487}{maps} \markbox{m1488}{$g$} \markbox{1489}{on} \markbox{1490}{the} \markbox{1491}{GDS,} \markbox{1492}{expressed} \markbox{1493}{in} \markbox{1494}{terms} \markbox{1495}{of} \markbox{1496}{its} \markbox{1497}{fibre} \markbox{m1498}{$X$} \markbox{1499}{and} \markbox{1500}{its} \markbox{1501}{base} \markbox{m1502}{$Y:=S/\!\sim_{\alpha}$}.
	
	
	
	
	\begin{proposition}
		\markbox{1503}{For}  \markbox{1504}{a} \markbox{1505}{continuous} \markbox{1506}{map} \markbox{m1507}{$g$} \markbox{1508}{on} \markbox{1509}{the} \markbox{1510}{generalized} \markbox{1511}{Dold} \markbox{1512}{space} \markbox{m1513}{$P(S,\alpha, X,\sigma)$}, \markbox{1514}{the} \markbox{1515}{pair} \markbox{m1516}{$\big(P(S,\alpha,X,\sigma),g\big)$} \markbox{1517}{does} \markbox{1518}{not} \markbox{1519}{have} \markbox{1520}{the} \markbox{1521}{CP} \markbox{1522}{if} \markbox{1523}{one} \markbox{1524}{of} \markbox{1525}{the} \markbox{1526}{following} hold:
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item {} The \markbox{1527}{pair} \markbox{m1528}{$\big(Y,p \circ g \circ s\big)$} \markbox{1529}{does} \markbox{1530}{not} \markbox{1531}{have} \markbox{1532}{the} \markbox{1533}{CP,} 
			\markbox{1534}{where} \markbox{m1535}{$s$} \markbox{1536}{denotes} \markbox{1537}{a} \markbox{1538}{global} \markbox{1539}{section} \markbox{1540}{of} \markbox{1541}{the} \markbox{m1542}{$X$}-bundle  
			\markbox{m1543}{$p: P(S, X) \to Y$}, \markbox{1544}{and} \markbox{m1545}{$g$} \markbox{1546}{is} \markbox{1547}{a} \markbox{1548}{fiber} \markbox{1549}{bundle} map.
			\item  {} There \markbox{1550}{exists} \markbox{1551}{a} \markbox{m1552}{$\sigma$}-equivariant \markbox{1553}{map} \markbox{m1554}{$f$}  \markbox{1555}{on} \markbox{m1556}{$X$} \markbox{1557}{and} \markbox{1558}{a}  \markbox{m1559}{$\alpha \times \sigma$}-equivariant \markbox{1560}{map} \markbox{m1561}{$\tilde g$} \markbox{1562}{on} \markbox{m1563}{$S\times X$} \markbox{1564}{inducing} \markbox{m1565}{$g$} \markbox{1566}{such} \markbox{1567}{that} \markbox{m1568}{$\mathrm{id}_S \times f$} \markbox{1569}{coincides} \markbox{1570}{with} \markbox{1571}{neither} \markbox{m1572}{$\tilde{g}$} \markbox{1573}{nor} \markbox{m1574}{$(\alpha \times \sigma) \circ \tilde{g}$}.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proposition}
	\fi
	
	Using \markbox{1575}{the} \markbox{1576}{study} \markbox{1577}{of} \markbox{m1578}{$\mathrm{End}\bigl(H^*(\mathbb S^{m}\times \mathbb C G_{n,k};\mathbb Q)\bigr),$}
	\markbox{1579}{we} \markbox{1580}{obtain} \markbox{1581}{several} \markbox{1582}{coincidence-theoretic} \markbox{1583}{consequences.} \markbox{1584}{First,} \markbox{1585}{we} \markbox{1586}{extend} Theorem~2 \markbox{1587}{of} \cite{glover-homer} \markbox{1588}{to} \markbox{1589}{the} \markbox{1590}{setting} \markbox{1591}{of} \markbox{1592}{coincidence} \markbox{1593}{theory} \markbox{1594}{and} \markbox{1595}{show} \markbox{1596}{that} \markbox{1597}{for} \markbox{1598}{a} \markbox{1599}{continuous} \markbox{1600}{self-map} \markbox{m1601}{$g$} \markbox{1602}{with} \markbox{1603}{nonzero} \markbox{1604}{Brouwer} \markbox{1605}{degree} \markbox{1606}{on} \markbox{m1607}{$\mathbb C G_{n,k}$} \markbox{1608}{with} \markbox{m1609}{$k(n-k)$} \markbox{1610}{even,} \markbox{1611}{any} \markbox{1612}{continuous} \markbox{1613}{map} \markbox{m1614}{$f$} \markbox{1615}{on} \markbox{m1616}{$\mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{1617}{has} \markbox{1618}{a} \markbox{1619}{coincidence} \markbox{1620}{with} \markbox{m1621}{$g$}. \markbox{1622}{See} Proposition~\ref{CP of CGnk}.
	
	\markbox{1623}{We} \markbox{1624}{then} \markbox{1625}{investigate} \markbox{1626}{the} \markbox{1627}{coincidence} \markbox{1628}{behaviour} \markbox{1629}{of} \markbox{1630}{the} \markbox{1631}{generalized} \markbox{1632}{Dold} \markbox{1633}{spaces} \markbox{m1634}{$P(m,n,k)$}. \markbox{1635}{For} \markbox{1636}{any} \markbox{1637}{continuous} \markbox{1638}{self-map} \markbox{m1639}{$g$} \markbox{1640}{with} \markbox{1641}{nonzero} \markbox{1642}{Brouwer} \markbox{1643}{degree} \markbox{1644}{on} \markbox{m1645}{$P(m,n,k)$}  \markbox{1646}{with} \markbox{m1647}{$k(n-k)$} \markbox{1648}{even} \markbox{1649}{and} \markbox{m1650}{$m$} \markbox{1651}{even,} \markbox{1652}{every} \markbox{1653}{map} \markbox{m1654}{$f$} \markbox{1655}{satisfying} \markbox{m1656}{$\tilde f^{*}(c_1)\neq a u$} \markbox{1657}{for} \markbox{1658}{any} \markbox{m1659}{$a\in\mathbb Q$} \markbox{1660}{has} \markbox{1661}{a} \markbox{1662}{coincidence} \markbox{1663}{with} \markbox{m1664}{$g$}; \markbox{1665}{when} \markbox{m1666}{$m$} \markbox{1667}{is} \markbox{1668}{odd,} \markbox{1669}{one} \markbox{1670}{additionally} \markbox{1671}{requires} \markbox{m1672}{$\tilde f^{*}(u)\neq -\tilde g^{*}(u)$}. \markbox{1673}{See} Theorem~\ref{coincidence thm}.
	
	\markbox{1674}{Under} \markbox{1675}{hypothesis} \markbox{1676}{(GH),} \markbox{1677}{if} \markbox{m1678}{$g$} \markbox{1679}{is} \markbox{1680}{a} \markbox{1681}{homotopy} \markbox{1682}{equivalence} \markbox{1683}{on} \markbox{m1684}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{1685}{with} \markbox{m1686}{$k(n-k)$} \markbox{1687}{even,} \markbox{1688}{then} \markbox{m1689}{$g$} \markbox{1690}{has} \markbox{1691}{a} \markbox{1692}{coincidence} \markbox{1693}{with} \markbox{1694}{any} \markbox{1695}{map} \markbox{m1696}{$f$} \markbox{1697}{on} \markbox{m1698}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{1699}{such} \markbox{1700}{that:} \\ 
	\markbox{1701}{--} \markbox{1702}{when} \markbox{m1703}{$m$} \markbox{1704}{is} \markbox{1705}{even,}  \markbox{m1706}{$\tilde f^{*}(c_1)=a u, a\in \mathbb Q$} \markbox{1707}{implies} \markbox{m1708}{$\tilde f^{*}(u)=b u$} \markbox{1709}{for} \markbox{1710}{some} \markbox{m1711}{$b\in\mathbb Q$};  \\
	\markbox{1712}{--} \markbox{1713}{when} \markbox{m1714}{$m$} \markbox{1715}{is} \markbox{1716}{odd,}  \markbox{m1717}{$\tilde f^{*}(u)\neq -\tilde g^{*}(u)$} \markbox{1718}{holds.} \markbox{1719}{See} Theorem~\ref{coincidence thm under hom}.  \\
	\markbox{1720}{Moreover,} \markbox{1721}{if} \markbox{m1722}{$m>2k$}, \markbox{1723}{no} \markbox{1724}{additional} \markbox{1725}{assumptions} \markbox{1726}{on} \markbox{m1727}{$f$} \markbox{1728}{are} needed.
	
	
	
	
	\markbox{1729}{The} \markbox{1730}{paper} \markbox{1731}{is} \markbox{1732}{organized} \markbox{1733}{as} \markbox{1734}{follows:} \markbox{1735}{In} Section~2 \markbox{1736}{we} \markbox{1737}{develop} \markbox{1738}{the} \markbox{1739}{necessary} \markbox{1740}{background} \markbox{1741}{and} \markbox{1742}{recall} \markbox{1743}{some} \markbox{1744}{relevant} \markbox{1745}{results.} Section~3 \markbox{1746}{is} \markbox{1747}{devoted} \markbox{1748}{to} \markbox{1749}{the} \markbox{1750}{study} \markbox{1751}{of} \markbox{1752}{graded} \markbox{1753}{endomorphisms} \markbox{1754}{of} \markbox{1755}{the} \markbox{1756}{rational} \markbox{1757}{cohomology} \markbox{1758}{algebra} \markbox{1759}{of} \markbox{m1760}{$\mathbb S^{m}\times \mathbb C G_{n,k}$}, \markbox{1761}{from} \markbox{1762}{which} \markbox{1763}{we} \markbox{1764}{extract} \markbox{1765}{several} \markbox{1766}{consequences.} \markbox{1767}{These} \markbox{1768}{are} \markbox{1769}{applied} \markbox{1770}{in} Section~4 \markbox{1771}{to} \markbox{1772}{obtain} \markbox{1773}{the} \markbox{1774}{coincidence-theoretic} results.\fi
	
	
	
	
	
	
	%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
	\section{Preliminaries}  \label{section 2}
	
	\markbox{1775}{In} \markbox{1776}{this} \markbox{1777}{section,} \markbox{1778}{we} \markbox{1779}{discuss} \markbox{1780}{some} \markbox{1781}{preliminaries} \markbox{1782}{and} \markbox{1783}{recall} \markbox{1784}{some} \markbox{1785}{results} \markbox{1786}{that} \markbox{1787}{will} \markbox{1788}{be} \markbox{1789}{required} \markbox{1790}{to} \markbox{1791}{proceed} \markbox{1792}{with} \markbox{1793}{our} study.
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Cohomology of complex Grassmannians}
	
	
	\markbox{1794}{Let} \markbox{m1795}{$\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{1796}{denote} \markbox{1797}{the} \markbox{1798}{complex} \markbox{1799}{Grassmannian} \markbox{1800}{consisting} \markbox{1801}{of} \markbox{1802}{complex} \markbox{m1803}{$k$}-planes \markbox{1804}{in} \markbox{m1805}{$\mathbb{C}^n$}. 
	%As a homogeneous space, it is diffeomorphic to $U(n)/U(k) \times U(n-k)$, where $U(r)$ denotes the group of unitary matrices of order $r$. 
	Let \markbox{m1806}{$\gamma_{n,k}$} \markbox{1807}{and} \markbox{m1808}{$\beta_{n,k}$} \markbox{1809}{denote} \markbox{1810}{the} \markbox{1811}{canonical} \markbox{1812}{complex} \markbox{m1813}{$k$}-plane \markbox{1814}{and} \markbox{m1815}{$(n-k)$}-plane \markbox{1816}{bundles,} \markbox{1817}{respectively,} \markbox{1818}{over} \markbox{m1819}{$\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$}.
	\markbox{1820}{Let} \markbox{1821}{the} \markbox{1822}{total} \markbox{1823}{Chern} \markbox{1824}{classes} \markbox{1825}{of} \markbox{1826}{the} \markbox{1827}{vector} \markbox{1828}{bundles} \markbox{m1829}{$\gamma_{n,k}$} \markbox{1830}{and} \markbox{m1831}{$\beta_{n,k}$} \markbox{1832}{be} \markbox{1833}{denoted} \markbox{1834}{by} \markbox{m1835}{$c(\gamma_{n,k}) = c$} \markbox{1836}{and} \markbox{m1837}{$c(\beta_{n,k}) = \bar{c}$}, \markbox{1838}{respectively.} Thus,
	$$c = 1 + c_1 + c_2 + \cdots + c_k, \quad \bar{c} = 1 + \bar{c}_1 + \bar{c}_2 + \cdots + \bar{c}_{n-k},$$
	\markbox{1839}{where} \markbox{m1840}{$c_i$} \markbox{1841}{and} \markbox{m1842}{$\bar{c}_i$} \markbox{1843}{denote} \markbox{1844}{the} \markbox{m1845}{$i$}-th \markbox{1846}{Chern} \markbox{1847}{classes} \markbox{1848}{of} \markbox{m1849}{$\gamma_{n,k}$} \markbox{1850}{and} \markbox{m1851}{$\beta_{n,k}$}, respectively.
	\markbox{1852}{Since} \markbox{m1853}{$\gamma_{n,k} \oplus \beta_{n,k} \cong \varepsilon_{\mathbb{C}}^n$}, \markbox{1854}{it} \markbox{1855}{follows} \markbox{1856}{that}  \markbox{m1857}{$c \cdot \bar{c} = 1$}.
	\markbox{1858}{The}  \markbox{1859}{cohomology} \markbox{1860}{ring} \markbox{1861}{of} \markbox{1862}{the} \markbox{1863}{complex} \markbox{1864}{Grassmannian} \markbox{1865}{is} \markbox{1866}{well} \markbox{1867}{known} \markbox{1868}{and} \markbox{1869}{given} \markbox{1870}{by}  
	$$
	H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}:=H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb{Q}) \cong \mathbb{Q}[c_1, c_2, \dots, c_k, \bar{c}_1, \bar{c}_2, \dots, \bar{c}_{n-k}]/\langle h_r: 1\leq r\leq n\rangle,$$  
	\markbox{1871}{where}  \markbox{1872}{the} \markbox{1873}{relations} \markbox{m1874}{$h_r$} \markbox{1875}{for} \markbox{m1876}{$r = 1, 2, \dots, n$} \markbox{1877}{are} \markbox{1878}{induced} \markbox{1879}{from} \markbox{1880}{the} \markbox{1881}{homogeneous} \markbox{1882}{parts} \markbox{1883}{of} \markbox{1884}{the} \markbox{1885}{equation} \markbox{m1886}{$c\cdot \bar c=1$} \markbox{1887}{and} \markbox{1888}{given} \markbox{1889}{by}  
	\[
	h_r := \sum_{i+j=r} c_i \bar{c}_j.
	\]  
	\markbox{1890}{Using} \markbox{1891}{the} \markbox{1892}{relations} \markbox{m1893}{$h_r, r=1,2,...,n-k$}, \markbox{1894}{the} \markbox{1895}{generators} \markbox{m1896}{$\bar{c}_i$} \markbox{1897}{for} \markbox{m1898}{$i = 1, 2, \dots, n-k$} \markbox{1899}{can} \markbox{1900}{be} \markbox{1901}{expressed} \markbox{1902}{inductively} \markbox{1903}{in} \markbox{1904}{terms} \markbox{1905}{of} \markbox{m1906}{$c_i$} \markbox{1907}{for} \markbox{m1908}{$i = 1, 2, \dots, k$}.  \markbox{1909}{Consequently,} \markbox{1910}{the} \markbox{1911}{relations} \markbox{m1912}{$h_r$} \markbox{1913}{for} \markbox{m1914}{$r = n-k+1, \dots, n$} \markbox{1915}{become} \markbox{1916}{homogeneous} \markbox{1917}{polynomials} \markbox{1918}{in} \markbox{m1919}{$c_i$} \markbox{1920}{of} \markbox{1921}{degree} \markbox{m1922}{$2r$}, \markbox{1923}{where} \markbox{1924}{the} \markbox{1925}{degree} \markbox{1926}{of} \markbox{1927}{each} \markbox{m1928}{$c_i$} \markbox{1929}{is} \markbox{m1930}{$2i$}. \markbox{1931}{Then} \markbox{1932}{the} \markbox{1933}{cohomology} \markbox{1934}{ring} \markbox{m1935}{$H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{1936}{can} \markbox{1937}{be} \markbox{1938}{rewritten} \markbox{1939}{as}  
	\begin{equation}\label{cohomo of grass}
		\mathbb{Q}[c_1, c_2, \dots, c_k]/\langle h_{n-k+1}, h_{n-k+2}, \dots, h_n \rangle.
	\end{equation}
	\markbox{1940}{Since} \markbox{1941}{there} \markbox{1942}{are} \markbox{1943}{no} \markbox{1944}{relations} \markbox{1945}{among} \markbox{1946}{the} \markbox{1947}{generators} \markbox{m1948}{$c_i$} \markbox{1949}{for} \markbox{m1950}{$i = 1, 2, \dots, k$} \markbox{1951}{up} \markbox{1952}{to} \markbox{1953}{degree} \markbox{m1954}{$2(n-k)$}, \markbox{1955}{the} \markbox{1956}{set} \markbox{1957}{of} \markbox{1958}{all} \markbox{1959}{monomials} \markbox{1960}{of} \markbox{1961}{degree} \markbox{m1962}{$2r$} \markbox{1963}{in} \markbox{1964}{terms} \markbox{1965}{of} \markbox{m1966}{$c_1, c_2, \ldots, c_k$} \markbox{1967}{forms} \markbox{1968}{a} \markbox{m1969}{$\mathbb{Q}$}-basis \markbox{1970}{of} \markbox{m1971}{$H^{2r}(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{1972}{for} \markbox{m1973}{$r \leq n-k$}.
	
	\markbox{1974}{From} \markbox{1975}{now} \markbox{1976}{on,} \markbox{1977}{we} \markbox{1978}{denote} \markbox{1979}{the} \markbox{1980}{indexing} \markbox{1981}{set} \markbox{m1982}{$\{1,2,\dots, k\}$} \markbox{1983}{by} \markbox{m1984}{$I$}.
	\begin{remark}
		\markbox{1985}{We} \markbox{1986}{can} \markbox{1987}{assume}  \markbox{m1988}{$k\leq n-k$} \markbox{1989}{for}  \markbox{m1990}{$\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{1991}{as} \markbox{m1992}{$\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{1993}{is} \markbox{1994}{homeomorphic} \markbox{1995}{to} \markbox{m1996}{$\mathbb{C}G_{n,n-k}$} \markbox{1997}{by} \markbox{1998}{using} \markbox{1999}{orthogonal} complementation.
	\end{remark}
	\markbox{2000}{The} \markbox{2001}{complex} \markbox{2002}{Grassmannian} \markbox{m2003}{$\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{2004}{is} \markbox{2005}{a} \markbox{2006}{homogeneous} \markbox{2007}{space} \markbox{2008}{and} \markbox{2009}{can} \markbox{2010}{be} \markbox{2011}{represented} \markbox{2012}{as} \markbox{2013}{the} \markbox{2014}{quotient} \markbox{2015}{of} \markbox{2016}{the} \markbox{2017}{unitary} \markbox{2018}{group} \markbox{m2019}{$U(n)$} \markbox{2020}{by} \markbox{2021}{the} \markbox{2022}{stabilizer} \markbox{2023}{subgroup} \markbox{m2024}{$U(k)\times U(n-k)$} \markbox{2025}{that} \markbox{2026}{is} 
	\begin{equation}\label{cgn as hom}
		\mathbb{C}G_{n,k} = U(n)/ (U(k)\times U(n-k)). 
	\end{equation} \markbox{2027}{Now} \markbox{2028}{we} \markbox{2029}{recall} \markbox{2030}{a} \markbox{2031}{result} \markbox{2032}{given} \markbox{2033}{in} \cite{shiga-tezuka}.    
	\begin{theorem}[\cite{shiga-tezuka}, \markbox{2034}{Theorem} \markbox{m2035}{\(A^{'}\)}]\label{Tezuka}
		\markbox{2036}{Let} \markbox{m2037}{$D_i(H^*(G/H;\mathbb{Q}))$} \markbox{2038}{be} \markbox{2039}{the} \markbox{m2040}{$\mathbb{Q}$}-vector \markbox{2041}{space} \markbox{2042}{of} \markbox{m2043}{$\mathbb{Q}$}-derivations \markbox{2044}{of} \markbox{m2045}{$H^*(G/H;\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{2046}{which} \markbox{2047}{decreases} \markbox{2048}{the} \markbox{2049}{degree} \markbox{2050}{by} \markbox{m2051}{$i>0$} \markbox{2052}{where} \markbox{m2053}{$G$} \markbox{2054}{is} \markbox{2055}{a} \markbox{2056}{connected,} \markbox{2057}{compact} \markbox{2058}{Lie} \markbox{2059}{group} \markbox{2060}{and} \markbox{m2061}{$H$} \markbox{2062}{is} \markbox{2063}{a} \markbox{2064}{closed} \markbox{2065}{subgroup} \markbox{2066}{of} \markbox{2067}{maximal} rank.
		%such that $\rank (H) = \rank (G)$.
		Then, \markbox{2068}{for} \markbox{2069}{all} \markbox{m2070}{$i$}, $$D_i(H^*(G/H;\mathbb{Q})) =0.$$  
	\end{theorem}
	\subsection{Graded endomorphisms on $\mathbf{H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}}$}
	\markbox{2071}{It} \markbox{2072}{was} \markbox{2073}{conjectured} \markbox{2074}{in} \cite{O} \markbox{2075}{that} \markbox{2076}{any} \markbox{2077}{graded} \markbox{2078}{endomorphism} \markbox{m2079}{$\phi$} \markbox{2080}{of} \markbox{2081}{the} \markbox{2082}{cohomology} \markbox{2083}{algebra} \markbox{m2084}{$H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{2085}{is} an\markbox{2086}{\textit{ Adams }}map \markbox{2087}{when} \markbox{m2088}{$k < n - k$}; \markbox{2089}{that} \markbox{2090}{is,} \markbox{2091}{there} \markbox{2092}{exists} \markbox{2093}{a} \markbox{2094}{rational} \markbox{m2095}{$\lambda$} \markbox{2096}{such} that
	\markbox{m2097}{$\phi(c_i) = \lambda^i c_i$}, \markbox{2098}{for} \markbox{2099}{all} \markbox{m2100}{$ i \in I.$} \markbox{2101}{Glover} \markbox{2102}{and} \markbox{2103}{Homer} \markbox{2104}{(see} \cite{glover-homer}) \markbox{2105}{and} \markbox{2106}{Hoffman} \markbox{2107}{(see} \cite{hoffman}) \markbox{2108}{proved} \markbox{2109}{the} \markbox{2110}{conjecture} \markbox{2111}{under} \markbox{2112}{the} \markbox{2113}{following} \markbox{2114}{hypothesis} respectively:
	\begin{align}
		\text{Either } k \leq 3 \text{ and } n > 2k \text{, or } k>3 \text{ and } n>2k^2 -1. \label{Homer}\\
		\text{ The graded endomorphism } \varphi  \text{ of } H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \text{ satisfies } \varphi(c_1) = \lambda c_1, \lambda\neq 0.  \label{Hoff}
	\end{align}
	%In this context, Glover and Homer \ref{Hoffman} (see \cite{glover-homer}) proved the following result.
	Let \markbox{2115}{us} \markbox{2116}{recall} \markbox{2117}{those} \markbox{2118}{results} \markbox{2119}{proved} \markbox{2120}{in} \cite{glover-homer, hoffman} \markbox{2121}{that} \markbox{2122}{will} \markbox{2123}{be} \markbox{2124}{used} \markbox{2125}{in} \markbox{2126}{the} \markbox{2127}{rest} \markbox{2128}{of} \markbox{2129}{this} \markbox{2130}{paper.}  
	\begin{theorem}[\cite{glover-homer}, \markbox{2131}{Theorem} \markbox{2132}{1,} \cite{hoffman}, \markbox{2133}{Theorem} 1.1]\label{hom and hof}
		\markbox{2134}{(i)} \markbox{2135}{Assume} \markbox{2136}{that} \markbox{2137}{the} \markbox{2138}{hypothesis} \eqref{Homer} \markbox{2139}{is} \markbox{2140}{satisfied.} \markbox{2141}{Then} \markbox{2142}{for} \markbox{2143}{every} \markbox{2144}{graded} \markbox{2145}{endomorphism} \markbox{m2146}{$\varphi$} \markbox{2147}{on} \markbox{m2148}{$ H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q})$}, \markbox{2149}{there} \markbox{2150}{exists} \markbox{2151}{a} \markbox{2152}{rational} \markbox{m2153}{$\lambda$} \markbox{2154}{such} that
		\[\varphi(c_i) = \lambda^i c_i,  \quad \forall i \in I.\]
		%where $c_i$ denotes the $i$-th Chern class of the canonical complex $k$-plane bundle $\gamma_{n,k}$ over the complex Grassmannian $\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$.
		(ii) \markbox{2155}{Assume} \markbox{2156}{that} \markbox{2157}{the} \markbox{2158}{hypothesis} \eqref{Hoff} \markbox{2159}{is} \markbox{2160}{satisfied.} \markbox{2161}{Then,} \markbox{2162}{we} have
		$$\varphi(c_i) = \begin{cases}
			\lambda^i c_i,   \forall i \in I& \text{ if } k<n-k,\\
			\lambda^i c_i,  \forall i \in I \quad \text{ or } \quad(-\lambda)^i (c^{-1})_i,    \forall i \in I & \text{ if } k= n-k,
		\end{cases}$$
		\markbox{2163}{where} \markbox{m2164}{$ (c^{-1})_i $} \markbox{2165}{is} \markbox{2166}{the} \markbox{m2167}{$ 2i $}-dimensional \markbox{2168}{part} \markbox{2169}{of} \markbox{2170}{the} \markbox{2171}{inverse} \markbox{2172}{of} \markbox{m2173}{$ c = 1 + c_1 + \cdots + c_k $} \markbox{2174}{in} \markbox{m2175}{$ H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}) $}.
	\end{theorem}
	\iffalse Hoffman \markbox{2176}{provided} \markbox{2177}{a} \markbox{2178}{classification} \markbox{2179}{of} \markbox{2180}{graded} \markbox{2181}{endomorphisms} \markbox{2182}{of} \markbox{m2183}{$H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{2184}{that} \markbox{2185}{are} \markbox{2186}{nonvanishing} \markbox{2187}{on} \markbox{m2188}{$H^2(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{2189}{(see} \cite{hoffman}). \markbox{2190}{We} \markbox{2191}{recall} \markbox{2192}{his} \markbox{2193}{result} \markbox{2194}{in} \markbox{2195}{the} \markbox{2196}{following} theorem.
	\begin{theorem}[]\label{hoffman}
		\markbox{2197}{Let} \markbox{m2198}{$ \varphi $} \markbox{2199}{be} \markbox{2200}{an} \markbox{2201}{endomorphism} \markbox{2202}{of} \markbox{m2203}{$ H^*(\mathbb CG_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}) $} \markbox{2204}{with} \markbox{m2205}{$ \varphi(c_1) = \lambda c_1 $}, \markbox{m2206}{$ \lambda\neq 0 $}. \markbox{2207}{Then} \markbox{2208}{if} \markbox{m2209}{$ k < n-k $},
		\[
		\varphi(c_i) = \lambda^i c_i, \quad 1 \le i \le k.
		\]
		
		\markbox{2210}{If} \markbox{m2211}{$ k = n $}, \markbox{2212}{there} \markbox{2213}{is} \markbox{2214}{the} \markbox{2215}{additional} possibility
		\[
		\varphi(c_i) = (-\lambda)^i (c^{-1})_i, \quad 1 \le i \le k,
		\]
		
		
	\end{theorem}\fi
	
	\subsection{Generalized Dold spaces}  \label{gen dold}
	\markbox{2216}{In} \cite{dold}, \markbox{2217}{the} \markbox{2218}{author} \markbox{2219}{introduced} \markbox{2220}{the} \markbox{2221}{notion} \markbox{2222}{of} \markbox{2223}{\textit{classical Dold manifolds}}  
	\markbox{m2224}{$P(m,n) := \mathbb{S}^m \times \mathbb{C}P^n / \!\! \sim$}  
	\markbox{2225}{where} \markbox{m2226}{$ (s, L) \sim (-s, \bar{L}) $}, \markbox{2227}{where} \markbox{2228}{the} \markbox{2229}{involution} \markbox{m2230}{$L\mapsto\bar L$} \markbox{2231}{on} \markbox{m2232}{$\mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{2233}{is} \markbox{2234}{induced} \markbox{2235}{from} \markbox{2236}{the} \markbox{2237}{standard} \markbox{2238}{conjugation} \markbox{2239}{on} \markbox{m2240}{$\mathbb C^n$}, \markbox{2241}{to} \markbox{2242}{construct} \markbox{2243}{generators} \markbox{2244}{in} \markbox{2245}{odd} \markbox{2246}{dimensions} \markbox{2247}{for} Ren{\'e} \markbox{2248}{Thom's} \markbox{2249}{unoriented} \markbox{2250}{cobordism} \markbox{2251}{ring.} %These spaces are of great interest, and many generalizations and studies have been done on them in the literature.
	
	\iffalse (Put \markbox{2252}{this} \markbox{2253}{in} \markbox{2254}{introduction)In} \cite{nath-sankaran}, \markbox{2255}{authors} \markbox{2256}{generalized} \markbox{2257}{the} \markbox{2258}{notion} \markbox{2259}{of} \markbox{2260}{Dold} \markbox{2261}{manifolds} \markbox{2262}{by} \markbox{2263}{replacing} \markbox{2264}{the} \markbox{2265}{complex} \markbox{2266}{projective} \markbox{2267}{space} \markbox{m2268}{$\mathbb{C}P^n$} \markbox{2269}{with} \markbox{2270}{an} \markbox{2271}{almost} \markbox{2272}{complex} \markbox{2273}{manifold} \markbox{m2274}{$X$} \markbox{2275}{equipped} \markbox{2276}{with} \markbox{2277}{a} \markbox{2278}{complex} \markbox{2279}{conjugation,} \markbox{2280}{i.e.,} \markbox{2281}{an} \markbox{2282}{involution} \markbox{m2283}{$\sigma: X \to X$} \markbox{2284}{with} \markbox{2285}{nonempty} \markbox{2286}{fixed-point} \markbox{2287}{set} \markbox{2288}{such} \markbox{2289}{that} \markbox{2290}{the} differential
	\markbox{m2291}{$d\sigma|_p: T_pX \to T_{\sigma(p)}X$}
	satisfies
	\markbox{m2292}{$J_{\sigma(p)} \circ d\sigma_p = -d\sigma_p \circ J_p,$}
	\markbox{2293}{where} \markbox{m2294}{$J$} \markbox{2295}{denotes} \markbox{2296}{the} \markbox{2297}{almost} \markbox{2298}{complex} \markbox{2299}{structure} \markbox{2300}{on} \markbox{m2301}{$X$}, \markbox{2302}{and} \markbox{2303}{called} \markbox{2304}{them} \markbox{2305}{\textit{generalized Dold manifolds}} \markbox{2306}{to} \markbox{2307}{investigate} \markbox{2308}{their} \markbox{2309}{manifold} \markbox{2310}{properties} \markbox{2311}{such} \markbox{2312}{as} \markbox{2313}{tangent} \markbox{2314}{bundles,} \markbox{2315}{Stiefel--Whitney} \markbox{2316}{classes,} \markbox{2317}{(stable)} \markbox{2318}{parallelizability,} \markbox{2319}{cobordism} \markbox{2320}{classes,} \markbox{2321}{and} \markbox{2322}{related} aspects.
	\fi
	
	In \cite{nath-sankaran, mandal-sankaran}, \markbox{2323}{the} \markbox{2324}{authors} \markbox{2325}{generalized} \markbox{2326}{the} \markbox{2327}{notion} \markbox{2328}{of} \markbox{2329}{classical} \markbox{2330}{Dold} \markbox{2331}{manifolds} \markbox{2332}{by} \markbox{2333}{replacing} \markbox{2334}{the} \markbox{2335}{sphere} \markbox{m2336}{$ \mathbb{S}^m $} \markbox{2337}{with} \markbox{2338}{an} \markbox{2339}{arbitrary} \markbox{2340}{topological} \markbox{2341}{space} \markbox{m2342}{$ S $} \markbox{2343}{equipped} \markbox{2344}{with} \markbox{2345}{a} \markbox{2346}{free} \markbox{2347}{involution} \markbox{m2348}{$ \alpha $}, \markbox{2349}{analogous} \markbox{2350}{to} \markbox{2351}{the} \markbox{2352}{antipodal} \markbox{2353}{map} \markbox{2354}{on} \markbox{m2355}{$ \mathbb{S}^m $}, \markbox{2356}{and} \markbox{m2357}{$ \mathbb CP^n $} \markbox{2358}{with} \markbox{2359}{an} \markbox{2360}{arbitrary} \markbox{2361}{topological} \markbox{2362}{space} \markbox{m2363}{$ X $} \markbox{2364}{with} \markbox{2365}{an} \markbox{2366}{involution} \markbox{m2367}{$ \sigma: X \to X $} \markbox{2368}{having} \markbox{2369}{a} \markbox{2370}{nonempty} \markbox{2371}{fixed-point} \markbox{2372}{set,} \markbox{2373}{analogously} \markbox{2374}{to} \markbox{2375}{complex} \markbox{2376}{conjugation} \markbox{2377}{on} \markbox{m2378}{$\mathbb CP^n$}. \markbox{2379}{Then} \markbox{2380}{the} \markbox{2381}{quotient} \markbox{2382}{space}  
	\begin{equation}\label{gen dold space}
		P(S, \alpha, X, \sigma) := S \times X / \!\! \sim, \quad \text{where } (s, x) \sim (\alpha(s), \sigma(x)), 
	\end{equation}  
	\markbox{2383}{is} \markbox{2384}{called} \markbox{2385}{\textit{generalized Dold space}} \markbox{2386}{(in} \markbox{2387}{short} \markbox{2388}{GDS),} \markbox{2389}{often} \markbox{2390}{denoted} \markbox{2391}{simply} \markbox{2392}{as} \markbox{m2393}{$ P(S, X) $}. \markbox{2394}{Moreover,} \markbox{2395}{the} \markbox{2396}{quotient} \markbox{2397}{map}  
	\markbox{m2398}{$ S \times X \to P(S,X) $}  
	\markbox{2399}{is} \markbox{2400}{a} \markbox{2401}{double} \markbox{2402}{covering} \markbox{2403}{map.} %The focus of their study were used to study cohomology and complex $K$-theory of various GDS.
	
	Let \markbox{2404}{us} \markbox{2405}{fix} \markbox{2406}{a} \markbox{2407}{notation} \markbox{m2408}{$ Y $} \markbox{2409}{for} \markbox{m2410}{$ S/\!\!\sim_{\alpha} $}, \markbox{2411}{where} \markbox{m2412}{$ s\sim_{\alpha} \alpha(s), \forall s\in S $}. \markbox{2413}{Then,} \markbox{2414}{a} \markbox{2415}{GDS} \markbox{m2416}{$ P(S,X) $} \markbox{2417}{is} \markbox{2418}{the} \markbox{2419}{total} \markbox{2420}{space} \markbox{2421}{of} \markbox{2422}{a} \markbox{2423}{fiber} \markbox{2424}{bundle}  
	\markbox{m2425}{$X\hookrightarrow P(S,X) \twoheadrightarrow Y $}, \markbox{2426}{where} \markbox{2427}{the} \markbox{2428}{fiber} \markbox{2429}{bundle} \markbox{2430}{projection} \markbox{2431}{is} \begin{equation}\label{proj}
		p: P(S,X) \twoheadrightarrow Y, \quad [s,x]\mapsto [s].
	\end{equation}  \markbox{2432}{Choosing} \markbox{2433}{a} \markbox{2434}{fixed-point} \markbox{2435}{of} \markbox{m2436}{$\sigma$}, \markbox{2437}{say} \markbox{m2438}{$x_0\in \text{Fix}(\sigma)\neq \emptyset$}, \markbox{2439}{we} \markbox{2440}{can} \markbox{2441}{construct} \markbox{2442}{a} \markbox{2443}{section} \markbox{2444}{of} \markbox{2445}{the} \markbox{2446}{fiber} \markbox{2447}{bundle} \begin{equation}\label{sectio}
		s: Y \hookrightarrow P(S,X), \quad [s]\mapsto [s,x_0].
	\end{equation}    
	\markbox{2448}{In} \markbox{2449}{fact,} \markbox{2450}{we} \markbox{2451}{have} \markbox{2452}{an} \markbox{2453}{embedding}  
	\markbox{m2454}{$Y\times \text{Fix}(\sigma)\hookrightarrow P(S,X),$}  
	\markbox{2455}{where} \markbox{m2456}{$ \text{Fix}(\sigma) \subseteq X $} \markbox{2457}{has} \markbox{2458}{the} \markbox{2459}{subspace} \markbox{2460}{topology} \markbox{2461}{induced} \markbox{2462}{from} \markbox{m2463}{$ X $}.
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Rational cohomology of $\mathbf{P(\mathbb S^m,\mathbb CG_{n,k})}$} \label{gds}
	%The rational cohomology ring of \textit{generalized Dold space} $ P(\mathbb{S}^m, \mathbb{C}G(\nu)) $, which are fibered by a partial complex flag manifold $ \mathbb{C}G(\nu) $ of type $ \nu = (\nu_1 \leq \nu_2 \leq \dots \leq \nu_s) $ over a real projective space $ \mathbb{R}P^m $, is computed in \cite{mandal-sankaran2}. In particular, and we recall some relevant facts here.
	
	
	The \markbox{2464}{GDS} \markbox{m2465}{$P(\mathbb S^m,\mathbb CG_{n,k})$} \markbox{2466}{is} \markbox{2467}{defined} as
	\[
	\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}/\!\!\sim, \text { where } (s,L)\sim (-s,\bar L),
	\]
	\markbox{2468}{for} \markbox{2469}{which,} \markbox{m2470}{$\mathbb S^m$} \markbox{2471}{is} \markbox{2472}{equipped} \markbox{2473}{with} \markbox{2474}{the} \markbox{2475}{free} \markbox{2476}{action} \markbox{2477}{generated} \markbox{2478}{by} \markbox{2479}{the} \markbox{2480}{antipodal} \markbox{2481}{map} \markbox{m2482}{$\alpha$} \markbox{2483}{and} \markbox{2484}{the} \markbox{2485}{involution} \markbox{m2486}{$\sigma: L \mapsto \bar L$} \markbox{2487}{on} \markbox{m2488}{$\mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{2489}{is} \markbox{2490}{induced} \markbox{2491}{from} \markbox{2492}{the} \markbox{2493}{standard} \markbox{2494}{complex} \markbox{2495}{conjugation} \markbox{2496}{on} \markbox{m2497}{$\mathbb C^n.$} \markbox{2498}{We} \markbox{2499}{denote} \markbox{m2500}{$P(\mathbb S^m,\mathbb CG_{n,k})$} \markbox{2501}{simply} \markbox{2502}{by} \markbox{m2503}{$P(m,n,k).$}
	\markbox{2504}{By} \markbox{2505}{the} K\"unneth \markbox{2506}{formula,} \markbox{2507}{we} have
	\begin{equation}\label{Cohomology of H_times}
		H_{\times}^* := H^*(\mathbb{S}^m \times \mathbb{CG}_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}) \cong H^*(\mathbb{S}^m; \mathbb{Q}) \otimes H^*(\mathbb{CG}_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}) \cong \frac{\mathbb{Q}[u, c_1, \dots, c_k]}{\langle u^2, h_{n-k+1}, \dots, h_n \rangle}
	\end{equation}
	\markbox{2508}{where} \markbox{m2509}{$u \in H^m(\mathbb S^m; \mathbb Q)$} \markbox{2510}{denotes} \markbox{2511}{the} \markbox{2512}{generator} \markbox{2513}{corresponding} \markbox{2514}{to} \markbox{2515}{the} \markbox{2516}{fundamental} \markbox{2517}{class} \markbox{2518}{of} \markbox{m2519}{$\mathbb S^m$}. \markbox{2520}{Note} \markbox{2521}{that} \begin{equation}\label{H in terms of u}
		H^*_{\times} \cong H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}[u]/\langle u^2 \rangle \cong H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \oplus u H^*_{\mathbb{C}G},
	\end{equation} \markbox{2522}{where} \markbox{2523}{the} \markbox{2524}{latter} \markbox{2525}{isomorphism} \markbox{2526}{is} \markbox{2527}{a} \markbox{m2528}{$\mathbb Q$}-module \markbox{2529}{isomorphism.} \markbox{2530}{We} \markbox{2531}{have} \markbox{2532}{that} \markbox{m2533}{$H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{2534}{is} \markbox{2535}{a} \markbox{2536}{subring} \markbox{2537}{of} \markbox{m2538}{$H^*_\times$}.
	%For simplicity, denote $H^*(\mathbb{S}^m \times \mathbb{CG}_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}) $ by $H_{\times}^*$
	The \markbox{2539}{product} \markbox{2540}{involution} \markbox{m2541}{$\theta:= \alpha\times\sigma$} \markbox{2542}{on} \markbox{m2543}{$\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{2544}{induces} \markbox{2545}{an} \markbox{2546}{involution} \markbox{m2547}{$\theta^*$} \markbox{2548}{on} \markbox{m2549}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{2550}{given} by
	\begin{equation}\label{defn of theta*}
		\theta^*(c_i) = (-1)^i c_i,i\in I, \quad \theta^*(u) =  
		\begin{cases}  
			u, & \text{if } m \text{ is odd}, \\  
			-u, & \text{if } m \text{ is even}.  
		\end{cases}  
	\end{equation}
	%where $ H^*(\mathbb{S}^m; \mathbb{Q}) \cong \mathbb{Q}[u]/\langle u^2 \rangle $.
	%The induced involution $\theta^*$ is given by
	%t is proved in \cite{mandal-sankaran2} that $ H^*(P(m,n,k); \mathbb{Q}) $ is isomorphic to the fixed subring $ \text{Fix}(H^*(\theta; \mathbb{Q})) $ under $ \theta^* $ of $ H^*(\mathbb{S}^m \times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}) $ (Proposition 3.13 of \cite{mandal-sankaran2}). We recall the result below.
	The \markbox{2551}{cohomology} \markbox{2552}{ring} \markbox{m2553}{$ H^*(P(m, n,k);\mathbb Q) $} \markbox{2554}{was} \markbox{2555}{computed} \markbox{2556}{in} \cite{mandal-sankaran2} \markbox{2557}{and} \markbox{2558}{the} \markbox{2559}{following} \markbox{2560}{result} \markbox{2561}{was} proved.
	\begin{theorem}[{\cite[Theorem 3.13]{mandal-sankaran2}}]\label{cohomology of P(m,n,k)}
		\markbox{2562}{The} \markbox{2563}{cohomology} \markbox{2564}{algebra} \markbox{m2565}{\( H^*(P(m,n,k); \mathbb{Q}) \)} \markbox{2566}{is} \markbox{2567}{isomorphic} \markbox{2568}{to} \markbox{2569}{the} subalgebra
		\markbox{m2570}{$\mathrm{Fix}(\theta^*) \subseteq H^*(\mathbb{S}^m \times \mathbb{CG}_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}),$}
		\markbox{2571}{generated} \markbox{2572}{by} \markbox{2573}{the} \markbox{2574}{following} elements:
		\begin{align*}
			u \, c_{2p-1},\quad c_{2j},\quad c_{2p-1} \, c_{2q-1},\; \forall 2p-1, 2q-1, 2j \in I, \text{ if } m \text{ is even};\\
			u,\quad c_{2j},\quad c_{2p-1} \, c_{2q-1},\; \forall 2p-1, 2q-1, 2j \in I, \text{ if } m \text{ is odd}.
		\end{align*}
	\end{theorem}
	\markbox{2575}{A} \markbox{2576}{description} \markbox{2577}{of} \markbox{2578}{the} \markbox{2579}{cohomology} \markbox{2580}{algebra} \markbox{m2581}{$ H^*(P(m,n,k); \mathbb{Q}) $}, \markbox{2582}{as} \markbox{2583}{a} \markbox{2584}{quotient} \markbox{2585}{of} \markbox{2586}{a} \markbox{2587}{polynomial} \markbox{2588}{algebra,} \markbox{2589}{can} \markbox{2590}{be} \markbox{2591}{deduced} \markbox{2592}{as} \markbox{2593}{a} \markbox{2594}{particular} \markbox{2595}{case} \markbox{2596}{in} \markbox{2597}{Theorem} \markbox{2598}{3.14} \markbox{2599}{of} \cite{mandal-sankaran2}.
	%Since the description of the cohomology  algebra $H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb Q)$ in abstarct variables, is quite complicated in notations, instead we shall present the $\fix (H^*_\times)$ as $\mathcal R/$
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%5%%%%%%
	
	\section{Graded endomorphisms of $H^*(\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$} \label{section 3}
	
	\markbox{2600}{In} \markbox{2601}{this} \markbox{2602}{section,} \markbox{2603}{we} \markbox{2604}{classify} \markbox{2605}{graded} \markbox{2606}{endomorphisms} \markbox{2607}{of} \markbox{2608}{the} \markbox{2609}{rational} \markbox{2610}{cohomology} \markbox{2611}{algebra} \markbox{m2612}{$ H^*(\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}) $} \markbox{2613}{whose} \markbox{2614}{images} \markbox{2615}{are} \markbox{2616}{nonzero} \markbox{2617}{in} \markbox{m2618}{$H^2(\mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)$}. \markbox{2619}{Our} \markbox{2620}{approach} \markbox{2621}{relies} \markbox{2622}{on} \markbox{2623}{the} \markbox{2624}{study} \markbox{2625}{of} \markbox{2626}{graded} \markbox{2627}{endomorphisms} \markbox{2628}{of} \markbox{m2629}{$ H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q}) $} \markbox{2630}{from} \cite{glover-homer} \markbox{2631}{and} \cite{hoffman}. \markbox{2632}{Assume} \markbox{m2633}{$m>0$} \markbox{2634}{for} \markbox{2635}{the} \markbox{2636}{rest} \markbox{2637}{of} \markbox{2638}{this} paper.
	\subsection{} \markbox{2639}{The} \markbox{2640}{cohomology} \markbox{2641}{ring} \markbox{2642}{of} \markbox{2643}{the} \markbox{2644}{complex} \markbox{2645}{Grassmannian} \markbox{m2646}{$ \mathbb{C}G_{n,k} $} \markbox{2647}{is} \markbox{2648}{generated} \markbox{2649}{by} \markbox{2650}{the} \markbox{2651}{Chern} \markbox{2652}{classes} \markbox{m2653}{$c_i,\forall i \in I $} \markbox{2654}{as} \markbox{2655}{given} \markbox{2656}{in} \eqref{cohomo of grass}. \markbox{2657}{In} \eqref{Cohomology of H_times}, \markbox{2658}{we} \markbox{2659}{see} \markbox{2660}{that} \markbox{2661}{the} \markbox{2662}{cohomology} \markbox{2663}{ring} \markbox{2664}{of} \markbox{m2665}{$S^m \times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{2666}{is} \markbox{2667}{generated} \markbox{2668}{by} \markbox{m2669}{$u, c_i, \forall i \in I$}. \markbox{2670}{Therefore,} \markbox{2671}{it} \markbox{2672}{is} \markbox{2673}{sufficient} \markbox{2674}{to} \markbox{2675}{describe} \markbox{2676}{the} \markbox{2677}{images} \markbox{2678}{of} \markbox{2679}{the} \markbox{2680}{generators} \markbox{2681}{to} \markbox{2682}{classify} \markbox{2683}{graded} \markbox{2684}{endomorphisms} \markbox{2685}{of} \markbox{m2686}{$H_{\times}^*$}. \markbox{2687}{The} \markbox{2688}{following} \markbox{2689}{is} \markbox{2690}{the} \markbox{2691}{main} \markbox{2692}{result} \markbox{2693}{of} \markbox{2694}{this} section.
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	% We now state the following result concerning the classification of graded endomorphisms of $H^*_\times$ that are non-vanishing on  $H^2_{\mathbb{C}G} \subseteq H^*_\times$.
	\begin{theorem}\label{main thm}
		\markbox{2695}{Let} \markbox{m2696}{$\phi$} \markbox{2697}{be} \markbox{2698}{a} \markbox{2699}{graded} \markbox{2700}{endomorphism} \markbox{2701}{of} \markbox{m2702}{$H^*_{\times}$} \markbox{2703}{satisfying} \markbox{m2704}{$\phi(c_1) \neq \mu u,\, \mu \in \mathbb{Q}$}.  
		\markbox{2705}{Then} \markbox{2706}{the} \markbox{2707}{following} \markbox{2708}{holds,} \begin{enumerate}
			\item {} Either \markbox{m2709}{$\phi(u)=au$} \markbox{2710}{for} \markbox{2711}{some} \markbox{m2712}{$a \in \mathbb{Q}$}, \markbox{2713}{or} \markbox{m2714}{$\phi(u) \in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \subseteq H^*_{\times}$} \markbox{2715}{with} \markbox{m2716}{$\phi(u)^2=0$} \markbox{2717}{in} \markbox{m2718}{$H^*_{\times}$}.
			\item {} There \markbox{2719}{exists} \markbox{m2720}{$\lambda \in \mathbb Q\backslash\{0\}$} \markbox{2721}{such} that
			$$\phi(c_i) = \begin{cases}
				\lambda^i c_i,   \forall i \in I& \text{ if } k<n-k,\\
				\lambda^i c_i,  \forall i \in I \quad \text{ or } \quad(-\lambda)^i (c^{-1})_i,    \forall i \in I & \text{ if } k= n-k,
			\end{cases}$$
		\end{enumerate} \markbox{2722}{where} \markbox{m2723}{$ (c^{-1})_i $} \markbox{2724}{is} \markbox{2725}{the} \markbox{m2726}{$ 2i $}-dimensional \markbox{2727}{part} \markbox{2728}{of} \markbox{2729}{the} \markbox{2730}{inverse} \markbox{2731}{of} \markbox{m2732}{$ c = 1 + c_1 + \cdots + c_k $} \markbox{2733}{in} \markbox{m2734}{$ H^*_{ \mathbb CG} $}.
	\end{theorem}
	
	% \textcolor{red}{Maybe we can write this theorem in full generality when $\mathbb CG_{n,k}$ is replaced by $G/H$ as in Theorem $A'$ in \cite{shiga-tezuka}, and deduce this result as corollary.}
	
	\begin{proof}
		%Since $\phi$ is graded and non-vanishing on $H^2_{\mathbb CG}$, the image $\phi(c_1) = \lambda c_1+uP_1$ for some nonzero $\lambda \in \mathbb{Q}$ and $P_1\in H^{2-m}_{\mathbb CG}$.
		From \markbox{2735}{equation} \eqref{Cohomology of H_times} \markbox{2736}{and} \eqref{H in terms of u}, \markbox{2737}{we} \markbox{2738}{have} \markbox{m2739}{$H^*_{\times}\cong \mathcal R/\mathcal I \cong H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \oplus u H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}, \markbox{2740}{where} \markbox{m2741}{$\mathcal R:=\mathbb Q[u,c_1,\ldots,c_k]$} \markbox{2742}{and} \markbox{m2743}{$\mathcal I:=\langle u^2, h_{n-k+1},\ldots,h_n\rangle$}.
		%, we may regard $H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$ as a subring of $H^*_{\times}$.
		%Therefore, the elements in $H^*_\times$ are of the $P+uQ$ where $P$ and $Q$ are in $H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$.
