        %that are not multiple of $u$, can be written purely in terms of $c_1,c_2,\ldots,c_k.$
		
		%We begin with \textit{(1)} for $k < n - k$.  
		Let \markbox{m2744}{$p_1: H^*_{\times} = H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \oplus u H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \to H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{2745}{be} \markbox{2746}{the} \markbox{2747}{projection} \markbox{2748}{onto} \markbox{2749}{the} \markbox{2750}{first} \markbox{2751}{summand} \markbox{2752}{and} \markbox{m2753}{$i_1: H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \hookrightarrow H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \oplus u H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{2754}{be} \markbox{2755}{the} \markbox{2756}{inclusion} \markbox{2757}{into} \markbox{2758}{the} \markbox{2759}{first} \markbox{2760}{summand.} \markbox{2761}{The} \markbox{2762}{composite} \markbox{m2763}{$\phi_1:= p_1 \circ \phi \circ i_1$} \markbox{2764}{is} \markbox{2765}{a} \markbox{2766}{degree-preserving} \markbox{2767}{endomorphism} \markbox{2768}{of} \markbox{m2769}{$H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}. \markbox{2770}{We} \markbox{2771}{have} \markbox{2772}{the} \markbox{2773}{following} diagram:
		% https://q.uiver.app/#q=WzAsNCxbMCwwLCJIXipfe1xcbWF0aGJiIENHfVxcb3BsdXMgdSBIXipfe1xcbWF0aGJiIENHfSJdLFsxLDAsIkheKl97XFxtYXRoYmIgQ0d9IFxcb3BsdXMgdSBIXipfe1xcbWF0aGJiIENHfSJdLFswLDEsIkheKl97XFxtYXRoYmIgQ0d9Il0sWzEsMSwiSF4qX3tcXG1hdGhiYiBDR30iXSxbMCwxLCJcXHBoaSJdLFsyLDAsImlfMSIsMCx7InN0eWxlIjp7InRhaWwiOnsibmFtZSI6Imhvb2siLCJzaWRlIjoidG9wIn19fV0sWzEsMywicF8xIiwwLHsic3R5bGUiOnsiaGVhZCI6eyJuYW1lIjoiZXBpIn19fV0sWzIsMywiXFx0aWxkZVxccGhpIl1d
		\begin{equation}\label{comm diagram}
			\begin{tikzcd}
				{H^*_{\mathbb CG}\oplus u H^*_{\mathbb CG}} & {H^*_{\mathbb CG} \oplus u H^*_{\mathbb CG}} \\
				{H^*_{\mathbb CG}} & {H^*_{\mathbb CG}}
				\arrow["\phi", from=1-1, to=1-2]
				\arrow["{p_1}", two heads, from=1-2, to=2-2]
				\arrow["{i_1}", hook, from=2-1, to=1-1]
				\arrow["{\phi_1}", from=2-1, to=2-2]
			\end{tikzcd}
		\end{equation}
		\markbox{2774}{Thus,} \markbox{2775}{for}  \markbox{m2776}{$x \in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \subset H^*_\times$}, \markbox{2777}{one} \markbox{2778}{can} write
		\markbox{m2779}{$\phi(x) = \phi_1(x) + u P_x$}
		\markbox{2780}{for} \markbox{2781}{some} \markbox{m2782}{$P_x \in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \subset H^*_\times$} \markbox{2783}{because} \markbox{2784}{the} \markbox{2785}{kernal} \markbox{2786}{of} \markbox{m2787}{$p_1$}, \markbox{m2788}{$\ker(p_1) = u H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}.
		\iffalse we have
		\begin{equation} 
			\phi(x) = \phi_1(x) + u P_x, \quad \text{where  } P_x\in H^*_{\mathbb CG}.
		\end{equation}\fi
		This \markbox{2789}{implies} \markbox{2790}{that} \begin{equation}\label{defn of phi}
			\phi(c_i) = \phi_1(c_i) + u P_{c_i},\, \forall i \in I.
		\end{equation} \markbox{2791}{For} \markbox{2792}{simplicity,} \markbox{2793}{denote} \markbox{m2794}{$P_{c_i}$} \markbox{2795}{by} \markbox{m2796}{$P_i\in H^{2i-m}_{\mathbb CG}$} \markbox{2797}{which} \markbox{2798}{is} \markbox{2799}{a} \markbox{2800}{polynomial} \markbox{2801}{in} \markbox{m2802}{$c_1, \dots, c_k$} \markbox{2803}{of} \markbox{2804}{degree} \markbox{m2805}{$2i - m$} \markbox{2806}{as} \markbox{m2807}{$\deg c_i = 2i$} \markbox{2808}{and} \markbox{m2809}{$\deg u = m$}.
		
		
		
		\markbox{2810}{Since} \markbox{m2811}{$\phi(c_1)\neq \mu u, \, \mu \in \mathbb{Q}$}, \markbox{2812}{that} \markbox{2813}{implies} \markbox{m2814}{$\phi(c_1)$} \markbox{2815}{is} \markbox{2816}{of} \markbox{2817}{the} \markbox{2818}{form} \markbox{m2819}{$\lambda c_1+\mu u,\, \lambda,\mu \in \mathbb{Q}, \, \lambda \neq 0$}. \markbox{2820}{Then} \markbox{2821}{we} \markbox{2822}{have} \markbox{m2823}{$\phi_1(c_1) = \lambda c_1,\, \lambda\neq 0$} \markbox{2824}{on} \markbox{m2825}{$H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}.  \markbox{2826}{By} \thmref{hom and hof} \markbox{2827}{part} \markbox{2828}{\textit{(ii)}}, \markbox{2829}{we} \markbox{2830}{have,} 
		\begin{equation}\label{phi_1}
			\phi_1(c_i) = \begin{cases}
				\lambda^i c_i,   \forall i \in I& \text{ if } k<n-k,\\
				\lambda^i c_i,  \forall i \in I \quad \text{ or } \quad(-\lambda)^i (c^{-1})_i,    \forall i \in I & \text{ if } k= n-k,
			\end{cases}
		\end{equation} \markbox{2831}{where} \markbox{m2832}{$ (c^{-1})_i $} \markbox{2833}{is} \markbox{2834}{the} \markbox{m2835}{$ 2i $}-dimensional \markbox{2836}{part} \markbox{2837}{of} \markbox{2838}{the} \markbox{2839}{inverse} \markbox{2840}{of} \markbox{m2841}{$ c = 1 + c_1 + \cdots + c_k $} \markbox{2842}{in} \markbox{m2843}{$ H^*_{ CG} $}. \markbox{2844}{Using} \markbox{2845}{the} \markbox{2846}{observations} \markbox{2847}{given} \markbox{2848}{above} \markbox{2849}{it} \markbox{2850}{is} \markbox{2851}{convenient} \markbox{2852}{to} \markbox{2853}{prove} \markbox{2854}{part} \markbox{2855}{\textit{(2)}} \markbox{2856}{first.} \\
		
		
		\markbox{2857}{\textit{proof of part (2):}} \markbox{2858}{Using} \eqref{defn of phi} \markbox{2859}{and} \eqref{phi_1}, \markbox{2860}{it} \markbox{2861}{is} \markbox{2862}{sufficient} \markbox{2863}{to} \markbox{2864}{prove} \markbox{2865}{that} \markbox{m2866}{$P_i =0, \, \forall i \in I$}. \markbox{2867}{By} \eqref{phi_1}, \markbox{2868}{we} \markbox{2869}{have} \markbox{2870}{that} \markbox{m2871}{$\phi_1$} \markbox{2872}{is} \markbox{2873}{an} \markbox{2874}{automorphism} \markbox{2875}{of} \markbox{m2876}{$H^*_{\mathbb CG}$}. \markbox{2877}{Using} \markbox{2878}{the} \markbox{2879}{invertibility} \markbox{2880}{of} \markbox{m2881}{$\phi_1$} \markbox{2882}{and} \eqref{defn of phi}, \markbox{2883}{let} \markbox{m2884}{$D: H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \rightarrow H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{2885}{be} \markbox{2886}{defined} \markbox{2887}{by} $$D(x) = P_{\phi_1^{-1}(x)},\, \forall x \in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}.$$
		%By degree comparison, $P_i =0, \, \forall i \in I$ if $m$ is odd or $m > 2k$. Hence, we assume that $m$ is even, i.e. $m = 2s$ with $s\in I$.
		%whenever $\phi(x) = \phi_1(x) + uP_x$.  
		Equivalently, \markbox{2888}{we} \markbox{2889}{have} \markbox{m2890}{$D(\phi_1(x)) = P_x$}. \markbox{2891}{Now,} \markbox{2892}{we} \markbox{2893}{prove} \markbox{2894}{that} \markbox{m2895}{$D$} \markbox{2896}{is} \markbox{2897}{a} \markbox{m2898}{$\mathbb Q$}-linear \markbox{2899}{transformation} \markbox{2900}{and} \markbox{2901}{satisfies} \markbox{2902}{the} \markbox{2903}{Leibniz} rule.
		%Linearity over $\mathbb{Q}$ is immediate, since for $t \in \mathbb{Q}$ one has
		\begin{equation}\label{D is linear}
			\begin{split}
				uP_{tx} &= \phi(tx) - \phi_1(tx) = t(\phi(x) - \phi_1(x)) = utP_{x},\, \forall t \in \mathbb{Q},\\
				uP_{x + y} &= \phi(x+y) - \phi_1(x+y) = \phi(x) - \phi_1(x)+ \phi(y) - \phi_1(y)\\ &= u(P_{x}+P_{y}),\\
				uP_{x y} &= \phi(x y) - \phi_1(xy) = \phi(x)\phi(y)-\phi_1(x)\phi_1(y) \\
				&= (\phi_1(x)+uP_{x})(\phi_1(y)+uP_y)- \phi_1(x)\phi_1(y)\\
				&= u(P_x\phi_1(y)+\phi_1(x)P_y).
			\end{split}
		\end{equation}
		\markbox{2904}{Using} \eqref{H in terms of u} \markbox{2905}{and} \eqref{D is linear}, \markbox{2906}{we} \markbox{2907}{get}  \begin{align*}
			& D(t\phi_1(x)) = tD(\phi_1(x)),\quad D(\phi_1(x)+\phi_1(y)) = D(\phi_1(x))+D(\phi_1(y)),\\
			&D(\phi_1(x)\phi_1(y)) = D(\phi_1(x))\phi_1(y)+\phi_1(x)D(\phi_1(y)).
		\end{align*}
		\iffalse \textcolor{red}{(Do we need to emphasise that $D(h_i)\in \langle h_{n-k+1},\ldots,h_n\rangle$, or it is obvious from linearlity?)}
		
		\markbox{2908}{To} \markbox{2909}{verify} \markbox{2910}{that} \markbox{m2911}{$D$} \markbox{2912}{satisfies} \markbox{2913}{the} \markbox{2914}{Leibniz} \markbox{2915}{condition} \markbox{m2916}{$D(xy)=D(x)y+xD(y)$},
		\markbox{2917}{it} \markbox{2918}{suffices} \markbox{2919}{to} \markbox{2920}{check} that
		\markbox{m2921}{$D(\phi_1(x)\phi_1(y))=D(\phi_1(x))\phi_1(y)+\phi_1(x)D(\phi_1(y))$}
		\markbox{2922}{for} \markbox{2923}{all} \markbox{m2924}{$x,y \in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}, \markbox{2925}{since} \markbox{m2926}{$\phi_1$} \markbox{2927}{is} \markbox{2928}{an} \markbox{2929}{automorphism} \markbox{2930}{of} \markbox{m2931}{$H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}.
		\markbox{2932}{Indeed,} from
		\markbox{m2933}{$\phi(xy)=\phi(x)\phi(y)=(\phi_1(x)+uP_x)(\phi_1(y)+uP_y)$} \markbox{2934}{where} \markbox{m2935}{$x,y\in H^*_{\mathbb CG}$}, \markbox{2936}{we} obtain
		\markbox{m2937}{$\phi(xy)=\phi_1(xy)+u(P_x\phi_1(y)+\phi_1(x)P_y)$}.
		\markbox{2938}{Comparing} \markbox{2939}{with} \markbox{m2940}{$\phi(xy)=\phi_1(xy)+uP_{xy}$} gives
		\markbox{m2941}{$P_{xy}=P_x\phi_1(y)+\phi_1(x)P_y$}, \markbox{2942}{and} therefore
		\markbox{m2943}{$D(\phi_1(x)\phi_1(y))=D(\phi_1(x))\phi_1(y)+\phi_1(x)D(\phi_1(y))$}. \fi
		This \markbox{2944}{proves} \markbox{2945}{that} \markbox{m2946}{$D$} \markbox{2947}{is} \markbox{2948}{a} \markbox{2949}{derivation.} \markbox{2950}{For} \markbox{m2951}{$x \in H^i_{\mathbb{C}G}$}, \markbox{2952}{we} \markbox{2953}{have} \markbox{m2954}{$D(x) \in H^{i-m}_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{2955}{which} \markbox{2956}{implies} \markbox{2957}{that} \markbox{2958}{the} \markbox{2959}{derivation} \markbox{m2960}{$D$} \markbox{2961}{decreases} \markbox{2962}{the} \markbox{2963}{degree} \markbox{2964}{by} \markbox{m2965}{$\deg(u)=m>0$}. \markbox{2966}{By} \eqref{cgn as hom} \markbox{2967}{and} \thmref{Tezuka}, \markbox{2968}{we} \markbox{2969}{get} \markbox{2970}{that} \markbox{m2971}{$D$} \markbox{2972}{is} \markbox{2973}{a} \markbox{2974}{zero} \markbox{2975}{derivation.} \markbox{2976}{In} \markbox{2977}{particular} $$D(\phi_1(c_i))=P_i=0, \, \forall i \in I.$$
		%This completes the proof of \textit{(1)} in both cases $k<n-k$ and $k=n-k$.
		
		\markbox{2978}{\textit{proof of part (1):}} \markbox{2979}{Since} \markbox{m2980}{$\phi$} \markbox{2981}{is} \markbox{2982}{a} \markbox{2983}{graded} \markbox{2984}{endomorphism} \markbox{2985}{on} \markbox{m2986}{$H^*_{\times}$}, \markbox{2987}{therefore} $$\phi(u) = a u + P, \, a \in \mathbb{Q}, \text{ satisfying } (a u + P)^2 =0,$$ \markbox{2988}{where} \markbox{m2989}{$P$} \markbox{2990}{is} \markbox{2991}{a} \markbox{2992}{homogeneous} \markbox{2993}{polynomial} \markbox{2994}{in} \markbox{m2995}{$c_1, \dots, c_k$} \markbox{2996}{of} \markbox{2997}{degree} \markbox{m2998}{$m$}. \markbox{2999}{We} \markbox{3000}{have} \markbox{m3001}{$P^2 + 2 a u P =0$} \markbox{3002}{in} \markbox{m3003}{$H^*_{\times}$}. \markbox{3004}{Using} \eqref{H in terms of u}, \markbox{3005}{we} \markbox{3006}{get} \markbox{3007}{that} \markbox{m3008}{$2aP =0$} \markbox{3009}{in} \markbox{m3010}{$H^*_{\times}=\mathcal{R}/\mathcal{I}$}. \markbox{3011}{Hence,} \markbox{3012}{either} \markbox{m3013}{$a=0$} \markbox{3014}{or} \markbox{m3015}{$P\in \mathcal{I}$}.
		%for some $f, f_i\in \mathcal R$ and generators $h_i$ of $\mathcal{I}\subset \mathcal R$. Write $f_i = g_i + u l_i$ with $g_i, l_i$ in $\mathbb{Q}[c_1, \dots, c_k]$, then comparing terms not in $u^2$ gives:\[P^2 + 2 a u P = \sum g_i h_i + u \sum l_i h_i.\]Thus, $2 a u P = u \sum l_i h_i \in \mathcal{I}$, so if $a \neq 0$, then $P \in \mathcal{I}$ and hence $\phi(u) = a u$ in $H^*_{\times}$. If $a = 0$, then $\phi(u) = P(c_1, \dots, c_k)$ with $P^2 \in \mathcal{I}$.This completes the proof.
	\end{proof}
	
	
		\begin{remark}
			\thmref{main thm} \markbox{3016}{classifies} \markbox{3017}{all} \markbox{3018}{graded} \markbox{3019}{endomorphisms} \markbox{m3020}{$\phi$} \markbox{3021}{of} \markbox{m3022}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3023}{whose} \markbox{3024}{image} \markbox{3025}{is} \markbox{3026}{nonzero} \markbox{3027}{in} \markbox{m3028}{$H^2_{\mathbb CG}$} \markbox{3029}{if} \markbox{m3030}{$n>2$}. \markbox{3031}{In} \markbox{3032}{fact,} \markbox{m3033}{$n>2$} \markbox{3034}{implies} \markbox{m3035}{$c_1^2\neq 0$} \markbox{3036}{and} \markbox{m3037}{$\phi(u) \neq ac_1,\, a \in \mathbb{Q}\setminus\{0\}$} \markbox{3038}{as} \markbox{m3039}{$\phi(u)^2=0$}. \markbox{3040}{Therefore,} \markbox{3041}{the} \markbox{3042}{only} \markbox{3043}{remaining} \markbox{3044}{possibility} \markbox{3045}{is} \markbox{m3046}{$\phi(c_1)\neq \mu u,\, \mu \in \mathbb Q.$} 
			
			\markbox{3047}{On} \markbox{3048}{the} \markbox{3049}{other} \markbox{3050}{hand,} \markbox{3051}{when} \markbox{m3052}{$n=2,$} \markbox{m3053}{$\mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{3054}{is} \markbox{3055}{either} \markbox{3056}{a} \markbox{3057}{point} \markbox{3058}{or} \markbox{m3059}{$\mathbb S^2$} \markbox{3060}{and} \markbox{3061}{the} \markbox{3062}{classification} \markbox{3063}{of} \markbox{3064}{graded} \markbox{3065}{endomorphisms} \markbox{3066}{of} \markbox{m3067}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3068}{is} easy.
		\end{remark}
	
	
	
	\subsection{} \markbox{3069}{In} \thmref{main thm}, \markbox{3070}{we} \markbox{3071}{assume} \markbox{3072}{that} \markbox{m3073}{$\phi(c_1) \neq \mu u$}. \markbox{3074}{Let} \markbox{3075}{us} \markbox{3076}{try} \markbox{3077}{to} \markbox{3078}{look} \markbox{3079}{at} \markbox{3080}{the} \markbox{3081}{other} \markbox{3082}{case} \markbox{3083}{where} \markbox{m3084}{$\phi(c_1) = \mu u$}. \markbox{3085}{To} \markbox{3086}{address} \markbox{3087}{this,} \markbox{3088}{we} \markbox{3089}{use} \markbox{3090}{part} \markbox{3091}{(i)} \markbox{3092}{of} \thmref{hom and hof} \markbox{3093}{which} \markbox{3094}{leads} \markbox{3095}{to} \markbox{3096}{the} \markbox{3097}{following} proposition.
	
	
	\begin{proposition}\label{main thm 2}
		\markbox{3098}{Assume} \markbox{3099}{that} \markbox{3100}{hypothesis} \eqref{Homer} \markbox{3101}{is} satisfied.
		\markbox{3102}{Let} \markbox{m3103}{$\phi$} \markbox{3104}{be} \markbox{3105}{a} \markbox{3106}{graded} \markbox{3107}{endomorphism} \markbox{3108}{such} \markbox{3109}{that} \markbox{m3110}{$\phi(c_1)=\mu u,\, \mu \in \mathbb{Q}$} \markbox{3111}{in} \markbox{m3112}{$H^*_{\times}$}. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item {} Either \markbox{m3113}{$\phi(u)=a u$} \markbox{3114}{for} \markbox{3115}{some} \markbox{m3116}{$a \in \mathbb{Q}$}, \markbox{3117}{or} \markbox{m3118}{$\phi(u) \in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G} \subseteq H^*_{\times}$} \markbox{3119}{with} \markbox{m3120}{$\phi(u)^2=0$} \markbox{3121}{in} \markbox{m3122}{$H^*_{\times}$}.
			\item  {} \markbox{m3123}{$\phi(c_i) = uP_i, \, \forall i >1,$} \markbox{3124}{where} \markbox{m3125}{$P_i \in H^{2i-m}_{\mathbb CG}\subseteq H^*_\times$}. 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proposition}
	\begin{proof} \markbox{3126}{\textit{(1):}} \markbox{3127}{The} \markbox{3128}{proof} \markbox{3129}{of} \markbox{3130}{part} \markbox{3131}{\textit{(1)}} \markbox{3132}{is} \markbox{3133}{exactly} \markbox{3134}{the} \markbox{3135}{same} \markbox{3136}{as} \markbox{3137}{the} \markbox{3138}{proof} \markbox{3139}{of} \markbox{3140}{part} \markbox{3141}{\textit{(1)}} \markbox{3142}{of} \thmref{main thm}. \markbox{3143}{Therefore,} \markbox{3144}{we} \markbox{3145}{omit} \markbox{3146}{the} details.
		
		\markbox{3147}{\textit{(2):}} \markbox{3148}{Using} \eqref{comm diagram}, \markbox{3149}{we} \markbox{3150}{have} \markbox{3151}{that} \markbox{3152}{the} \markbox{3153}{map} \markbox{m3154}{$\phi_1$} \markbox{3155}{is} \markbox{3156}{a} \markbox{3157}{graded} \markbox{3158}{endomorphism} \markbox{3159}{on} \markbox{m3160}{$H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{3161}{such} \markbox{3162}{that} \markbox{m3163}{$\phi_1(c_1) =0$}. \markbox{3164}{By} \thmref{hom and hof}, \markbox{m3165}{$\phi_1(c_i) =0, \, \forall i\in I$}, \markbox{3166}{then} \markbox{3167}{by} \eqref{defn of phi}, \markbox{3168}{we} \markbox{3169}{get} \markbox{m3170}{$\phi(c_i) = uP_i$} \markbox{3171}{for} \markbox{3172}{some} \markbox{m3173}{$P_i \in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}, \markbox{3174}{with} \markbox{m3175}{$\deg(P_i) = 2i - m$}. \end{proof}
	%  When $\lambda \neq 0$, the proof follows directly from Theorem~\ref{main thm}.
	\begin{remark}
		\markbox{3176}{In} \thmref{main thm} \markbox{3177}{and} \propref{main thm 2}, \markbox{3178}{if} \markbox{3179}{we} \markbox{3180}{assume} \markbox{m3181}{$2m \leq n-k$}  \markbox{3182}{then} \markbox{m3183}{$\phi(u)=0$} \markbox{3184}{whenever} \markbox{m3185}{$\phi(u) \in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}. \markbox{3186}{This} \markbox{3187}{is} \markbox{3188}{because} \markbox{m3189}{$H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{3190}{has} \markbox{3191}{no} \markbox{3192}{nontrivial} \markbox{3193}{relations} \markbox{3194}{up} \markbox{3195}{to} \markbox{3196}{degree} \markbox{m3197}{$2(n-k)$} \markbox{3198}{and} \markbox{m3199}{$u^2=0$} \markbox{3200}{implies} \markbox{3201}{that} \markbox{m3202}{$\phi(u)^2=0$} \markbox{3203}{forcing} \markbox{m3204}{$\phi(u)=0$}.
		
	\end{remark}
	%Now suppose $\lambda = 0$, i.e., $\phi(c_1) = 0$ in $H^*_\times$.
	%Unlike the case of Grassmannian, the following proposition guarantees the existence of non-trivial graded endomorphisms $\phi$ on $H^*_\times$ even if $\phi(c_1) =0$.
   A \markbox{3205}{graded} \markbox{3206}{endomorphism} \markbox{3207}{of} \markbox{m3208}{$H^*_{\mathbb CG}$} \markbox{3209}{that} \markbox{3210}{vanishes} on
   \markbox{m3211}{$H^2_{\mathbb CG}$} \markbox{3212}{is} \markbox{3213}{expected} \markbox{3214}{to} \markbox{3215}{be} \markbox{3216}{trivial,} \markbox{3217}{in} \markbox{3218}{view} \markbox{3219}{of} \markbox{3220}{Hoffman's} \markbox{3221}{conjecture} \cite{hoffman}. \markbox{3222}{However,} \markbox{3223}{unlike} \markbox{3224}{the} \markbox{3225}{case} \markbox{3226}{of} \markbox{3227}{the} \markbox{3228}{complex} \markbox{3229}{Grassmannian,} \markbox{3230}{there} \markbox{3231}{exist} \markbox{3232}{many} \markbox{3233}{non-trivial} \markbox{3234}{graded} \markbox{3235}{endomorphisms} \markbox{3236}{of} \markbox{m3237}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3238}{that} \markbox{3239}{vanish} \markbox{3240}{on} \markbox{m3241}{$H^2_{\mathbb CG}$}. \markbox{3242}{The} \markbox{3243}{following} \markbox{3244}{proposition} \markbox{3245}{provides}   \markbox{3246}{such} \markbox{3247}{examples} \markbox{3248}{when} \markbox{m3249}{$m$} \markbox{3250}{is} \markbox{3251}{even} \markbox{3252}{and}   \markbox{m3253}{$1\le m \le 2k$}.



	
	
	\begin{proposition}
		\markbox{3254}{For} \markbox{3255}{each} \markbox{m3256}{$i\in I$}, \markbox{3257}{choose} \markbox{m3258}{$P_i \in H^{2i-m}_{\mathbb C G} \subseteq H^*_\times$} \markbox{3259}{and} \markbox{3260}{either} \markbox{m3261}{$Q = au,\, a\in \mathbb Q$}, \markbox{3262}{or}  \markbox{m3263}{$Q\in H^*_{\mathbb CG}\subseteq H^*_{\times}$} \markbox{3264}{with} \markbox{m3265}{$Q^2=0$}  \markbox{3266}{in} \markbox{m3267}{$ H^*_{\times}$}. \markbox{3268}{Then} \markbox{3269}{there} \markbox{3270}{exist} \markbox{3271}{a} \markbox{3272}{graded} \markbox{3273}{endomorphism} \markbox{m3274}{$\phi$} \markbox{3275}{on} \markbox{m3276}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3277}{such} \markbox{3278}{that} 
		\[
		\phi(c_i)=uP_i, \; \forall i\in I, \text{ and  } \quad \phi(u)=Q.
		\]
	\end{proposition}
	\begin{proof}
		\markbox{3279}{Define} \markbox{m3280}{$\phi$} \markbox{3281}{on} \markbox{m3282}{$H^*_{\times} = \mathcal{R}/\mathcal{I}$} \markbox{3283}{by} \markbox{m3284}{$\phi(c_i)=uP_i, \; \forall i\in I, \text{ and } \phi(u)=Q.$} \markbox{3285}{It} \markbox{3286}{is} \markbox{3287}{sufficient} \markbox{3288}{to} \markbox{3289}{prove} \markbox{3290}{that} \markbox{m3291}{$\phi$} \markbox{3292}{is} \markbox{3293}{well} \markbox{3294}{defined,} \markbox{3295}{that} \markbox{3296}{is,} \markbox{m3297}{$\mathcal{I}\subseteq \ker (\phi)$}. \markbox{3298}{Observe} \markbox{3299}{that} \markbox{m3300}{$u^2 =0$} \markbox{3301}{in} \markbox{m3302}{$H^*_{\times}$} \markbox{3303}{which} \markbox{3304}{implies} \markbox{3305}{that} \begin{equation}\label{ideal cicj}
			\phi(c_i c_j) = \phi(c_i) \phi(c_j) = uP_i \cdot uP_j = u^2 P_i P_j = 0.
		\end{equation} \markbox{3306}{Using} \eqref{ideal cicj} \markbox{3307}{and} \markbox{m3308}{$\phi(u^2)=Q^2 =0$}, \markbox{3309}{we} \markbox{3310}{have} \markbox{m3311}{$\mathcal{I}\subseteq \langle u^2, c_i c_j \,|\, i,j \in I \rangle \subseteq \ker(\phi).$} 
	\end{proof}
	
	
	\subsection{} \markbox{3312}{In} \markbox{3313}{this} \markbox{3314}{subsection,} \markbox{3315}{we} \markbox{3316}{derive} \markbox{3317}{some} \markbox{3318}{immediate} \markbox{3319}{applications} \markbox{3320}{of} \thmref{main thm}.
	\begin{corollary}
		%It is natural to consider a more general situation with several spheres instead of a single one.  
		Let \markbox{3321}{us} \markbox{3322}{consider} \markbox{m3323}{$X = \mathbb{S}^{2m_1} \times \cdots \times \mathbb{S}^{2m_r} \times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{3324}{and} \markbox{3325}{denote} \markbox{3326}{by} \markbox{m3327}{$u_j$} \markbox{3328}{the} \markbox{3329}{generator} \markbox{3330}{of} \markbox{m3331}{$H^{2m_j}(\mathbb{S}^{2m_j}; \mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{3332}{corresponding} \markbox{3333}{to} \markbox{3334}{the} \markbox{3335}{fundamental} \markbox{3336}{class} \markbox{3337}{of} \markbox{m3338}{$\mathbb S^{2m_j}$} \markbox{3339}{for} \markbox{3340}{all} \markbox{m3341}{$1\leq j \leq r.$} \markbox{3342}{Define}  
		\[
		H^*_{\mathbf{m}, \mathbb{C}G} := H^*(\mathbb{S}^{2m_1} \times \cdots \times \mathbb{S}^{2m_r} \times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}; \mathbb{Q})
		\;\cong\; H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}[u_1,\ldots,u_r] \big/ \langle u_1^2,\ldots,u_r^2 \rangle,
		\] \markbox{3343}{where} \markbox{m3344}{$\mathbf{m} = (m_1, \ldots, m_r)$}.
		%where each $u_j$ denotes the degree-$m_j$ generator of $H^*(\mathbb{S}^{m_j}; \mathbb{Q})$.  
		Suppose \markbox{m3345}{$\phi: H^*_{\mathbf{m}, \mathbb{C}G} \to H^*_{\mathbf{m}, \mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{3346}{is} \markbox{3347}{a} \markbox{3348}{graded} \markbox{3349}{endomorphism} \markbox{3350}{satisfying} \markbox{m3351}{$\phi(c_1)=\lambda c_1,\, \lambda \neq 0$}. \markbox{3352}{Then} $$\phi(c_i) = \begin{cases}
			\lambda^i c_i,   \forall i \in I& \text{ if } k<n-k,\\
			\lambda^i c_i,  \forall i \in I \quad \text{ or } \quad(-\lambda)^i (c^{-1})_i,    \forall i \in I & \text{ if } k= n-k,
		\end{cases}$$
		\markbox{3353}{where} \markbox{m3354}{$ (c^{-1})_i $} \markbox{3355}{is} \markbox{3356}{the} \markbox{m3357}{$ 2i $}-dimensional \markbox{3358}{part} \markbox{3359}{of} \markbox{3360}{the} \markbox{3361}{inverse} \markbox{3362}{of} \markbox{m3363}{$ c = 1 + c_1 + \cdots + c_k $} \markbox{3364}{in} \markbox{m3365}{$ H^*_{ \mathbb CG} $}. 
	\end{corollary}
	\begin{proof}
		\markbox{3366}{The} \markbox{3367}{proof} \markbox{3368}{of} \markbox{3369}{this} \markbox{3370}{corollary} \markbox{3371}{is} \markbox{3372}{similar} \markbox{3373}{to} \markbox{3374}{the} \markbox{3375}{proof} \markbox{3376}{of} \markbox{3377}{part} \markbox{3378}{\textit{2}} \markbox{3379}{of} \thmref{main thm}. \markbox{3380}{Apply} \markbox{3381}{induction} \markbox{3382}{on} \markbox{m3383}{$r$} \markbox{3384}{and} \markbox{3385}{replace} \markbox{m3386}{$\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{3387}{with} \markbox{m3388}{$\hat{X} := \mathbb{S}^{2m_1}\times\cdots\times \mathbb{S}^{2m_{i-1}}\times \mathbb{S}^{2m_{i+1}}\times\cdots\times \mathbb{S}^{2m_r}\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k},$} \markbox{3389}{and} \markbox{3390}{the} \markbox{3391}{sphere} \markbox{m3392}{$\mathbb{S}^m$} \markbox{3393}{with} \markbox{m3394}{$\mathbb{S}^{2m_i}$} \markbox{3395}{in} \thmref{main thm}. \markbox{3396}{Since} \begin{equation}\label{Sm as hom}
			\mathbb S^{2m_j}=SO(2m_j+1)/SO(2m_j)
		\end{equation}
		\markbox{3397}{where} \markbox{3398}{the} \markbox{3399}{orthogonal} \markbox{3400}{groups} \markbox{m3401}{$SO(2m_j+1)$} \markbox{3402}{and} \markbox{m3403}{$SO(2m_j)$} \markbox{3404}{have} \markbox{3405}{the} \markbox{3406}{same} \markbox{3407}{rank} \markbox{m3408}{$m_j$}. \markbox{3409}{Using} \eqref{Sm as hom} \markbox{3410}{and} \eqref{cgn as hom}, \markbox{m3411}{$\hat{X}$} \markbox{3412}{satisfies} \markbox{3413}{the} \markbox{3414}{hypothesis} \markbox{3415}{of} \thmref{Tezuka}. \markbox{3416}{Therefore,} \markbox{3417}{every} \markbox{m3418}{$\mathbb{Q}$}-linear \markbox{3419}{derivation} \markbox{3420}{of} \markbox{m3421}{$H^*(\hat{X};\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{3422}{that} \markbox{3423}{decreases} \markbox{3424}{the} \markbox{3425}{degree} \markbox{3426}{by} \markbox{m3427}{$2m_i$} \markbox{3428}{is} trivial.
		%Since the $m_i$ are even, the    and $\mathbb CG_{n,k}=U(n)/U(k)\times U(n-k)$, the space $X$ can be realized as a homogeneous space $G/H$, where $G$ is a connected compact Lie group and $H$ a closed subgroup of maximal rank.  This satisfies the hypotheses of Shiga--Tezuka's Theorem~$A'$ \cite{sigha-tezuka}, which then implies that  The argument then proceeds as in Theorem~\ref{main thm}, which completes the proof.  
	\end{proof}
	\markbox{3429}{Let} \markbox{3430}{us} \markbox{3431}{turn} \markbox{3432}{our} \markbox{3433}{attention} \markbox{3434}{to} \markbox{3435}{the} \markbox{3436}{generalized} \markbox{3437}{Dold} \markbox{3438}{spaces} \markbox{m3439}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{3440}{defined} \markbox{3441}{in} \subsecref{gds}. \markbox{3442}{The} \markbox{3443}{following} \markbox{3444}{remark} \markbox{3445}{helps} \markbox{3446}{us} \markbox{3447}{to} \markbox{3448}{describe} \markbox{3449}{endomorphisms} \markbox{3450}{of} \markbox{m3451}{$H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{3452}{induced} \markbox{3453}{by} \markbox{3454}{continuous} \markbox{3455}{functions} \markbox{3456}{on} \markbox{m3457}{$P(m,n,k)$}. \markbox{3458}{These} \markbox{3459}{observations} \markbox{3460}{will} \markbox{3461}{be} \markbox{3462}{used} \markbox{3463}{in} \secref{section 4}.
	%to understand how continuous self-maps of $P(m,n,k)$ induce homomorphisms on the cohomology ring $H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb{Q})$. 
	%Let us record a few useful observations.
	\begin{remark}\label{lift}
		\markbox{3464}{For} \markbox{3465}{a} \markbox{3466}{continuous} \markbox{3467}{map} \markbox{m3468}{$f$} \markbox{3469}{on} \markbox{m3470}{$P(m,n,k)$}, \markbox{3471}{we} \markbox{3472}{have}  
		\begin{equation} \label{lift of f}
			f_*\circ \pi_*\big(\pi_1(\mathbb{S}^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k})\big)
			\subseteq \pi_*\big(\pi_1(\mathbb{S}^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k})\big),
		\end{equation}
		\markbox{3473}{where} \markbox{m3474}{$\pi_1(X)$} \markbox{3475}{denotes} \markbox{3476}{the} \markbox{3477}{fundamental} \markbox{3478}{group} \markbox{3479}{of} \markbox{3480}{a} \markbox{3481}{topological} \markbox{3482}{space} \markbox{m3483}{$X$}. \markbox{3484}{Hence,} \markbox{3485}{the} \markbox{3486}{composite} \markbox{m3487}{$f\circ \pi$} \markbox{3488}{admits} \markbox{3489}{a} \markbox{3490}{lift} \markbox{m3491}{$\tilde f$} on
		\markbox{m3492}{$\mathbb{S}^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{3493}{for} \markbox{3494}{the} \markbox{3495}{double} \markbox{3496}{covering}  
		\markbox{m3497}{$\pi:\mathbb{S}^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}\to P(m,n,k)$}.
	\end{remark}
	\markbox{3498}{Using} \remref{lift}, \markbox{3499}{we} \markbox{3500}{get} \markbox{3501}{the} \markbox{3502}{following} \markbox{3503}{commutative} diagram,
	
	\begin{equation}\label{comm diag on H}
		\begin{tikzcd}
			{H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb Q)}  & {H^*(\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q)} \\
			{H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb Q)} & {H^*(\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Q).}
			\arrow["{\pi^*}", from=1-1, to=1-2]
			\arrow["{f^*}"', from=1-1, to=2-1]
			%\arrow[hook, from=1-2, to=1-3]
			\arrow["{\bar f^*}", from=1-2, to=2-2]
			%\arrow["{\bar f^*}", from=1-3, to=2-3]
			\arrow["{\pi^*}", from=2-1, to=2-2]
			%\arrow[hook, from=2-2, to=2-3]
		\end{tikzcd}
	\end{equation}
	\markbox{3504}{where} \markbox{m3505}{$\pi^*$} \markbox{3506}{is} \markbox{3507}{an} \markbox{3508}{injective} \markbox{3509}{map.} \markbox{3510}{Using} \thmref{cohomology of P(m,n,k)} \markbox{3511}{and} \eqref{comm diag on H} \markbox{3512}{we} \markbox{3513}{obtain} \markbox{3514}{the} \markbox{3515}{following} \markbox{3516}{two} \markbox{3517}{corollaries.} 
	%as an immediate application of respectively. 	
	\begin{corollary}\label{cor3}
		\markbox{3518}{Let} \markbox{m3519}{$f^*$} \markbox{3520}{be} \markbox{3521}{an} \markbox{3522}{endomorphism} \markbox{3523}{of} \markbox{m3524}{$H^*(P(m,n,k); \mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{3525}{induced} \markbox{3526}{by} \markbox{3527}{a} \markbox{3528}{continuous} \markbox{3529}{function} \markbox{m3530}{$f$} \markbox{3531}{on} \markbox{m3532}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{3533}{satisfying} \markbox{m3534}{$f^*(c_1^2) \ne 0$}. Then
		\markbox{m3535}{$f^*$} \markbox{3536}{is} \markbox{3537}{the} \markbox{3538}{restriction} \markbox{3539}{of} \markbox{3540}{a} \markbox{3541}{graded} \markbox{3542}{endomorphism} \markbox{m3543}{$\tilde{f}^*$} \markbox{3544}{on}  \markbox{m3545}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3546}{satisfying} \markbox{m3547}{$\tilde{f}^*(c_1) = \lambda c_1, \lambda \neq 0$},  \markbox{3548}{to} \markbox{3549}{the} \markbox{3550}{fixed} \markbox{3551}{subring} \markbox{m3552}{$\mathrm{Fix}(\theta^*)$} \markbox{3553}{of} \markbox{m3554}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3555}{where} \markbox{m3556}{$\theta = \alpha\times \sigma$}.
	\end{corollary}
	\begin{corollary}\label{cor4}
		\markbox{3557}{Let} \markbox{m3558}{$f^*$} \markbox{3559}{be} \markbox{3560}{an} \markbox{3561}{endomorphism} \markbox{3562}{of} \markbox{m3563}{$H^*(P(m,n,k); \mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{3564}{induced} \markbox{3565}{by} \markbox{3566}{a} \markbox{3567}{continuous} \markbox{3568}{function} \markbox{m3569}{$f$} \markbox{3570}{on} \markbox{m3571}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{3572}{satisfying} \markbox{m3573}{$f^*(c_1^2) =0$} \markbox{3574}{and} \markbox{m3575}{$n>2$}. Then
		\markbox{m3576}{$f^*$} \markbox{3577}{is} \markbox{3578}{the} \markbox{3579}{restriction} \markbox{3580}{of} \markbox{3581}{a} \markbox{3582}{graded} \markbox{3583}{endomorphism} \markbox{m3584}{$\tilde{f}^*$} \markbox{3585}{on}  \markbox{m3586}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3587}{satisfying} \markbox{m3588}{$\tilde{f}^*(c_1) = au, a \in \mathbb{Q}$},  \markbox{3589}{to} \markbox{3590}{the} \markbox{3591}{fixed} \markbox{3592}{subring} \markbox{m3593}{$\mathrm{Fix}(\theta^*)$} \markbox{3594}{of} \markbox{m3595}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3596}{where} \markbox{m3597}{$\theta = \alpha\times \sigma$}.
	\end{corollary}
	\markbox{3598}{Using} \thmref{main thm} \markbox{3599}{in} \corref{cor3}, \markbox{3600}{and} \propref{main thm 2} \markbox{3601}{in} \corref{cor4} \markbox{3602}{along} \markbox{3603}{with} \markbox{3604}{hypothesis} \eqref{Homer}, \markbox{3605}{we} \markbox{3606}{can} \markbox{3607}{determine} \markbox{m3608}{$f^*$}.
    %if we add the assumption that the hypothesis \eqref{Homer} is satisfied in \corref{cor4}.
	
	Moreover, \markbox{3609}{there} \markbox{3610}{exist} \markbox{3611}{graded} \markbox{3612}{endomorphisms} \markbox{3613}{of} \markbox{m3614}{$H^*(P(m,n,k))$} \markbox{3615}{that} \markbox{3616}{are} \markbox{3617}{not} \markbox{3618}{induced} \markbox{3619}{by} \markbox{3620}{any} \markbox{3621}{continuous} \markbox{3622}{self-map} \markbox{3623}{of} \markbox{m3624}{$P(m,n,k)$}, \markbox{3625}{and} \markbox{3626}{cannot} \markbox{3627}{be} \markbox{3628}{realized} \markbox{3629}{as} \markbox{3630}{restrictions} \markbox{3631}{of} \markbox{3632}{graded} \markbox{3633}{endomorphisms} \markbox{3634}{of} \markbox{m3635}{$H^*_{\times}$}. \markbox{3636}{Let} \markbox{3637}{us} \markbox{3638}{see} \markbox{3639}{an} \markbox{3640}{example} \markbox{3641}{of} \markbox{3642}{such} \markbox{3643}{graded} endomorphism.
	
	
	%Also, there exist graded endomorphisms of $H^*(P(m,n,k); \mathbb{Q})$ which are not restriction of any graded endomorphism of $H^*_\times$, if the graded endomorphism is not induced from a continuous function on $P(m,n,k)$. Let us see an example of such graded endomorphism of $H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb{Q})$.
	\begin{example}
		\markbox{3644}{If} \markbox{m3645}{$m$} \markbox{3646}{odd,} \markbox{m3647}{$n>2$} \markbox{3648}{and} \markbox{m3649}{$k = 1$}, \markbox{3650}{then} \markbox{m3651}{$P(m,n,1)$} \markbox{3652}{is} \markbox{3653}{fibered} \markbox{3654}{by} \markbox{3655}{the} \markbox{3656}{complex} \markbox{3657}{projective} \markbox{3658}{space}  \markbox{m3659}{$\mathbb{C} P^{n-1}$} \markbox{3660}{over} \markbox{3661}{the} \markbox{3662}{real} \markbox{3663}{projective} \markbox{3664}{space} \markbox{m3665}{$\mathbb{R} P^m$}. \markbox{3666}{In} \markbox{3667}{this} \markbox{3668}{case,}  \markbox{m3669}{$H^*_\times\cong \mathbb Q[u,c_1]/\langle u^2, c_1^n\rangle$} \markbox{3670}{and} \markbox{3671}{using} \eqref{defn of theta*}\ and \thmref{cohomology of P(m,n,k)}, \markbox{3672}{the} \markbox{3673}{rational} \markbox{3674}{cohomology} \markbox{3675}{ring} $$H^*(P(m,n,1); \mathbb{Q}) \cong \mathbb{Q}[u, b] / \langle u^2, b^{\lfloor (n+1)/2 \rfloor} \rangle,$$ \markbox{3676}{where} \markbox{m3677}{$u$} \markbox{3678}{is} \markbox{3679}{a} \markbox{3680}{generator} \markbox{3681}{of} \markbox{m3682}{$H^m(\mathbb{R}P^m;\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{3683}{and} \markbox{m3684}{$b$} \markbox{3685}{restricts} \markbox{3686}{to} \markbox{m3687}{$c_1^2\in H^2(\mathbb CP^{n-1};\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{3688}{under} \markbox{3689}{the} \markbox{3690}{fiber} \markbox{3691}{inclusion.} 
		%Here, $\lfloor x\rfloor$ denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to $x$.
		
		Consider \markbox{3692}{the} endomorphism
		\[
		\phi \colon H^*(P(m,n,1); \mathbb{Q}) \to H^*(P(m,n,1); \mathbb{Q}), \quad \text{defined by }\quad u \mapsto u,  b \mapsto -b.
		\]
		\markbox{3693}{Then} \markbox{m3694}{$\phi$} \markbox{3695}{is} \markbox{3696}{a} \markbox{3697}{well-defined} \markbox{3698}{graded} \markbox{3699}{endomorphism} \markbox{3700}{but} \markbox{3701}{it} \markbox{3702}{cannot} \markbox{3703}{be} \markbox{3704}{a} \markbox{3705}{restriction} \markbox{3706}{of} \markbox{3707}{a} \markbox{3708}{graded} \markbox{3709}{endomorphism} \markbox{3710}{of} \markbox{m3711}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3712}{because} \markbox{3713}{any} \markbox{3714}{such} \markbox{3715}{map} \markbox{3716}{induces} \markbox{m3717}{$c_1^2 \mapsto \lambda^2 c_1^2$} \markbox{3718}{for} \markbox{3719}{some} \markbox{m3720}{$\lambda \in \mathbb{Q}$}, \markbox{3721}{and} \markbox{m3722}{$\lambda^2 \neq -1$}.
	\end{example}
	
	
	\iffalse
	\begin{corollary}
		\markbox{3723}{Assume} \markbox{3724}{that} \markbox{m3725}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{3726}{be} \markbox{3727}{an} \markbox{3728}{orientable} \markbox{3729}{manifold} \markbox{3730}{and} \markbox{m3731}{$n>2$}. \markbox{3732}{Let} \markbox{m3733}{$f$} \markbox{3734}{be} \markbox{3735}{a} \markbox{3736}{continuous} \markbox{3737}{map} \markbox{3738}{on} \markbox{m3739}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{3740}{with} \markbox{3741}{nonzero} \markbox{3742}{Brouwer} \markbox{3743}{degree.} \markbox{3744}{Then}  
		\markbox{3745}{the} \markbox{3746}{induced} \markbox{3747}{map} \markbox{m3748}{$f^*$} \markbox{3749}{is} \markbox{3750}{an} \markbox{3751}{automorphism} \markbox{3752}{on} \markbox{m3753}{$H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb Q)$}.
	\end{corollary}
	\begin{proof}
		\markbox{3754}{Using} \remref{lift}, \markbox{3755}{there} \markbox{3756}{exists} \markbox{3757}{a} \markbox{3758}{lift} \markbox{m3759}{$\tilde f: \mathbb{S}^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}\to \mathbb{S}^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} 
		\markbox{3760}{satisfying} \markbox{m3761}{$\pi\circ \tilde f = f\circ \pi$}. \markbox{3762}{Using} \corref{cor3} \markbox{3763}{and} \corref{cor4}, \markbox{3764}{we} \markbox{3765}{have} \markbox{m3766}{$f^*$} \markbox{3767}{is} \markbox{3768}{the} \markbox{3769}{restriction} \markbox{3770}{of} \markbox{3771}{a} \markbox{3772}{graded} \markbox{3773}{endomorphism} \markbox{m3774}{$\tilde{f}^*$} \markbox{3775}{on}  \markbox{m3776}{$H^*_\times$} \markbox{3777}{satisfying} \markbox{3778}{either} $$\tilde{f}^*(c_1) = \lambda c_1, \lambda \neq 0, \text{ if } f^*(c_1^2) \neq 0, \text{ or } \tilde f^*(c_1) =au, a\in \mathbb{Q}, \text{ if } f^*(c_1^2) =0,$$  \markbox{3779}{to} \markbox{3780}{the} \markbox{3781}{fixed} \markbox{3782}{subring} \markbox{m3783}{$\mathrm{Fix}(\theta^*)$} \markbox{3784}{of} \markbox{m3785}{$H^*_\times$}.
		
		\markbox{3786}{Let} \markbox{m3787}{$d=k(n-k)$}.  \markbox{3788}{The} \markbox{3789}{top} \markbox{3790}{cohomology} \markbox{m3791}{$H^{2d+m}_\times\cong\mathbb{Q}$} \markbox{3792}{is} \markbox{3793}{generated} \markbox{3794}{by} 
		\markbox{m3795}{$uc_1^d$}.  \markbox{3796}{The} \markbox{3797}{nonzero} \markbox{3798}{Brouwer} \markbox{3799}{degree} \markbox{3800}{of} \markbox{m3801}{$f$} \markbox{3802}{implies} \markbox{3803}{nonzero} \markbox{3804}{Brouwer} \markbox{3805}{degree} \markbox{3806}{of} \markbox{m3807}{$\tilde f$} \markbox{3808}{i.e.} \begin{equation}\label{brouwer}
			\tilde f^*(uc_1^d)=\nu\,uc_1^d \in uH^{*}_{\mathbb{C}G}, \, \nu \neq 0.
		\end{equation}
		
		\markbox{3809}{Let} \markbox{3810}{us} \markbox{3811}{consider} \markbox{3812}{the} \markbox{3813}{first} \markbox{3814}{case} \markbox{3815}{where} \markbox{m3816}{$f^*(c_1^2) \neq 0$} \markbox{3817}{then} \markbox{m3818}{$\tilde f^*(c_1) = \lambda c_1, \lambda \neq 0$}. \markbox{3819}{Using} \thmref{main thm}, \markbox{3820}{we} \markbox{3821}{have} \markbox{m3822}{$\tilde f^*(c_i) = \lambda^i c_i$}. \markbox{3823}{Also,} $$\tilde f^*(u) = \mu u, \mu \in \mathbb{Q}, \text{ or } \tilde f^*(u)\in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}.$$ \markbox{3824}{If} \markbox{m3825}{$\tilde f^*(u)\in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}, \markbox{3826}{then} \markbox{m3827}{$\tilde f^*(uc_1^d) \in H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}
		\markbox{3828}{which} \markbox{3829}{is} \markbox{3830}{a} \markbox{3831}{contradiction} \markbox{3832}{to} \eqref{brouwer}. \markbox{3833}{Therefore,} \markbox{m3834}{$\tilde f^*(u) = \mu u $} \markbox{3835}{where} \markbox{m3836}{$\mu \neq 0$} \markbox{3837}{because} \markbox{m3838}{$\nu \neq 0$}. \markbox{3839}{So,} \markbox{m3840}{$\tilde f^*$} \markbox{3841}{is} \markbox{3842}{an} automorphism.
		
		\markbox{3843}{Let} \markbox{3844}{us} \markbox{3845}{consider} \markbox{3846}{the} \markbox{3847}{other} \markbox{3848}{case} \markbox{3849}{when} \markbox{m3850}{$f^*(c_1^2) = 0$} \markbox{3851}{then} \markbox{m3852}{$\tilde f^*(c_1) = au, a \in \mathbb{Q}$}. \markbox{3853}{Since,} \markbox{m3854}{$u^2 =0$} \markbox{3855}{and} \markbox{m3856}{$d\geq 2$} \markbox{3857}{we} \markbox{3858}{have} $$\tilde f^*(uc_1^d) = \tilde f^*(u) (\tilde f^*(c_1))^d = \tilde f^*(u) a^d u^d =0$$ \markbox{3859}{which} \markbox{3860}{is} \markbox{3861}{a} \markbox{3862}{contradiction} \markbox{3863}{to} \eqref{brouwer}. \markbox{3864}{Hence,} \markbox{3865}{this} \markbox{3866}{case} \markbox{3867}{would} \markbox{3868}{not} \markbox{3869}{arise.} 
	\end{proof}
	\fi
	
	The \markbox{3870}{following} \markbox{3871}{corollary} \markbox{3872}{helps} \markbox{3873}{us} \markbox{3874}{to} \markbox{3875}{understand} \markbox{3876}{the} \markbox{3877}{relationship} \markbox{3878}{between} \markbox{3879}{the} \markbox{3880}{automorphisms} \markbox{3881}{of} \markbox{m3882}{$H^*(P(m,n,k))$} \markbox{3883}{with} \markbox{3884}{the} \markbox{3885}{automorphisms} \markbox{3886}{of} \markbox{m3887}{$H^*_{\times}$}.
	\begin{corollary}\label{automor}
		\markbox{3888}{Let} \markbox{m3889}{$f^*$} \markbox{3890}{be} \markbox{3891}{an} \markbox{3892}{automorphism} \markbox{3893}{of} \markbox{m3894}{$H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb{Q})$} \markbox{3895}{induced} \markbox{3896}{by} \markbox{3897}{a} \markbox{3898}{continuous} \markbox{3899}{function} \markbox{m3900}{$f$} \markbox{3901}{on} \markbox{m3902}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{3903}{and} \markbox{3904}{assume} \markbox{3905}{that} \markbox{m3906}{$n> 2$}. \markbox{3907}{Then} \markbox{m3908}{$\tilde{f}^*$} \markbox{3909}{is} \markbox{3910}{an} \markbox{3911}{automorphism} \markbox{3912}{of} \markbox{m3913}{$H^*_{\times}$}, \markbox{3914}{where} \markbox{m3915}{$\tilde{f}$} \markbox{3916}{is} \markbox{3917}{as} \markbox{3918}{in} \remref{lift}. \\ \markbox{3919}{Moreover} \markbox{3920}{there} \markbox{3921}{exist} \markbox{m3922}{$\lambda, \mu \in \mathbb{Q}\backslash \{0\}$} \markbox{3923}{such} \markbox{3924}{that} \markbox{m3925}{$\tilde{f}^*(u) = \mu u$} \markbox{3926}{and} \markbox{m3927}{$\tilde{f}^*(c_i)$} \markbox{3928}{is} \markbox{3929}{of} \markbox{3930}{the} \markbox{3931}{form} \markbox{3932}{given} \markbox{3933}{in} \markbox{3934}{\textit{(2)}} \markbox{3935}{of} \thmref{main thm}.
	\end{corollary}
	\begin{proof}
		\markbox{3936}{Using} \remref{lift}, \markbox{3937}{we} \markbox{3938}{have} \markbox{m3939}{$\tilde{f}^*$} \markbox{3940}{is} \markbox{3941}{a} \markbox{3942}{graded} \markbox{3943}{endomorphism} \markbox{3944}{of} \markbox{m3945}{$H^*_{\times}$}. \markbox{3946}{When} \markbox{m3947}{$n>2$}, \markbox{3948}{we} \markbox{3949}{have} \markbox{m3950}{$c_1^2\neq 0$} \markbox{3951}{in} \markbox{m3952}{$\fix (\theta^*)\subseteq H^*_\times$}, \markbox{3953}{where} Fix\markbox{m3954}{$(\theta^*)$} \markbox{3955}{is} \markbox{3956}{the} \markbox{3957}{fixed} \markbox{3958}{subring} \markbox{3959}{under} \markbox{m3960}{$\theta^*$} \markbox{3961}{defined} \markbox{3962}{in} \eqref{defn of theta*}. \markbox{3963}{Since} \markbox{m3964}{$f^*$} \markbox{3965}{is} \markbox{3966}{an} \markbox{3967}{automorphism,} \markbox{3968}{we} \markbox{3969}{have} \markbox{m3970}{$f^*(c_1^2) \neq 0$}. \markbox{3971}{Using} \corref{cor3}, \markbox{3972}{there} \markbox{3973}{exist} \markbox{m3974}{$\lambda \in \mathbb{Q}$} \markbox{3975}{such} \markbox{3976}{that} \markbox{m3977}{$\tilde{f}^*(c_1) = \lambda c_1, \lambda \neq 0$}.\\
		\markbox{3978}{By} \thmref{main thm}, \markbox{m3979}{$\tilde{f}^*(c_i)$} \markbox{3980}{is} \markbox{3981}{of} \markbox{3982}{the} \markbox{3983}{form} \markbox{3984}{given} \markbox{3985}{in} \markbox{3986}{\textit{(2)}} \markbox{3987}{of} \thmref{main thm}. \markbox{3988}{Also,} $$\tilde{f}^*(u) = \mu u, \, \mu \in \mathbb{Q} \quad \text{ or } \quad \tilde{f}^*(u) = Q$$ \markbox{3989}{where} \markbox{m3990}{$Q$} \markbox{3991}{is} \markbox{3992}{a} \markbox{3993}{polynomial} \markbox{3994}{of} \markbox{3995}{degree} \markbox{m3996}{$m$} \markbox{3997}{in} \markbox{m3998}{$H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$} \markbox{3999}{with} \markbox{m4000}{$Q^2 =0$}. \markbox{4001}{To} \markbox{4002}{conclude} \markbox{4003}{the} \markbox{4004}{result,} \markbox{4005}{we} \markbox{4006}{need} \markbox{4007}{to} \markbox{4008}{prove} \markbox{4009}{that} \markbox{m4010}{$\tilde{f}^*(u) = \mu u$} \markbox{4011}{where} \markbox{m4012}{$\mu \neq 0$}. \\
		\markbox{4013}{Suppose} \markbox{4014}{that} \markbox{m4015}{$\tilde{f}^*(u) = Q$}, \markbox{4016}{then} \markbox{4017}{the} \markbox{4018}{image} \markbox{4019}{set} \markbox{m4020}{$\im \tilde{f}^*\subseteq H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}$}. \markbox{4021}{Using} \corref{cor3}, \markbox{4022}{we} \markbox{4023}{get} $$\im f^*  \cong \im \tilde{f^*}|_{Fix (\theta^*)}\subseteq H^*_{\mathbb{C}G}.$$ \markbox{4024}{This} \markbox{4025}{is} \markbox{4026}{a} \markbox{4027}{contradiction} \markbox{4028}{to} \markbox{4029}{the} \markbox{4030}{assumption} \markbox{4031}{that} \markbox{m4032}{$f^*$} \markbox{4033}{is} \markbox{4034}{an} \markbox{4035}{automorphism} \markbox{4036}{because} \markbox{4037}{using} \thmref{cohomology of P(m,n,k)}, \markbox{4038}{either} \markbox{m4039}{$u$} \markbox{4040}{or} \markbox{m4041}{$uc_{1}$} \markbox{4042}{(depending} \markbox{4043}{on} \markbox{4044}{the} \markbox{4045}{parity} \markbox{4046}{of} \markbox{m4047}{$m$}) \markbox{4048}{is} \markbox{4049}{in} \markbox{m4050}{$\im f^*=\fix (\theta^*) \cong H^*(P(m,n,k);\mathbb{Q})$}. \markbox{4051}{Therefore,} \markbox{m4052}{$\tilde{f}^*(u) = \mu u, \mu \in \mathbb{Q}$} \markbox{4053}{and} \markbox{m4054}{$\mu \neq 0$} \markbox{4055}{because} \markbox{m4056}{$f^*$} \markbox{4057}{is} \markbox{4058}{an} automorphism.
	\end{proof}
	\subsection{} \markbox{4059}{The} \markbox{4060}{following} \markbox{4061}{theorem} \markbox{4062}{provides} \markbox{4063}{a} \markbox{4064}{criterion} \markbox{4065}{for} \markbox{4066}{the} \markbox{4067}{image} \markbox{4068}{of} \markbox{4069}{the} \markbox{4070}{spherical} \markbox{4071}{cohomology} \markbox{4072}{class} \markbox{4073}{mapped} \markbox{4074}{to} \markbox{4075}{a} \markbox{4076}{scaler} \markbox{4077}{multiple} \markbox{4078}{of} \markbox{4079}{itself} \markbox{4080}{under} \markbox{4081}{the} \markbox{4082}{graded} \markbox{4083}{endomorphism} on
	\markbox{m4084}{$H^*(\mathbb{S}^m \times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb Z)$} \markbox{4085}{induced} \markbox{4086}{from} \markbox{4087}{a} \markbox{4088}{continuous} map.
	
	
	
	\begin{theorem}\label{ind from top}
		\markbox{4089}{Let} \markbox{m4090}{$f$} \markbox{4091}{be} \markbox{4092}{a} \markbox{4093}{continuous} \markbox{4094}{map} \markbox{4095}{on} \markbox{m4096}{$\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{4097}{such} \markbox{4098}{that} \markbox{4099}{it} \markbox{4100}{stabilizes} \markbox{4101}{a} \markbox{4102}{copy} \markbox{4103}{of} \markbox{4104}{Grassmannian} \markbox{m4105}{$\{{x_0}\}\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{4106}{for} \markbox{4107}{some} \markbox{m4108}{$x_0\in \mathbb S^m.$} \markbox{4109}{Then} \markbox{4110}{the} \markbox{4111}{induced} \markbox{4112}{endomorphism} \markbox{4113}{in} \markbox{4114}{cohomology} \markbox{4115}{satisfies} \markbox{m4116}{$f^*(u) = \mu u$} \markbox{4117}{for} \markbox{4118}{some} \markbox{m4119}{$\mu \in \mathbb Z$}.
	\end{theorem}
	
	
	%\begin{theorem}\label{ind from top}
	%Let $x_0 \in \mathbb{S}^m$ and consider a graded endomorphism $f^*$ on $H^*_{\times}$  induced from a topological map $f$ on $\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$ such that $f (\{x_0 \}\times\mathbb CG_{n,k})\subseteq \{x_0\}\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$.  Then $f^*(u)=\mu u$ for some $\mu\in \mathbb Q.$
	%\end{theorem}
	
	
	\begin{proof}
		\markbox{4120}{Let} \markbox{m4121}{$\mathbb T^m$} \markbox{4122}{be} \markbox{4123}{the} \markbox{4124}{torus} \markbox{m4125}{$(\mathbb S^1)^m$} and
		\markbox{m4126}{$q:\mathbb T^m\to \mathbb S^m$} \markbox{4127}{be} \markbox{4128}{the} \markbox{4129}{quotient} \markbox{4130}{map} \markbox{4131}{that} \markbox{4132}{collapses} \markbox{4133}{the} \markbox{4134}{complement} \markbox{m4135}{$C$} \markbox{4136}{of} \markbox{4137}{an} \markbox{4138}{open} \markbox{4139}{disk} \markbox{m4140}{$D\subset \mathbb T^m$} \markbox{4141}{to} \markbox{4142}{the} \markbox{4143}{point} \markbox{m4144}{$x_0$} \markbox{4145}{in} \markbox{m4146}{$\mathbb{S}^m$}.  \markbox{4147}{Denote} \markbox{m4148}{$p_i$} \markbox{4149}{the} \markbox{m4150}{$i$}-th \markbox{4151}{projection} \markbox{4152}{map} \markbox{4153}{on} \markbox{m4154}{$\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{4155}{for} \markbox{m4156}{$i=1,2$} \markbox{4157}{and} \markbox{m4158}{$s:\mathbb S^m\setminus\{x_0\}\to D$} \markbox{4159}{is} \markbox{4160}{the} \markbox{4161}{inverse} \markbox{4162}{of} \markbox{4163}{the} \markbox{4164}{restriction} \markbox{m4165}{$q|_D$}.
		\markbox{4166}{Since} \markbox{m4167}{$f$} \markbox{4168}{stabilizes} \markbox{m4169}{$\{x_0\}\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$}, \markbox{4170}{define} \markbox{4171}{continuous} maps
		\markbox{m4172}{$g:\mathbb{C}G_{n,k}\to \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} \markbox{4173}{by} \markbox{m4174}{$(x_0,g(y)) = f(x_0,y)$} \markbox{4175}{and} \markbox{m4176}{$\tilde f:\mathbb T^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}\to \mathbb T^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}$} by
		\[
		\tilde f(x,y)=
		\begin{cases}
			\big(s\circ p_1\circ f(q(x),y),\,\,p_2\circ f(q(x),y)\big), & x\in D,\\[2pt]
			\big(x,g(y)\big), & x\in C.
		\end{cases}
		\]
		%where and $p_i$ denotes the $i$-th projection.  
		Then \markbox{4177}{it} \markbox{4178}{is} \markbox{4179}{easy} \markbox{4180}{to} \markbox{4181}{check} \markbox{4182}{that} \markbox{4183}{the} \markbox{4184}{following} \markbox{4185}{diagram} commutes:
		\[ \begin{tikzcd}
			{\mathbb T^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}} & {\mathbb T^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}} \\
			{\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}} & {\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}}
			\arrow["{\tilde f}", from=1-1, to=1-2]
			\arrow["{q\times \mathrm{id}}"', two heads, from=1-1, to=2-1]
			\arrow["{q\times \mathrm{id}}", two heads, from=1-2, to=2-2]
			\arrow["f", from=2-1, to=2-2]
		\end{tikzcd}
		\]
		
		\markbox{4186}{Since,} \markbox{4187}{the} \markbox{4188}{quotient} \markbox{4189}{map} \markbox{m4190}{$q$} \markbox{4191}{has} \markbox{4192}{Brouwer} \markbox{4193}{degree} \markbox{4194}{1,} \markbox{4195}{the} \markbox{4196}{induced} \markbox{4197}{map} \markbox{4198}{on} \markbox{4199}{rational} \markbox{4200}{cohomology} \markbox{m4201}{$q^*: H^*(\mathbb{S}^m; \mathbb{Z}) \rightarrow H^*(\mathbb{T}^m;\mathbb{Z})$} \markbox{4202}{sends} \markbox{m4203}{$u\mapsto 1\cdot u_1 u_2 \dots u_m$} \markbox{4204}{where} \markbox{m4205}{$u_i$} \markbox{4206}{denote} \markbox{4207}{the} \markbox{4208}{one} \markbox{4209}{dimensional} \markbox{4210}{cohomology} \markbox{4211}{class} \markbox{4212}{corresponding} \markbox{4213}{to} \markbox{4214}{the} \markbox{4215}{fundamental} \markbox{4216}{class} \markbox{4217}{of} \markbox{4218}{the} \markbox{m4219}{$i$}-th \markbox{4220}{circle} \markbox{4221}{factor} \markbox{4222}{of} \markbox{m4223}{$\mathbb T^m$} \markbox{4224}{for} \markbox{m4225}{$i\in \{1,2,\ldots,m\}$} \markbox{4226}{with} \markbox{4227}{appropriate} \markbox{4228}{orientation.} 
		%Let $u$ be a generator of $H^m(\mathbb S^m;\mathbb Z)$ so that $q^*(u)=u_1u_2\cdots u_m$.  
		Since \markbox{m4229}{$H^{\mathrm{odd}}(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb Z)=0$}, \markbox{4230}{the} \markbox{4231}{induced} \markbox{4232}{map} \markbox{m4233}{$\tilde f^*$} \markbox{4234}{sends} \markbox{4235}{each} \markbox{m4236}{$u_i$} \markbox{4237}{to} \markbox{4238}{a} \markbox{4239}{polynomial} \markbox{m4240}{$P_i(u_1,\dots,u_m)$}.  \markbox{4241}{We} \markbox{4242}{slightly} \markbox{4243}{abuse} \markbox{4244}{notation} \markbox{4245}{by} \markbox{4246}{using} \markbox{4247}{the} \markbox{4248}{same} \markbox{4249}{symbols} \markbox{4250}{for} \markbox{4251}{the} \markbox{4252}{cohomology} \markbox{4253}{classes} \markbox{4254}{of} \markbox{m4255}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m;\mathbb Z)$} \markbox{4256}{and} \markbox{m4257}{$H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb Z)$} \markbox{4258}{when} \markbox{4259}{viewed} \markbox{4260}{in} \markbox{m4261}{$H^*(\mathbb S^m\times \mathbb CG_{n,k};\mathbb Z)$}.
		\markbox{4262}{The} \markbox{4263}{induced} \markbox{4264}{diagram} \markbox{4265}{in} \markbox{4266}{cohomology} \markbox{4267}{implies} \markbox{4268}{the} \markbox{4269}{following} \markbox{4270}{commutative} diagram.
		\[
		\begin{tikzcd}
			{\prod_{i=1}^m u_i} & {\prod_{i=1}^m P_i(u_1,\ldots,u_m)} \\
			u & {f^*(u)}
			\arrow["{\tilde f^*}", maps to, from=1-1, to=1-2]
			\arrow["{(q\times \mathrm{id})^*}"', maps to, from=2-1, to=1-1]
			\arrow["{f^*}", maps to, from=2-1, to=2-2]
			\arrow["{(q\times \mathrm{id})^*}"', maps to, from=2-2, to=1-2]
		\end{tikzcd}
		\]
		\markbox{4271}{This} \markbox{4272}{implies} \markbox{4273}{that} \markbox{m4274}{$f^*(u)$} \markbox{4275}{does} \markbox{4276}{not} \markbox{4277}{contain} \markbox{4278}{any} \markbox{4279}{nonzero} \markbox{4280}{element} \markbox{4281}{from} \markbox{m4282}{$H^*(\mathbb{C}G_{n,k};\mathbb Z)$}.  
		\markbox{4283}{Thus,} \markbox{m4284}{$f^*(u)=\mu u$} \markbox{4285}{for} \markbox{4286}{some} \markbox{m4287}{$\mu\in \mathbb Z$}.
	\end{proof}
	%\begin{remark}
		%To remain consistent with notations, we have written the proof of \thmref{ind from top} over $\mathbb{Q}$, but the same proof also works over $\mathbb{Z}$.
	%\end{remark}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\section{Coincidence theory of $P(m,n,k)$} \label{section 4}
	\markbox{4288}{In} \markbox{4289}{this} \markbox{4290}{section,} \markbox{4291}{we} \markbox{4292}{study} \markbox{4293}{the} \markbox{4294}{\textit{coincidence theory}} \markbox{4295}{of} \markbox{4296}{generalized} \markbox{4297}{Dold} \markbox{4298}{spaces} \markbox{m4299}{$P(m,n,k)$} \markbox{4300}{defined} \markbox{4301}{in} \subsecref{gds}. \markbox{4302}{We} \markbox{4303}{establish} \markbox{4304}{the} \markbox{4305}{necessary} \markbox{4306}{conditions} \markbox{4307}{for} \markbox{4308}{a} \markbox{4309}{generalized} \markbox{4310}{Dold} \markbox{4311}{space} \markbox{m4312}{$P(S,X)$} \markbox{4313}{defined} \markbox{4314}{in} \eqref{gen dold space} \markbox{4315}{to} \markbox{4316}{satisfy} \markbox{4317}{the} \markbox{4318}{coincidence} \markbox{4319}{property.} 
	%Our study builds upon previous results on the \emph{graded endomorphisms} of the rational cohomology ring $H^*_\times$ in section~\ref{graded endomorphism} and the \emph{rational cohomology ring of generalized Dold spaces} as established in \cite{mandal-sankaran2}.
	
	\subsection{} \markbox{4320}{Let} \markbox{4321}{us} \markbox{4322}{recall} \markbox{4323}{certain} \markbox{4324}{definitions} \markbox{4325}{that} \markbox{4326}{will} \markbox{4327}{be} \markbox{4328}{required} \markbox{4329}{in} \markbox{4330}{the} \markbox{4331}{rest} \markbox{4332}{of} \markbox{4333}{this} section.
	
	\begin{definition}
		\markbox{4334}{Let} \markbox{m4335}{$(X,g)$} \markbox{4336}{be} \markbox{4337}{a} \markbox{4338}{pair,} \markbox{4339}{where} \markbox{m4340}{$g$} \markbox{4341}{is} \markbox{4342}{a} \markbox{4343}{continuous} \markbox{4344}{map} \markbox{4345}{on} \markbox{4346}{a} \markbox{4347}{topological} \markbox{4348}{space} \markbox{m4349}{$X$}. \markbox{4350}{The} \markbox{4351}{pair} \markbox{m4352}{$(X,g)$} \markbox{4353}{is} \markbox{4354}{said} \markbox{4355}{to} \markbox{4356}{have} \markbox{4357}{the} \markbox{4358}{\textbf{coincidence property}} \markbox{4359}{(in} \markbox{4360}{short,} \markbox{4361}{CP)} \markbox{4362}{if,} \markbox{4363}{for} \markbox{4364}{every} \markbox{4365}{continuous} \markbox{4366}{map} \markbox{m4367}{$f : X \to X$}, \markbox{4368}{there} \markbox{4369}{exists} \markbox{4370}{a} \markbox{4371}{point} \markbox{m4372}{$x \in X$} \markbox{4373}{such} \markbox{4374}{that} \markbox{m4375}{$f(x) = g(x)$}.
	\end{definition}
	
	\markbox{4376}{If} \markbox{4377}{we} \markbox{4378}{consider} \markbox{m4379}{$g$} \markbox{4380}{to} \markbox{4381}{be} \markbox{4382}{the} \markbox{4383}{identity} \markbox{4384}{map} \markbox{4385}{on} \markbox{m4386}{$X$}, \markbox{4387}{then} \markbox{4388}{the} \markbox{4389}{notion} \markbox{4390}{of} \markbox{4391}{coincidence} \markbox{4392}{reduces} \markbox{4393}{to} \markbox{4394}{that} \markbox{4395}{of} \markbox{4396}{a} \markbox{4397}{fixed} \markbox{4398}{point,} \markbox{4399}{resulting} \markbox{4400}{in} \markbox{4401}{the} \markbox{4402}{following} definition.
	
	
	
	\begin{definition}
		\markbox{4403}{A} \markbox{4404}{topological} \markbox{4405}{space} \markbox{m4406}{$X$} \markbox{4407}{is} \markbox{4408}{said} \markbox{4409}{to} \markbox{4410}{have} \markbox{4411}{\textbf{fixed-point property}} \markbox{4412}{(FPP)} \markbox{4413}{if} \markbox{4414}{every} \markbox{4415}{continuous} \markbox{4416}{map} \markbox{m4417}{$f : X \to X$} \markbox{4418}{admits} \markbox{4419}{a} \markbox{4420}{fixed-point;} \markbox{4421}{that} \markbox{4422}{is,} \markbox{4423}{there} \markbox{4424}{exists} \markbox{m4425}{$x \in X$} \markbox{4426}{such} \markbox{4427}{that} \markbox{m4428}{$f(x) = x$}.
	\end{definition}
	
	
	%Our aim is to understand the situations when two continuous maps on the generalized Dold spaces $P(S,X)$ defined in \subsecref{gen dold}, have coincidence.
	 The \markbox{4429}{following} \markbox{4430}{proposition} \markbox{4431}{provides} \markbox{4432}{a} \markbox{4433}{criteria} \markbox{4434}{in} \markbox{4435}{terms} \markbox{4436}{of} \markbox{4437}{the} \markbox{4438}{fiber} \markbox{m4439}{$X$} \markbox{4440}{and} \markbox{4441}{the} \markbox{4442}{base} \markbox{4443}{space} \markbox{m4444}{$Y := S/\!\!\sim_\alpha$}, \markbox{4445}{allowing} \markbox{4446}{one} \markbox{4447}{to} \markbox{4448}{infer} \markbox{4449}{the} \markbox{4450}{coincidence} \markbox{4451}{properties} \markbox{4452}{of} \markbox{4453}{the} \markbox{4454}{total} \markbox{4455}{space} \markbox{m4456}{$P(S,X)$}.
	
	%As a first step, we establish the following proposition, which provides necessary conditions for a generalized Dold space to exhibit certain coincidence properties. 
	
	
	
	
	\iffalse
	\begin{proposition}
		\  \markbox{4457}{A} \markbox{4458}{generalized} \markbox{4459}{Dold} \markbox{4460}{space} \markbox{m4461}{$P(S,\alpha,X,\sigma)$} \markbox{4462}{does} \markbox{4463}{not} \markbox{4464}{have} \markbox{4465}{fixed} \markbox{4466}{point} \markbox{4467}{property} \markbox{4468}{if} \markbox{4469}{any} \markbox{4470}{of} \markbox{4471}{the} \markbox{4472}{following} holds:\\
		\markbox{4473}{(i)} \markbox{m4474}{$Y=S/\!\!\sim _{\alpha}$} \markbox{4475}{does} \markbox{4476}{not} \markbox{4477}{have} \markbox{4478}{the} \markbox{4479}{fixed} \markbox{4480}{point} property.\\
		\markbox{4481}{(ii)} \markbox{4482}{There} \markbox{4483}{exists} \markbox{4484}{a} \markbox{4485}{map} \markbox{m4486}{$f:X\to X$} \markbox{4487}{having} \markbox{4488}{no} \markbox{4489}{fixed-point} \markbox{4490}{and} \markbox{m4491}{$f\circ \sigma=\sigma \circ f$}.
	\end{proposition}
	\begin{proof}
		\markbox{4492}{(i)} \markbox{4493}{Let} \markbox{m4494}{$g:Y\to Y$} \markbox{4495}{be} \markbox{4496}{fixed} \markbox{4497}{point} \markbox{4498}{free.} \markbox{4499}{Then} \markbox{m4500}{$\phi:=s\circ g\circ p$} \markbox{4501}{on} \markbox{m4502}{$P(S,X)$} \markbox{4503}{also} \markbox{4504}{has} \markbox{4505}{no} \markbox{4506}{fixed} \markbox{4507}{points,} \markbox{4508}{where} \markbox{m4509}{$p$} \markbox{4510}{is} \markbox{4511}{the} \markbox{m4512}{$X$}-bundle \markbox{4513}{projection} \markbox{4514}{and} \markbox{m4515}{$s$} \markbox{4516}{is} \markbox{4517}{a} \markbox{4518}{section.}  
		\markbox{4519}{(ii).}   \markbox{4520}{Suppose} \markbox{4521}{that} \markbox{m4522}{$f:X\to X$} \markbox{4523}{has} \markbox{4524}{no} \markbox{4525}{fixed} \markbox{4526}{points} \markbox{4527}{and} \markbox{4528}{that} \markbox{m4529}{$f\circ \sigma=\sigma \circ f$}.
		\markbox{4530}{Now} \markbox{4531}{define} \markbox{m4532}{$\psi:P(S,X)\to P(S,X)$} \markbox{4533}{as} \markbox{m4534}{$[s,x]\mapsto [s,f(x)]$}. \markbox{4535}{The} \markbox{4536}{well-definedness} \markbox{4537}{follows} \markbox{4538}{because} \markbox{m4539}{$\psi([\alpha(s),\sigma(x)])=[\alpha(s),f\circ\sigma(x)]=[\alpha(s),\sigma \circ f(x)]=[s,f(x)]=\psi ([s,x])$}. \markbox{4540}{Clearly,} \markbox{m4541}{$\psi$} \markbox{4542}{has} \markbox{4543}{no} \markbox{4544}{fixed} \markbox{4545}{points.} \markbox{4546}{This} \markbox{4547}{completes} \markbox{4548}{the} proof.
	\end{proof}
	\fi
	
	
	%Recall that $P(S,X)$ has the fiber bundle structure $X\hookrightarrow P(SX)\twoheadrightarrow Y:=S/\!\! \sim_\alpha$, where $p$ is the $X$-bundle projection and $s$ is a section.  
	\begin{proposition}\label{necessary condition}
		\markbox{4549}{Let} \markbox{m4550}{$(P(S,X),g)$} \markbox{4551}{be} \markbox{4552}{a} \markbox{4553}{pair,} \markbox{4554}{where} \markbox{m4555}{$g$} \markbox{4556}{is} \markbox{4557}{a} \markbox{4558}{continuous} \markbox{4559}{map} \markbox{4560}{on} \markbox{4561}{the} \markbox{4562}{generalized} \markbox{4563}{Dold} \markbox{4564}{space} \markbox{m4565}{$P(S,X)$}. \markbox{4566}{Then} \markbox{m4567}{$(P(S,X),g)$} \markbox{4568}{does} \markbox{4569}{not} \markbox{4570}{have} \markbox{4571}{the} \markbox{4572}{CP} \markbox{4573}{if} \markbox{4574}{one} \markbox{4575}{of} \markbox{4576}{the} \markbox{4577}{following} hold:
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item {} The \markbox{4578}{continuous} \markbox{4579}{map} \markbox{m4580}{$g$} \markbox{4581}{is} \markbox{4582}{a} \markbox{4583}{fiber} \markbox{4584}{bundle} \markbox{4585}{map} \markbox{4586}{and} \markbox{4587}{the} \markbox{4588}{pair} \markbox{m4589}{$(Y,p \circ g \circ s)$} \markbox{4590}{does} \markbox{4591}{not} \markbox{4592}{have} \markbox{4593}{the} \markbox{4594}{CP,} 
			\markbox{4595}{where} \markbox{m4596}{$Y = S/\!\!\sim_\alpha$} \markbox{4597}{and} \markbox{m4598}{$s$} \markbox{4599}{denotes} \markbox{4600}{a} \markbox{4601}{section} \markbox{4602}{of} \markbox{4603}{the} \markbox{m4604}{$X$}-bundle \markbox{4605}{projection} \markbox{m4606}{$p$} \markbox{4607}{defined} \markbox{4608}{in} \eqref{sectio} \markbox{4609}{and} \eqref{proj}.
			
			\item  
			{} There \markbox{4610}{exists} \markbox{4611}{a} \markbox{m4612}{$\sigma$}-equivariant \markbox{4613}{map} \markbox{m4614}{$f$} \markbox{4615}{(i.e.} \markbox{m4616}{$f\circ\sigma =\sigma\circ f$}) \markbox{4617}{on} \markbox{m4618}{$X$} \markbox{4619}{and} \markbox{4620}{a} \markbox{m4621}{$\alpha \times \sigma$}-equivariant \markbox{4622}{map} \markbox{m4623}{$\tilde g$} \markbox{4624}{on} \markbox{m4625}{$S\times X$} \markbox{4626}{inducing} \markbox{m4627}{$g$} \markbox{4628}{such} that
			\markbox{m4629}{$\mathrm{id}_S \times f$} \markbox{4630}{coincides} \markbox{4631}{with} \markbox{4632}{neither} \markbox{m4633}{$\tilde{g}$} nor
			\markbox{m4634}{$(\alpha \times \sigma) \circ \tilde{g}$}.
		\end{enumerate}
		
		
		
	\end{proposition}
	\begin{proof} \markbox{4635}{\textit{(1)}}
		\markbox{4636}{Suppose} \markbox{4637}{that} \markbox{4638}{the} \markbox{4639}{pair} \markbox{m4640}{$(Y,p \circ g \circ s)$} \markbox{4641}{does} \markbox{4642}{not} \markbox{4643}{have} \markbox{4644}{the} \markbox{4645}{CP.} 
		\markbox{4646}{Then} \markbox{4647}{there} \markbox{4648}{exists} \markbox{4649}{a} \markbox{4650}{continuous} \markbox{4651}{map} \markbox{m4652}{$f : Y \to Y$} \markbox{4653}{such} \markbox{4654}{that} \begin{equation} \label{pogos}
			f(x) \neq p \circ g \circ s(x), \, \forall x \in Y.
		\end{equation}
		\markbox{4655}{We} \markbox{4656}{are} \markbox{4657}{given} \markbox{4658}{that} \markbox{m4659}{$g$} \markbox{4660}{is} \markbox{4661}{a} \markbox{4662}{fiber} \markbox{4663}{bundle} \markbox{4664}{map,} \markbox{4665}{which} \markbox{4666}{implies} \markbox{4667}{that} \markbox{4668}{there} \markbox{4669}{exist}  \markbox{m4670}{$g_1:Y\to Y$}, \markbox{4671}{satisfying}  \markbox{m4672}{$p \circ g = g_1 \circ p.$}
		\markbox{4673}{Consider} \markbox{m4674}{$p\circ g\circ s=g_1\circ p\circ s=g_1 $}.
		\markbox{4675}{Thus,} \markbox{m4676}{$p \circ g = g_1 \circ p$} implies
		\[
		p \circ g(x) = p \circ g \circ s \circ p(x),\, \forall x \in P(S, X).
		\]
		\markbox{4677}{Define} \markbox{4678}{the} \markbox{4679}{map} \markbox{m4680}{$\phi := s \circ f \circ p$} \markbox{4681}{on} \markbox{m4682}{$P(S, X)$}. \markbox{4683}{We} \markbox{4684}{claim} \markbox{4685}{that} \markbox{m4686}{$\phi(y)\neq g(y), \, \forall y \in P(S,X)$}. \\ \markbox{4687}{Suppose} \markbox{4688}{there} \markbox{4689}{exist} \markbox{m4690}{$y \in P(S, X)$} \markbox{4691}{such} \markbox{4692}{that} \markbox{m4693}{$\phi(y) = g(y)$}, \markbox{4694}{then} 
		\[
		p \circ g \circ s(p(y)) = p \circ g(y)
		= p \circ s \circ f \circ p (y) 
		= f(p(y)),
		\]
		\markbox{4695}{which} \markbox{4696}{contradicts} \eqref{pogos}.
		
		
		\markbox{4697}{\textit{(2)}} %Let $G$ be a group of order $2$ generated by $\alpha \times \sigma$ acting on the topological space $S\times X$ by composition.
		Let \markbox{m4698}{$G$} \markbox{4699}{denote} \markbox{4700}{the} \markbox{4701}{group} \markbox{4702}{of} \markbox{4703}{deck} \markbox{4704}{transformations} \markbox{4705}{of} \markbox{4706}{the} \markbox{4707}{double} \markbox{4708}{covering} \markbox{m4709}{$\pi : S \times X \to P(S, X)$}, \markbox{4710}{generated} \markbox{4711}{by} \markbox{4712}{the} \markbox{4713}{free} \markbox{4714}{involution} \markbox{m4715}{$\alpha \times \sigma.$}
		\markbox{4716}{The} \markbox{4717}{proof} \markbox{4718}{then} \markbox{4719}{follows} \markbox{4720}{from} \markbox{4721}{a} \markbox{4722}{general} \markbox{4723}{observation} \markbox{4724}{that} \markbox{4725}{if} \markbox{4726}{for} \markbox{4727}{two} \markbox{m4728}{$G$}-equivariant \markbox{4729}{maps} \markbox{m4730}{$\tilde\phi, \tilde\psi$} \markbox{4731}{on} \markbox{m4732}{$S\times X$}, \markbox{4733}{the} \markbox{4734}{maps} \markbox{m4735}{$\tilde \phi$} \markbox{4736}{and} \markbox{m4737}{$t \cdot \tilde\psi$} \markbox{4738}{have} \markbox{4739}{no} \markbox{4740}{point} \markbox{4741}{of} \markbox{4742}{coincidence,} \markbox{4743}{for} \markbox{4744}{any} \markbox{m4745}{$t \in G$}; \markbox{4746}{then} \markbox{4747}{the} \markbox{4748}{maps} \markbox{4749}{they} \markbox{4750}{induce} \markbox{4751}{on} \markbox{4752}{the} \markbox{4753}{orbit} \markbox{4754}{space} \markbox{m4755}{$P(S,X)$}, \markbox{4756}{namely} \markbox{m4757}{$\phi, \psi$}, \markbox{4758}{are} \markbox{4759}{also} coincidence-free.
		%$id_{S}\times f$ coincides with neither $\tilde g$ nor $(\alpha \times \sigma)\circ \tilde g$ then the two $G$-equivariant maps $\tilde\phi, \tilde\psi: M \to M$ on a topological space $M$, the maps $\tilde \phi$ and $t \cdot \tilde\psi$ have no point of coincidence, for any $t \in G$; then the maps they induce on the orbit space $M/G$, namely $\phi, \psi: M/G \to M/G$, are coincidence-free.
	\end{proof}
	
	\iffalse
	\begin{proposition}
		
		
		\markbox{4760}{Let} \markbox{m4761}{$g : P(S,X) \to P(S,X)$} \markbox{4762}{be} \markbox{4763}{a} \markbox{4764}{map} \markbox{4765}{induced} \markbox{4766}{by} \markbox{4767}{an} \markbox{m4768}{$\alpha \times \sigma$}-equivariant \markbox{4769}{map} \markbox{m4770}{$\tilde{g} : S \times X \to S \times X$}. 
		\markbox{4771}{Suppose} \markbox{4772}{there} \markbox{4773}{exists} \markbox{4774}{a} \markbox{m4775}{$\sigma$}-equivariant \markbox{4776}{map} \markbox{m4777}{$f : X \to X$} \markbox{4778}{such} \markbox{4779}{that} \markbox{4780}{both} \markbox{4781}{the} \markbox{4782}{pairs} \markbox{m4783}{$id_S\times f, \tilde g$} \markbox{4784}{and} \markbox{m4785}{$id_S\times f,\alpha\times\sigma\circ \tilde g$} \markbox{4786}{dont} \markbox{4787}{have} \markbox{4788}{any} \markbox{4789}{point} \markbox{4790}{of} coincidence.
		\markbox{4791}{Then} \markbox{4792}{the} \markbox{4793}{space} \markbox{m4794}{$P(S,X)$} \markbox{4795}{does} \markbox{4796}{not} \markbox{4797}{have} \markbox{4798}{the} \markbox{m4799}{$g$}-coincidence property.
	\end{proposition}
	\begin{proof}
		\markbox{4800}{Define} \markbox{m4801}{$\phi : P(S,X) \to P(S,X)$} \markbox{4802}{by} \markbox{m4803}{$\phi([s,x]) = [s, f(x)]$}. 
		\markbox{4804}{This} \markbox{4805}{map} \markbox{4806}{is} \markbox{4807}{well} \markbox{4808}{defined} because
		\markbox{m4809}{$\phi([\alpha(s), \sigma(x)]) = [\alpha(s), f(\sigma(x))] = [\alpha(s), \sigma(f(x))] = [s, f(x)]$}, \markbox{4810}{using} \markbox{4811}{the} \markbox{4812}{fact} \markbox{4813}{that} \markbox{m4814}{$f\circ \sigma=\sigma\circ f$}.
		
		\markbox{4815}{Similarly,} \markbox{4816}{define} \markbox{m4817}{$\psi : P(S,X) \to P(S,X)$} \markbox{4818}{by} \markbox{m4819}{$\psi([s,x]) = [g_1(s), g_2(x)]$}, 
		\markbox{4820}{where} \markbox{m4821}{$g_j = p_j \circ \tilde{g} \circ i_j$}, \markbox{4822}{and} \markbox{m4823}{$p_j$} \markbox{4824}{and} \markbox{m4825}{$i_j$} \markbox{4826}{denote} \markbox{4827}{the} \markbox{4828}{projection} \markbox{4829}{and} \markbox{4830}{inclusion} \markbox{4831}{maps} \markbox{4832}{on} \markbox{4833}{the} \markbox{m4834}{$j$}-th \markbox{4835}{factor} (\markbox{m4836}{$j=1,2$}). 
		\markbox{4837}{The} \markbox{4838}{map} \markbox{m4839}{$\psi$} \markbox{4840}{is} \markbox{4841}{well} \markbox{4842}{defined} \markbox{4843}{since} \markbox{m4844}{$\tilde{g}$} \markbox{4845}{is} \markbox{m4846}{$\alpha \times \sigma$}-equivariant.
		
		\markbox{4847}{Since,} \markbox{4848}{the} \markbox{4849}{maps} \markbox{m4850}{$f$} \markbox{4851}{and} \markbox{m4852}{$p_2 \circ \tilde{g} \circ i_2 = g_2$} \markbox{4853}{have} \markbox{4854}{no} \markbox{4855}{coincidence} \markbox{4856}{points.} 
		\markbox{4857}{Hence,} \markbox{4858}{for} \markbox{4859}{any} \markbox{m4860}{$[s,x] \in P(S,X)$}, \markbox{4861}{the} \markbox{4862}{second} \markbox{4863}{coordinates} \markbox{4864}{in} \markbox{m4865}{$\phi([s,x])$} \markbox{4866}{and} \markbox{m4867}{$\psi([s,x])$} \markbox{4868}{are} \markbox{4869}{different.} 
		\markbox{4870}{Therefore,} \markbox{m4871}{$\phi$} \markbox{4872}{and} \markbox{m4873}{$\psi$} \markbox{4874}{have} \markbox{4875}{no} \markbox{4876}{points} \markbox{4877}{of} \markbox{4878}{coincidence,} \markbox{4879}{and} \markbox{m4880}{$P(S,X)$} \markbox{4881}{does} \markbox{4882}{not} \markbox{4883}{possess} \markbox{4884}{the} \markbox{m4885}{$g$}-CP.
	\end{proof}
	\fi
	
		In \markbox{4886}{particular} \markbox{4887}{if} \markbox{4888}{we} \markbox{4889}{take} \markbox{m4890}{$g$} \markbox{4891}{to} \markbox{4892}{be} \markbox{4893}{the} \markbox{4894}{identity} \markbox{4895}{map} \markbox{4896}{in} \propref{necessary condition}, \markbox{4897}{we} \markbox{4898}{recover} Proposition~7.2.1 \markbox{4899}{of} \cite{mandal}, \markbox{4900}{which} \markbox{4901}{proves} \markbox{4902}{that} \markbox{4903}{if} \markbox{4904}{the} \markbox{4905}{base} \markbox{m4906}{$Y$} \markbox{4907}{does} \markbox{4908}{not} \markbox{4909}{have} \markbox{4910}{the} \markbox{4911}{FPP,} \markbox{4912}{or} \markbox{4913}{there} \markbox{4914}{exist} \markbox{4915}{a} \markbox{m4916}{$\sigma$}-equivarinat \markbox{4917}{map} \markbox{4918}{on} \markbox{4919}{the} \markbox{4920}{fibre} \markbox{m4921}{$X$} \markbox{4922}{with} \markbox{4923}{no} \markbox{4924}{fixed} \markbox{4925}{point} \markbox{4926}{then} \markbox{m4927}{$P(S,X)$} \markbox{4928}{does} \markbox{4929}{not} \markbox{4930}{have} \markbox{4931}{the} \markbox{4932}{FPP.} \markbox{4933}{As} \markbox{4934}{a} \markbox{4935}{consequence,} \markbox{m4936}{$P(m,n)$} \markbox{4937}{does} \markbox{4938}{not} \markbox{4939}{have} \markbox{4940}{the} \markbox{4941}{FPP} \markbox{4942}{if} \markbox{4943}{either} \markbox{m4944}{$m$} \markbox{4945}{or} \markbox{m4946}{$n$} \markbox{4947}{is} odd.
	\iffalse
	\begin{remark}\label{necessary criterion for FFP}
		\markbox{4948}{A} \markbox{4949}{generalized} \markbox{4950}{Dold} \markbox{4951}{space} \markbox{m4952}{$P(S,X)$} \markbox{4953}{does} \markbox{4954}{not} \markbox{4955}{have} \markbox{4956}{the} \markbox{4957}{FPP} \markbox{4958}{if} \markbox{4959}{any} \markbox{4960}{of} \markbox{4961}{the} \markbox{4962}{following} holds:
		
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item {} \markbox{m4963}{$Y=S/\!\!\sim _{\alpha}$} \markbox{4964}{does} \markbox{4965}{not} \markbox{4966}{have} \markbox{4967}{the} FPP.
			\item {} There \markbox{4968}{exists} \markbox{4969}{a} \markbox{m4970}{$\sigma$}-equivariant \markbox{4971}{map} \markbox{m4972}{$f$} \markbox{4973}{on} \markbox{m4974}{$X$} \markbox{4975}{that} \markbox{4976}{has} \markbox{4977}{no} \markbox{4978}{fixed} point.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{remark}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\markbox{4979}{We} \markbox{4980}{have} \markbox{4981}{the} \markbox{4982}{following} \markbox{4983}{observation} \markbox{4984}{as} \markbox{4985}{an} \markbox{4986}{immediate} \markbox{4987}{consequence} \markbox{4988}{of} \markbox{4989}{Remark} \ref{necessary criterion for FFP}.
	
	\begin{remark}
		\markbox{4990}{Let} \markbox{m4991}{$P(m,n)$} \markbox{4992}{be} \markbox{4993}{a} \markbox{4994}{classical} \markbox{4995}{Dold} \markbox{4996}{manifold} \markbox{4997}{such} \markbox{4998}{that} \markbox{4999}{either} \markbox{m5000}{$m$} \markbox{5001}{or} \markbox{m5002}{$n$} \markbox{5003}{is} \markbox{5004}{odd.} \markbox{5005}{Then}  
		%and the existence of a fixed point free map on $\mathbb CP^n$ which commutes with the conjugation, 
		\markbox{m5006}{$P(m,n)$} \markbox{5007}{does} \markbox{5008}{not} \markbox{5009}{have} \markbox{5010}{the} FPP.
	\end{remark}
	\begin{proof}
		\markbox{5011}{When} \markbox{m5012}{$m$} \markbox{5013}{is} \markbox{5014}{odd,} \markbox{5015}{the} \markbox{5016}{proof} \markbox{5017}{follows} \markbox{5018}{from} \markbox{5019}{part} \markbox{5020}{\textit{(1)}} \markbox{5021}{of} \remref{necessary criterion for FFP}. \\ \markbox{5022}{When} \markbox{m5023}{$n$} \markbox{5024}{is} \markbox{5025}{odd,} \markbox{5026}{we} \markbox{5027}{have} \markbox{5028}{a} \markbox{5029}{continuous} \markbox{m5030}{$\sigma$}-equivariant \markbox{5031}{map}  \markbox{m5032}{$f:\mathbb CP^n\to \mathbb CP^n$} \markbox{5033}{defined} \markbox{5034}{by} 
		\[
		[x_1:x_2:\cdots:x_n:x_{n+1}]\mapsto [ x_2:- x_1:\cdots: x_{n+1}:- x_{n}]
		\] \markbox{5035}{which} \markbox{5036}{does} \markbox{5037}{not} \markbox{5038}{have} \markbox{5039}{any} \markbox{5040}{fixed} point.
		%Clearly, $f\circ \sigma=\sigma\circ f$, where  
		Thus, \markbox{5041}{using} \markbox{5042}{part} \markbox{5043}{\textit{(2)}} \markbox{5044}{of} \remref{necessary criterion for FFP}, \markbox{m5045}{$P(m,n)$} \markbox{5046}{does} \markbox{5047}{not} \markbox{5048}{have} \markbox{5049}{fixed-point} property.
	\end{proof}
	%\textcolor{red}{Converse of the above remark seems to be true.}
	\fi
	
	
	\iffalse
	We \markbox{5050}{need} \markbox{5051}{the} \markbox{5052}{following} \markbox{5053}{theorems} \markbox{5054}{in} \markbox{5055}{the} sequal.
	\begin{theorem}[Lefschetz \markbox{5056}{Fixed-Point} Theorem]\label{Lefschetz theorem}
		\markbox{5057}{Let} \markbox{m5058}{$X$} \markbox{5059}{be} \markbox{5060}{a} \markbox{5061}{finite} \markbox{5062}{simplicial} \markbox{5063}{complex,} \markbox{5064}{and} \markbox{5065}{let} \markbox{m5066}{$f : X \to X$} \markbox{5067}{be} \markbox{5068}{a} \markbox{5069}{continuous} \markbox{5070}{map.}  
		\markbox{5071}{Define} \markbox{5072}{the} number
		\[
		\tau(f) = \sum_{n} (-1)^n \operatorname{tr}\!\big(f_* : H_n(X) \to H_n(X)\big),
		\]
		\markbox{5073}{called} \markbox{5074}{the} \markbox{5075}{\emph{Lefschetz number}} \markbox{5076}{of} \markbox{m5077}{$f$}.  
		\markbox{5078}{If} \markbox{m5079}{$\tau(f) \ne 0$}, \markbox{5080}{then} \markbox{m5081}{$f$} \markbox{5082}{has} \markbox{5083}{at} \markbox{5084}{least} \markbox{5085}{one} \markbox{5086}{fixed} point.
	\end{theorem}
	\fi
	
	
	%\begin{theorem}[\cite{glover-homer}, Theorem 2]\label{GH2} For $k,n$ as in Theorem \ref{GH1}, the complex Grassmannian $\mathbb CG_{n,k}$ has the fixed-point property if and only if $k(n-k)$ is even. \end{theorem}
	
	
	\iffalse
	In \markbox{5087}{(Theorem} \markbox{5088}{2,} \cite{glover-homer}), \markbox{5089}{it} \markbox{5090}{is} \markbox{5091}{proved} \markbox{5092}{that} \markbox{m5093}{$\mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{5094}{has} \markbox{5095}{fixed-point} \markbox{5096}{property} \markbox{5097}{if} \markbox{5098}{and} \markbox{5099}{only} \markbox{5100}{if} \markbox{m5101}{$k(n-k)$} \markbox{5102}{is} \markbox{5103}{even,} \markbox{5104}{provided} \markbox{5105}{either} \markbox{5106}{(i)} \markbox{m5107}{$k\leq 3$} \markbox{5108}{and} \markbox{m5109}{$n>2k$} \markbox{5110}{or} \markbox{5111}{(ii)} \markbox{m5112}{$k>3$} \markbox{5113}{and} \markbox{m5114}{$n> 2k^2-1$}.
	\markbox{5115}{It} \markbox{5116}{is} \markbox{5117}{well} \markbox{5118}{known} \markbox{5119}{that} \markbox{5120}{there} \markbox{5121}{exists} \markbox{5122}{a} \markbox{5123}{fixed-point} \markbox{5124}{free} \markbox{5125}{map}   \markbox{m5126}{$ L \mapsto L^\perp   $} \markbox{5127}{on}   \markbox{m5128}{$ \mathbb{C}G_{n,k}   $} \markbox{5129}{when}   \markbox{m5130}{$ k = n - k   $}.
	
	\markbox{5131}{The} \markbox{5132}{following} \markbox{5133}{remark} \markbox{5134}{follows} \markbox{5135}{easily} \markbox{5136}{from} \markbox{5137}{Theorem} \ref{hoffman} \cite{hoffman} \markbox{5138}{and} \markbox{5139}{Theorem} \ref{GH2} \cite{glover-homer}.
	\begin{remark}Let \markbox{m5140}{$f$} \markbox{5141}{be} \markbox{5142}{continuous} \markbox{5143}{self-map} \markbox{5144}{on} \markbox{m5145}{$\mathbb CG_{n,k}$} \markbox{5146}{such} that
		\markbox{m5147}{$ f^*(c_1) = \lambda c_1 $}, \markbox{m5148}{$ \lambda\neq 0 $}. \markbox{5149}{Assume} \markbox{5150}{that} \markbox{m5151}{$k(n-k)$} \markbox{5152}{is} \markbox{5153}{even} \markbox{5154}{and} \markbox{m5155}{$k\neq n-k$}. \markbox{5156}{Then} \markbox{m5157}{$f$} \markbox{5158}{has} \markbox{5159}{a} \markbox{5160}{fixed} \markbox{5161}{point.} 
	\end{remark}
	\begin{proof}
		\markbox{5162}{By} Theorem~\ref{hoffman} \cite{hoffman}, \markbox{5163}{the} \markbox{5164}{map} \markbox{m5165}{$f^*$} \markbox{5166}{is} \markbox{5167}{an} \markbox{5168}{Adams} \markbox{5169}{map.} \markbox{5170}{Using} \markbox{5171}{the} \markbox{5172}{computation} \markbox{5173}{of} \markbox{5174}{the} \markbox{5175}{Lefschetz} \markbox{5176}{number} \markbox{m5177}{$L(f)$} \markbox{5178}{from} \markbox{5179}{the} \markbox{5180}{proof} \markbox{5181}{of} Theorem~\ref{GH1}, \markbox{5182}{we} \markbox{5183}{observe} \markbox{5184}{that} \markbox{m5185}{$L(f) \ne 0$} \markbox{5186}{because} \markbox{m5187}{$k(n-k)$} \markbox{5188}{is} \markbox{5189}{even.} \markbox{5190}{Thus,} \markbox{m5191}{$f$} \markbox{5192}{must} \markbox{5193}{have} \markbox{5194}{a} \markbox{5195}{fixed} \markbox{5196}{point.} \markbox{5197}{This} \markbox{5198}{completes} \markbox{5199}{the} proof.
	\end{proof}
	\fi
	
	\subsection{} \markbox{5200}{Let} \markbox{5201}{us} \markbox{5202}{recall} \markbox{5203}{a} \markbox{5204}{well} \markbox{5205}{known} \markbox{5206}{result} \markbox{5207}{in} \markbox{5208}{coincidence} \markbox{5209}{theory,} \markbox{5210}{the} \markbox{5211}{Lefschetz} \markbox{5212}{Coincidence} \markbox{5213}{Theorem,} \markbox{5214}{which} \markbox{5215}{will} \markbox{5216}{be} \markbox{5217}{used} \markbox{5218}{to} \markbox{5219}{prove} \markbox{5220}{results} \markbox{5221}{in} \markbox{5222}{the} \markbox{5223}{rest} \markbox{5224}{of} \markbox{5225}{this} paper.\\
	
	\markbox{5226}{For} \markbox{5227}{a} \markbox{5228}{closed} \markbox{5229}{oriented} \markbox{5230}{manifold} \markbox{m5231}{$M$} \markbox{5232}{of} \markbox{5233}{dimension} \markbox{m5234}{$n$}, \markbox{5235}{let} \markbox{m5236}{$[M]\in H^n(M;\mathbb Q)$} \markbox{5237}{denote} \markbox{5238}{a} \markbox{5239}{chosen} \markbox{5240}{fundamental} \markbox{5241}{class.} \markbox{5242}{Then} \markbox{5243}{we} \markbox{5244}{have} \markbox{5245}{the} Poincar\'e  \markbox{5246}{duality} \markbox{5247}{isomorphism} \markbox{m5248}{$D_M:H^k(M;\mathbb Q)\to H_{n-k}(M;\mathbb Q)$}, \markbox{5249}{defined} \markbox{5250}{by} 
	\begin{equation}\label{poinc dua}
		D_M(\alpha)=[M]\frown \alpha, \, \forall \alpha\in H^k(M;\mathbb Z).
	\end{equation}

	
	\begin{theorem}[Lefschetz \markbox{5251}{Coincidence} Theorem]\label{LCT}
		\markbox{5252}{Let} \markbox{m5253}{$f,g$} \markbox{5254}{be} \markbox{5255}{two} \markbox{5256}{continuous} \markbox{5257}{maps} \markbox{5258}{on} \markbox{5259}{a} \markbox{5260}{compact,} \markbox{5261}{connected,} \markbox{5262}{oriented} \markbox{5263}{manifold} \markbox{m5264}{$M$} \markbox{5265}{of}  \markbox{5266}{dimension} \markbox{m5267}{$n$}. \markbox{5268}{The} \markbox{5269}{Lefschetz} \markbox{5270}{coincidence} \markbox{5271}{number} \markbox{5272}{is} \markbox{5273}{defined} \markbox{5274}{as} 
		$$L(f,g):= \sum_{i=0}^{n} (-1)^i \mathrm{tr}\big(D_M \circ g^* \circ D_M^{-1} \circ f_* \; : \; H_i(M;\mathbb{Q}) \longrightarrow H_i(M;\mathbb{Q})\big).
		$$ \markbox{5275}{If} \markbox{m5276}{$L(f,g) \neq 0$}, \markbox{5277}{then} \markbox{5278}{there} \markbox{5279}{exists} \markbox{m5280}{$x \in M$} \markbox{5281}{such} \markbox{5282}{that} \markbox{m5283}{$f(x) = g(x)$}.
	\end{theorem}
	\markbox{5284}{When}  \markbox{m5285}{$g=\operatorname{id}_M$}, \markbox{5286}{the} \markbox{5287}{theorem} \markbox{5288}{reduces} \markbox{5289}{to} \markbox{5290}{the} \markbox{5291}{Lefschetz} \markbox{5292}{Fixed-Point} \markbox{5293}{Theorem} \markbox{5294}{for} \markbox{m5295}{$M$}.\\
	
	\markbox{5296}{To} \markbox{5297}{study} \markbox{5298}{the} \markbox{5299}{coincidence} \markbox{5300}{theory} \markbox{5301}{of} \markbox{5302}{generalized} \markbox{5303}{Dold} \markbox{5304}{spaces} \markbox{5305}{fibred} \markbox{5306}{by} \markbox{5307}{complex} \markbox{5308}{Grassmannians} \markbox{5309}{over} \markbox{5310}{real} \markbox{5311}{projective} \markbox{5312}{spaces,} \markbox{5313}{it} \markbox{5314}{is} \markbox{5315}{helpful} \markbox{5316}{to} \markbox{5317}{first} \markbox{5318}{understand} \markbox{5319}{the} \markbox{5320}{coincidence} \markbox{5321}{theory} \markbox{5322}{of} \markbox{5323}{complex} \markbox{5324}{Grassmannians,} \markbox{5325}{a} \markbox{5326}{topic} \markbox{5327}{of} \markbox{5328}{independent} \markbox{5329}{interest.} \markbox{5330}{We} \markbox{5331}{now} \markbox{5332}{prove} \markbox{5333}{the} \markbox{5334}{following} \markbox{5335}{lemma} \markbox{5336}{(cf.} \markbox{5337}{Theorem} \markbox{5338}{2,} \cite{glover-homer}) \markbox{5339}{to} \markbox{5340}{prove} \propref{CP of CGnk}.
	\begin{lemma}\label{sum neq 0}
